### Post by IYY on 2007-03-11
Here are the rules:

[LIST=1]
[*]No commonly used applications: This means, no Firefox, Gimp, Inkscape, Open Office, Beryl etc.
[*]Application must be in the repositories (Kubuntu, Xubuntu, Feisty repos are all fine).
[*]Application must be fairly easy to use, so that its usefulness can be quickly apparent.
[/LIST]

Ok, so here are a couple of applications I've recently discovered that are truly amazing:

**Qalculate!**

This is without doubt the most powerful calculator I've ever used. And not only is it powerful, but it's also incredibly easy to use. It can not only be used for simple calculations, but also to factor, simplify, integrate, differentiate, sum, take means, calculate areas, do unit conversions, matrix multiplication... anything you can think of in the realm of math, science, engineering or finance. It even has a periodic table built in!

One thing I can tell you for certain: if I had this nifty little tool during my highschool education, I would not have learned anything, because it can do everything for me!

Even for simple calculations this tool is better than a regular calculator due to its intuitive interface that helps eliminate errors. For example, suppose I type in a slightly ambiguous expression like

12+5^2

as I type, text will appear underneath the input box telling me that the calculator understands the expression as 
 
12+(5^2)

Makes you far more confident, and less error prone.

The program is available in both QT and GTK.

**Agave**

A far less ambitious program than Qalculate, but useful nonetheless. Agave is a colour scheme designer. You can pick a colour, and the program will show you its complement, split complement (a 3 colour scheme), triads, tetrads, an analogous scheme, or a monochromatic scheme. 

So, if you are designing a webpage or a pamphlet, or even doing some digital painting, this program will tell you which colours go well together. 

A tip: some people don't know that in GTK, you can drag and drop almost anything. So, you can grab a colour from The Gimp, drag it into Agave, and then drag and drop the complement of that colour back into The Gimp. Very useful.

**Hydrogen**

I am an amateur musician, but when it comes to electronic music I am twice as uneducated. Anyway, Hydrogen still managed to impress me. This application can be used to create drum and other percussion patterns. It's very easy to use (I figured it out instantly, with 0 experience in the field), and can be fun for those who have never played an instrument or done any work with sound. 

It's a QT app, but looks equally good in both Gnome and KDE since it has its own theme anyway.

**Zim**

Zim is a desktop wiki. I guess it's very similar to Tomboy notes which you may be familiar with, but is designed for a more general purpose. You can create your own wikis (like Wikipedia) on your own computer, without using a browser, and with a very simple WYSIWYG interface. Can be handy to stay organized.

A GTK app.

**Beneath a Steel Sky**

This is an old cyberpunk point-and-click adventure game that has been ported (with ScummVM) to Linux. It's completely free, can be downloaded from the repositories, and even comes with speech (that is, every line of dialog in the game is spoken). The graphics are a bit dated, but the storyline is excellent. If you enjoyed games like Monkey Island, King Quest and Quest for Glory, you will love this one.

Ok... I'm done. Your turn!

### Post by Henry Rayker on 2007-03-11
I second **filelight**.

It makes a multilayered pi chart of your harddrive usage. (So you get a graphical feel for not only which directories are taking up the most space, but also what subdirectories inside of that and so on.) This is the best program I have ever used to look at disk usage.

Another that I really like is **rtorrent**.

Basically, it's an ncurses based command line torrent manager...it feels as if my downloads are quicker, and I know it uses a lot less of my system resources than anything else I tried.

### Post by Mateo on 2007-03-11
good thread, i'm definitely giving some of these applications a shot.

There are two scripts in my signature that I know no one uses but me.  Included in these scripts is:

**theyoke**: a very simple CLI rss aggregator.  it's good to use in conjunction with wget or some other application for grabbing files or posts.

**youtube-dl**: command line program for downloading youtube videos.

----------------

some others I use that aren't super popular:

**Stellarium**:  In my mind, the best astronomy program. I like it much better than celestia because it's like looking at the night's sky from your house.

**hellanzb**: I don't know why it's not more popular.  I guess because torrents are more popular than usenet.  but for grabbing binary files, it's definitely the best program that exists.

**gcolor2**: a very nice program for web development. it will tell you the color of anything on your computer.

### Post by Spr0k3t on 2007-03-12
I'm going to add a throw for **Ex Falso**.  This is an ID3 tag editor that let's you generator the tags on the fly.  Do clusters, directories, albums, by filename, etc.  It also allows you to set your preferred tagging method and file renaming.  So if you get a bunch of new music off of a CD you just put on your drive, and want to tag and move them easily, Ex Falso will move and rename the files tagging them for you.  It takes a bit to really see the power the application has... but it's well worth the curve if you have a decent size music directory.

---

### Post by Bakerconspiracy on 2007-03-12
I too found **filelight** very useful. Well disigned little program.

I have come to offer **streamtuner** coupled with **streamripper**. Streamripper takes all the online radio stations from shoutcast and many other online radio station hosts, and creates an easy to use browser for radio stations based on genre. With streamripper you can easily rip the music that is being streamed to your computer (a very easy way to accumulate a nice music library), but very illegal. Just set streamripper to not reconnect when you have been kicked from a server and no one will ever find out :)

### Post by userundefine on 2007-03-12
Great idea for a thread.  I'm already finding cool things.

**yakuake**.  KDE app.  This is a godsend for people who like the terminal to always be accessible.  You can assign a keyboard shortcut, and when you hit it **yakuake** flies out and gives you a terminal immediately.  My shortcut is Ctrl + Spacebar.  You can control the speed of the animation too if you want it to happen faster.  It sits in memory so is always ready.  Keeps my hand off the mouse reaching down to my toolbar to execute, and frees up that screen real estate since I no longer have a need for a shortcut to Konsole.  You can also have tabbed terminals within **yakuake**, and matched with GNU screen you never will need another terminal program.

---

### Post by K.Mandla on 2007-03-12
[Mirage]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/x11/mirage"), which is a very straightforward GTK image viewer. Does resizing, conversion and some other things. I use it on old machines that would suffer under the Gimp.

[ePDFView]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/text/epdfview"), which is similar in that it's a simple, lightweight PDF viewer (as you might have imagined) built on GTK. No Gnome deps.

[Leafpad]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/editors/leafpad"), GTK notepad-like editor. Does it exactly that, and not a stitch more. But that's what I like about it.

[Qingy]("http://qingy.sourceforge.net/"), a framebuffer substitute for getty (think: login manager) that is much, much lighter than KDM/GDM and looks better than XDM/WDM. 

[Kazehakase]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/web/kazehakase"), which is a Gecko-based browser that will run circles around Firefox, especially on older machines.

[lxpanel]("http://sourceforge.net/projects/lxpanel"), because Openbox users need to dump PyPanel.

[xcompmgr]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/x11/xcompmgr"), because Openbox users can do transparency too.

[Xfe]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/x11/xfe") or [PCManFM]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/utils/pcmanfm"), if you can be bothered to choose. PCManFM has more features and looks better, but Xfe is about the fastest graphical file manager I can find, and the 0.98 version actually looks good for a change.

[rxvt-unicode]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/x11/rxvt-unicode"), by far the best-looking terminal emulator, for my money.

+1 for Deluge, HTop, gColor2, Audacious and rtorrent. Special runner-up prize to Midnight Commander. ;)

---

### Post by cstudent on 2007-03-12
nautilus-open-terminal

Adds a right click menu option to open the terminal, either from the desktop or in a nautilus directory. If you use it in a nautilus directory, it will open terminal in that directory. I always have to log out and back in when I first install it to see it.

### Post by Rui Pais on 2007-03-12
> **Mateo said:**
> what is diff?

a nightmare :p 

A terminal app that outputs the differences between 2 files. 
I think it's the only thing on terminal that i couldn't get used... 
 
it' s very usefull for kernel configs, several versions of config files, merging or compare code, text, lists, etc.

Some distros, like Gentoo, use it as a basic tool. When the user are updating a file that have config files that don't match the one present on user installation...


edit:
another good use for meld, it's for merging entrys of menu.lst when one had several Linuxs and one separeted boot partition with a grub menu to manage all those OSs. A simple click to add or remove entrys avoid a lot of errors :)

### Post by Onyros on 2007-03-13
I think I must add a disclaimer to my PCManFM recommendations: even though it is a great app, it's still somewhat buggy. The main existing bug is the fact that it doesn't grey out deletion whenever a file's not selected; and when you do proceed with deletion, it deletes the entire folder you're currently browsing... meaning: if you're browsing the desktop and you accidentally delete with no file selected... your entire Desktop will be "rm'ed" (not only its contents, the folder itself).

So, as cool as it is... it's better to delete through the terminal, at least until PCMan corrects that "little" bug.

(and yeah, I've lost my share of important files because of PCManFM, but I still use and recommend it)

---

### Post by Onyros on 2007-03-14
> **Mateo said:**
> thanks, but do you know if it runs well on low-end systems (systems that run fluxbox or something like that).Yep, I use PCManFM on a wide spectrum of machines, for example a Pentium III 733MHz with 384MB RAM or an IBM Thinkpad T23 (Pentium III-M 1GHz + 512MB RAM), with Fluxbox & E17, and it runs perfectly, faster than any other GUI file manager other than XFE.

It takes less than 10MB of RAM, even if you open multiple instances of the program (which you won't, because it has native tab support enabled), so it's perfect in terms of RAM usage.

### Post by Oki on 2007-03-15
If you download a CHM file(= Microsoft Compressed HTML Help", witch is a proprietary format), there is a lot of viewers for Linux(as xCHM, gnochm, kchmviewer, kchm), but I dont like how it works(so used to PDF). 

The command based program **CHMLIB** can extract it for you, and very fast. 

The program **HTMLDOC** can convert the extracted files to a PDF for you. HTMLDOC can also download urls as HTML, PS, PDF or Seperated HTML. Is great when you find a guide on the nett that you want to save.

---

### Post by jenhsun on 2007-03-16
Synergy: Multi-Moniter and PC solution.
I have 4 pc and 4 LCD running my daily tasks. I have XP, windows server, ubuntu dekstop...all different platform. I don't want to use switch to switch to and from my LCD. This is a cool utility for you, even you can copy the texts from Linux to and from Windows.

Start-Up Manager: Change Boot Loading screen.
GUI based to change loading screen. So your startup will be very different.

gcursor: change X11 mouse theme.
GUI based too, change mouse theme.

This python script picks up a pdf file, and it makes a presentation with it. Give a go, it doesn't even has to be installed on a Linux machine (ah... the wonder of python :D))

[Emesene](http://emesene-msn.blogspot.com/) (A msn meesenger written in Python (Use the deb package on the attachment, because the ones on the main website sometimes don't work)

[Frets on Fire](http://louhi.kempele.fi/~skyostil/uv/fretsonfire/) (A Guittar-Hero like game that run on Linux)

PyDance (A Dance Dance Revolution type of game written in Python (it's in the repositories))

[DoomRL](http://doom.chaosforge.org/) (A five minutes rougelike game, based on Doom. A nice change for when you just lost your 9 level Wizard with a pet Dragon on Nethack :D)

[Berserk!]("http://berserk.chaosforge.org/") (Another game from the same author of DoomRL, but this one is even shorter :D Just survive for the longest time possible)

And I think that's all :D

---

### Post by IYY on 2007-03-17

Its in the repos.

Its a windows-matching utility for gnome, some excellent functionality available from this. some examples:

[LIST]
[*]Place a transparent terminal as your background
[*]Dock your gaim contacts list to the side of the desktop
[*]BEST USE EVER: pin the gimp toolbar/layers windows to ALL workspaces allowing you to manipulate images full screen over multiple desktops without having to go looking for the damn panels!
[/LIST]

I installed this app and figured out how to use it, but I can't come up with a script for this third idea (Gimp). Could you please post your .ds file for it?

### Post by deadlydeathcone on 2007-03-18
> **AndyCooll said:**
> I've just had a look at this. It's ok, however currently it doesn't hold a candle to Easytag. For instance pattens for renaming files are somewhat limited, as is the adding of album covers etc, as is the creation of playlists, I could go on ... :cool:

Ex Falso is my favorite as Cowbell seems to screw up custom tags, and although Easytag is cool it has an incredibly weird ui. [Picard]("http://musicbrainz.org/doc/PicardQt") (the official client of Musicbrainz), though, is the best by far for tagging entire albums, and the [version for Feisty]("http://users.musicbrainz.org/~luks/picard-qt/picardqt.png") is nearly automated.

Other than that Agave is a nice tool that generates color schemes, [Kompozer ]("http://www.getdeb.net/search.php?keywords=kompozer")is an improved nvu, and Gtkdebconf lists all of the configurable packages installed, which is handy. I also have to mention nicotine+, which is great for finding painfully obscure music. If anyone wants it I attached a Feisty deb for the newest version, as it isn't officially packaged yet.

### Post by NotPhil on 2007-03-19
> **IYY said:**
> 
[LIST=1]
[*]No commonly used applications: This means, no Firefox, Gimp, Inkscape, Open Office, Beryl etc.
[*]Application must be in the repositories (Kubuntu, Xubuntu, Feisty repos are all fine).
[*]Application must be fairly easy to use, so that its usefulness can be quickly apparent.
[/LIST]
How about some apps that aren't in the repositories?

[LIST]
[*][Gemstone]("http://www.ninthavenue.com.au/products/gemstone") lets you use OpenOffice Base for accounting.
[*][Grism]("http://www.grism.org/index.html") allows you to track stocks.
[*][Homebank]("http://homebank.free.fr/") is a pretty nice electronic checkbook.
[*][Inkblot]("http://www.mikegtn.net/1117") tells you how much ink your printer has left in it.
[*][PanelFM]("http://panelfm.sourceforge.net/") gives the GNOME Panel a quick, menu-based, file browser.
[*][PyChess]("http://pychess.googlepages.com/") is an attractive front-end for chess programs.
[*][Sirius]("http://sirius.bitvis.nu/") is a well-designed Reversi game.
[*][Warzone 2100]("http://wz2100.net/introduction.html") is a port of a 3D real-time strategy game.
[/LIST]

### Post by molgar on 2007-03-21
[Glipper]("http://glipper.sourceforge.net/") - a great clipboard manager, it's on the repos.

[GCStar]("http://www.gcstar.org/") - want to make a database of all your dvds, books...? This is the right app to do it with.

### Post by happy-and-lost on 2007-03-21
**Debian.exe** - Aside from having the best domain on the internet ([http://goodbye-microsoft.com/]("http://goodbye-microsoft.com/")), it's a fantastic tool which works seamlessly. Differs from Ubuntu's equivalent because it doesn't install Debian in the Windows partition, it's basically the netinstall CD without the need for a CD. Very, very useful for getting Debian on machines with no CD/USB/Floppy.

**viruskiller** - Game in the repos. Nuke little green viruses which come flooding into your folders from IE, MSN, Outlook and the Recycle Bin :) [http://www.parallelrealities.co.uk/virusKiller.php]("http://www.parallelrealities.co.uk/virusKiller.php")

### Post by ComplexNumber on 2007-03-22
the best dictionary that i've found is stardict. it allows ther user to add to the dictionaries (eg add computer dictionaries, geological dictionaries, etc).  it even pronounces words where the pronunciation is unclear. other applications that others probably haven't heard of that i use include:
-solfege - ear training application.
-mtpaint - a paint type program.
-desktop data manager - great for screenshots because it allows you to specifiy a screen area as an alternative to capturing the whole screen.
-meld - an application to find and highlight the differences between any 2 or 3 different files.
-regexxer - a search and replace text tool.
-fslint- an application that finds: duplicate files, installed packages, 
bad names, name clashes, temp files, bad symlinks, bad IDs, empty directories, non-stripped binaries, and redundant whitespaces.

### Post by ComplexNumber on 2007-03-22
> **urukrama said:**
> Stardict can pronounce words? Really? I've never come acros that feature.

But I second this. Stardict is a great app!
yes, but you have to install something called  WyabdcRealPeopleTTS.


> WyabdcRealPeopleTTS package make StarDict can pronounce those English words. It is just many .wav files.
In Linux, you can extract(tar -xjvf) the tarball at "/usr/share/". In Windows, you can use WinRAR to extract the tarball and install it at "C:\Program Files\" or "Program Files\StarDict\".you can find it [here]("http://stardict.sourceforge.net/") near the bottom of the page.

### Post by K.Mandla on 2007-03-22
Did anyone mention [Kazehakase]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/edgy/web/kazehakase")? It's a GTK/Gecko-based browser that makes Firefox (and even Iceweasel) look like a bloated old cow by comparison. It also has a lot of customizable points that make it very interesting to play with. 

I'm sure someone has mentioned it as a browser alternative, in which case I respectfully submit this as a sincere +1. :D

### Post by K.Mandla on 2007-03-22
> **jonty-comp said:**
> No, I mean like conky, but a fully-functioning terminal.  I've seen it on peoples' desktop shots before, and I know the name somewhere, I just can't find it in my vastly inferior brain. :(

EDIT: It might well be Tilda, but it seems I can't get rid of the annoying beryl shadow. :p
You can do that with rxvt-unicode or with xfce4-terminal (and maybe some others); both have the option to turn off the scrollbars, menu bar and window frames. Then set the pseudo-transparency to the lowest setting, and voila! A terminal directly on your desktop.

### Post by DX 00 on 2007-03-22
I'm surprised no one has said **gdesklets.** This is a very cool app that allows you to have all kinds of cool info on your desktop and they look almost as background pics. I currently have them monitoring my cpu/mem/hdd/network plus I have a really cool clock as well.

### Post by ComplexNumber on 2007-03-22
> **DX 00 said:**
> I'm surprised no one has said **gdesklets.** This is a very cool app that allows you to have all kinds of cool info on your desktop and they look almost as background pics. I currently have them monitoring my cpu/mem/hdd/network plus I have a really cool clock as well.
gdesklets is just starting a possible revival.....hopefully and possibly. it went through a patch of being unmaintained, so all the developers for the various gdesklet applications went elsewhere, i'm told. its nowhere near as involved as, say, superkaramba at this present time. many gdesklets just simply don't work properly or don't work at all with the latest gdesklets engine.

### Post by Rhubarb on 2007-03-26
ffmpeg2theora
This nifty command line app lets you easily convert any video that ffmpeg can read (which is a lot) into the lovely ogg theora video format.
It's in the repositories.

Sauerbraten
A 1st person OpenGL shoot'em up.
Cross platform, online multiplayer, easily configurable / tweakable, and is under constant development (expect a new version very soon).
It has a VERY powerful (& very easy to use) in-game map editor too, that supports online co-operative map making - once up and running, press "e" to enter edit mode, then scroll the mousewheel to see for yourself how easy it is.
It's not in the repositories.
[http://www.sauerbraten.org](http://www.sauerbraten.org)

Yukon
Allows you to capture anything you see that's rendered in OpenGL (for games etc)
It's not in the repositories.
[http://www.neopsis.com/projects/yukon/](http://www.neopsis.com/projects/yukon/)

mencoder
A very powerful application that allows you to transcode pretty much any video format into any other video format.
This is a huge program and has many many options.  Type in :man mencoder" and you'll see.
It's in the repositories.

stellarium
This has been mentioned before in this thead, so +1 to it.
It's a great OpenGL star gazing app - great if you want to know where (insert your favourite celestial object here) is at any given time.
It managed to beautifully display the lunar eclipse that happened recently (3rd March).
It's in the repositories.

---

### Post by Mateo on 2007-03-26
I have to shout out **elinks**, a terminal browser.  It's a lot of fun.  I use it sometimes just because the pages load faster, and I'm more likely to actually read stuff instead of mindless browsing.  I still can't figure out how to log onto ubuntuforums with it.  Also, if you use the real terminal instead of the terminal emulator, it uses nice color schemes for pages.  It's a lot easier on your eyes but still manages to look good.

---

### Post by SuSUntu on 2007-03-27
> **ice60 said:**
> i love proxo, i'm using grypen's filters with the ssl certificates and DLLs to filter ssl too :D from the addons here -
[http://www.proxomitron.info/files/index.html](http://www.proxomitron.info/files/index.html)

the certificate has run out, but there are new ones from grypen's site. some people don't like them though for some reason i can't remember why now.

I'm a Sidki config guy, myself. I've probably tried 'em all over the years (I've been using Proxo since 1998-99).

> **ice60 said:**
> 
Desktop Data Manager - a clipboard manager, screenshot app (with various nice settings) and download manager, although i use wget for that.
[http://data-manager.sourceforge.net/index.html](http://data-manager.sourceforge.net/index.html)
[http://data-manager.sourceforge.net/screenshots.html](http://data-manager.sourceforge.net/screenshots.html)
[http://data-manager.sourceforge.net/features.html](http://data-manager.sourceforge.net/features.html)


By the way, while I've got your attention, I wanted to comment on Desktop Data Manager which you recommended (along with a few other people in this thread). One of my  productivity complaints about Linux when I first started using it was its implementation of the clipboard. It just seemed very poor and ineffective, and there were no really powerful clipboard management tools. In Windows, I use [ClipMate]("http://www.thornsoft.com/"); ClipMate's been part of my utility arsenal for years, and it is one of maybe 5 utilities I have ever paid for; I'm big on freeware / open source in Windows as well, but the non-commercial clipboard utilities in Windows cannot approach the functionality of ClipMate (yet most have a lot more features than Glipper or DDM).

Anyway, I've grown to be basically satisfied with Glipper, but I'm always open for something better. So, in this thread, I saw DDM mentioned (multiple times), and I decided to give it a try. However it seems pretty buggy, so I'll ask if you are getting the same issues (the following comments are strictly related to the clipboard manager and not the DL manager or the screenshot utility):

- DDM occasionally becomes a runaway process and must be killed
- the keybindings do not work, default or otherwise
- the Detailed History feature does not appear to provide detail of anything at all (maybe this isn't a bug, but if not, it certainly isn't doing what I intuitively thought it should be doing)
- DDM will not show up in the notification area if launched automatically with Sessions (although it does appear in the list of processes when launched this way)
- launching DDM from a terminal to get debug info shows multiple critical failures / errors, though it will ultimately launch and reside in the notification area
- several other quirky things

I installed DDM using multiple methods, and all presented the same issues:

- installed via *.deb created using checkinstall
- installed via *.deb using the package creation script supplied with DDM source
- installed via the pre-built *.deb supplied by the author of DDM

I uninstalled DDM completely and went back to Glipper, but I figure I must be doing something wrong since you weren't the only one to recommend DDM. Plus, I've watched the screencast on the DDM site, and at least it seemed to have worked for the author. :)

I'm running Edgy 6.10, 32-bit.

---

### Post by Aliarse on 2007-03-27
> **Rhubarb said:**
> Sauerbraten

I downloaded this earlier on today (before i read your post), its not bad, very fast paced shooter, unlike for example, americas army.

What i dont like however, is the fact opposing teams spawn on the same spot, meaning as soon as the game starts, some punk shoots you, could also do with more weapons, i only counted about 5..

My addition to this thread (if someone hasnt already posted it..) would be :

[Tremulous.]("http://tremulous.net/")

> Tremulous is a free, open source game that blends a team based FPS with elements of an RTS. Players can choose from 2 unique races, aliens and humans. Players on both teams are able to build working structures in-game like an RTS. These structures provide many functions, the most important being spawning. The designated builders must ensure there are spawn structures or other players will not be able to rejoin the game after death. Other structures provide automated base defense (to some degree), healing functions and much more...

 Its in repository.

to tell the truth i haven't used DDM for a while, i have only recently reinstalled it on this new install and i'm using xfce atm (i'm using the xfce clipboard panel plugin)

however, i just complied it from source, all i can say is i will have read the install and README files and had a look at the outputs during the install to make sure i had all the dependences.

i haven't had those problems you described, although i use the mouse far too much and might not know about the keybindings problem if i had it. i had one problem once and that was one of the buffers wasn't working 100% of the time, but AFAIK it's working fine with this install.

the only thing i can say is you could try making a startup script and put that in the session startup in case it's being launched before the panel. -

```
#!/bin/bash

sleep 5 ; path/to/DDM
exit 0
```
save that somewhere, make it executable (chmod +x *script_name*), then put it in sessions. another thing is i can't get ubuntu installed on my hardware so i'm using suse.

OK, i just ran it and i do get the keybinding errors too :|

### Post by Onyros on 2007-03-30
> **Mateo said:**

lynx doesn't have tabbed browsing though, does it?That's the beauty of Fluxbox... any program can be tabbed ;) (you can also drag tabs around with the middle-click and group apps that way)

You just have to configure the programs which instances you want to open in a new tab instead of a window of its own.

I currently use tabbed xterms, tabbed leafpads, tabbed AbiWord, tabbed links2 (I must try elinks, too), you get the idea.

### Post by vnt87 on 2007-04-04
There is this editor that I really like: [Komodo Edit]("http://www.activestate.com/products/komodo_edit/")
It's free, but I'm not sure if it's opensource. It's a great code editor that features a very nice GUI that integrates perfectly into your WM, code highlighting and comparing for a variaty of languages, Firefox-style extensions etc. My only complain with it is its startup time, which is not that slow for an ordinary program but still quite slow for a text editor. 
I still miss Notepad++ on Windows though, wish somebody could port it to run natively on Linux.

### Post by kerry_s on 2007-04-04
gtklp <- for those dang applications that refuse to detect printers, this will make them use cups, just put gtklp for the printer.

gv <- alternative light weight pdf/ps viewer, ugly but gets the job done

scrot <- my favorite screen shot shooter

emelfm <- the lightest(557kb), fastest, most programmable file manager, not the prettiest, obsolete, is rock solid though. 

axle <- multi-thread down loader, combine it with firefox flash got extension and it's a winner

graveman <-burner, if you need 1 that doesn't depend on the DE this 1's a good burner, simple, takes getting use to the setup.

Dock apps i use in fluxbox:

wmdrawer <- if you just got to have icons, but don't want them on the desktop

Mixer.app <- simple volume control, controls master, cd, pcm

bbrun <- a very nice run program, i use bbrun -a

---

### Post by forrestcupp on 2007-04-05
dvdisaster.  It's in the repo's.  It will salvage all readable data off a scratched or corrupted dvd/cd and make an iso file so you can put the salvaged data on a good dvd.  Also if you use it on a dvd/cd that isn't scratched, it will make a small reference file for that dvd so that if it gets scratched in the future, it can read the readable material, and fix the rest with the reference.  Pretty handy.

---

### Post by finferflu on 2007-04-05
How about **checkgmail**? It's a gmail mail checker that sits in the system tray and pops up a little window (like Sonata, for instance), when you get a new message, saying:

> New mail from <sender>

And if you hover over it you can see a small preview of all the unread emails.

If you're not using Beryl, you can also archive or delete mails from the system tray, but with Beryl it doesn't work, however if you just click on it, it opens Gmail in your favourite browser ;)

---

### Post by SuSUntu on 2007-04-05
> **kerry_s said:**
> 
emelfm <- the lightest(557kb), fastest, most programmable file manager, not the prettiest, obsolete, is rock solid though. 


You seem to know your apps, so you must be aware of EmelFM2 and likely have perfectly legit reasons for sticking with EmelFM. It's a nice file manager.

However, for those that may not be aware, EmelFM2 is available. It's prettier (that's a relative assessment) and it's in active development. The latest version (0.3.3) was released 2007-03-20.

I've been using it for quite a while, and I currently have 0.3.2 installed with no issues on Edgy 6.10.

[http://emelfm2.net/emelFM2](http://emelfm2.net/emelFM2)

---

### Post by SuSUntu on 2007-04-05
> **forrestcupp said:**
> dvdisaster.  It's in the repo's.  It will salvage all readable data off a scratched or corrupted dvd/cd and make an iso file so you can put the salvaged data on a good dvd.  Also if you use it on a dvd/cd that isn't scratched, it will make a small reference file for that dvd so that if it gets scratched in the future, it can read the readable material, and fix the rest with the reference.  Pretty handy.

Here's a nice, semi-long discussion of DVDisaster vs. PAR over at the HydrogenAudio forum:

[http://www.hydrogenaudio.org/forums/index.php?showtopic=51536&st=0](http://www.hydrogenaudio.org/forums/index.php?showtopic=51536&st=0)

It's civil and has lots of direct and tangential info relative to data recovery methods. I've seen similar discussions before (probably at CDFreaks), but I remembered the HA thread specifically because it is fairly recent (Jan 07).

Anyway, thought potential users of DVDisaster might want some more info since the topic can be pretty technical.

---

### Post by SuSUntu on 2007-04-05
> **vnt87 said:**
> There is this editor that I really like: [Komodo Edit]("http://www.activestate.com/products/komodo_edit/")
It's free, but I'm not sure if it's opensource. It's a great code editor that features a very nice GUI that integrates perfectly into your WM, code highlighting and comparing for a variaty of languages, Firefox-style extensions etc. My only complain with it is its startup time, which is not that slow for an ordinary program but still quite slow for a text editor. 
I still miss Notepad++ on Windows though, wish somebody could port it to run natively on Linux.

Thanks very much for that link. I consider myself to be a rabid software enthusiast and try to seek out all the best for a given platform. I've pretty much worn out the nooks and crannies over the years with Windows, and I know most of the very best freeware text editors for that OS.

I mostly use ConTEXT, SciTE, and HTML-Kit on the Windows side, but I occasionally use MetaPad (notepad replacement), PSPad, and Crimson Editor.

On Linux, I have:

- Eclipse with PHP, PERL, JAVA and SubVersion support plugins - too cumbersome for smaller projects, and I generally have an aversion to (or bias against)  JAVA-based applications 

- SciTE - nice, powerful, simple and to the point, great for quick projects or as your main text / code file viewer

- Gedit - okay with various plug-ins installed (project, spellchecker, etc.) but like most Gnome apps, even with the plug-ins, its pretty stripped-down, feature-wise

- Scribes - for some people, it might be a Gnome replacement for SciTE, but it's not as customizable and doesn't have tabs (every file has to be opened in a separate window and that gets pretty messy). I can't use it.

I just downloaded and installed Komodo and it looks like a very close drop-in replacement for ConTEXT (if its really good enough, it might become a replacement for ConTEXT for my work in Windows). I do get your point about slight startup sluggishness, but I may be able to live with that if it proves itself in use. Gedit on the other hand can be kind of slow starting up with several plug-ins installed (relative to what one would expect from a simple text editor), yet I don't feel like its feature-set warrants the slowness. 

I'm surprised I've never seen or heard of Komodo, though its likely because of the closed-nature of the code and the licensing for the IDE version. That doesn't bother me, especially since I have tried the OSS alternatives, even the KDE stuff (more alternatives welcome), and so far I'm dissatisfied. Anyway, I've got a little project I'm working on now that had me searching for this very type of application again, so, thanks for pointing this one out. Hopefully it's stable in use. If it is, its a keeper.

---

I also don't like how emelfm2 does the settings, in emelfm it's dirt simple and i believe simple is better. :)  I know emelfm is getting on in it's years, but it still solid as a rock, i've even used it to rescue data from corrupted drives where other file managers would just choke up. So i figure as long as it still works i'll use it.

### Post by dannyboy79 on 2007-04-05
gxiso = gtk application used to extract XBOX iso files. also is suppose to be able to upload the extracted files right into your xbox but I haven't gotten that part to work. I have read that it may be do to avalaunch's ftp server since it really doesn't abide by the ftp standards and it has some kind of turbo thing enabled (yes I have tried disabling that avalaunch feature but to no avail). i just use it to extract the xbox iso to my hard drive, then simply ftp the contents using gftp or samba. great for backing up your own personal games and then restoring them to xbob hard drive.

### Post by Onyros on 2007-04-08
I've been meaning to write about Grip ever since I first replied to this thread, but somehow always forgot about it (that's what happens when you take something for granted).

In my good ol' Windows days, I used Exact Audio Copy; when messing around with Ubuntu, kept on using EAC (through WINE) and then, one glorious day found out about (a beautiful alliteration, makes me wanna sing and all)... **Grip** (e.g., + LAME, for mp3).

No need to use WINo apps with that, especially if one keeps one's CD's pretty much untouched after first ripping them to whatever you want to rip them to. Don't really know about EAC's superiority in terms of error/scratch correction, but I recommend **Grip** for the average user and for the audiophile alike. It's a pleasure to use, too. I find it better to use than CDex or EAC, for that matter.

Also, there have been people mentioning **Geany**, and I must give a +1 to that, as well.

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-04-10
I just came across [Incollector]("http://www.incollector.devnull.pl/"), an application to collect and organise various kinds of notes, quotes, serial numbers, urls, conversations, etc. You can tagg all your entries, which makes it easier to search for them, rate them, comment on your notes, 

I never got used to Tomboy's way of doing things, and find Incollector's approach much more pleasing and practical.

You can find a deb package for Dapper [here]("http://www.getdeb.net/download.php?release=79&fpos=0").

### Post by Henry Rayker on 2007-04-11
I don't remember if thunar as installed by the repos in Ubuntu has it (or if there is even an option), but yum in Fedora has a neat extension that allows you to rename media files (I've only worked with mp3 at the moment) using their ID3 tags. I'm fairly anal about these things, but tend to find that it is easier to rename a bunch of tags (especially with easytag or a similar tag editor) than to rename a bunch of files (even writing scripts sucks because, oftentimes, you have to still hand type the names)...This way, you type them once.

When you right click the file and select rename, a window pops up with some drop-down menus. The most relevant is the one that determines what information it uses. You have several format choices and can specify to use underscores instead of spaces or all lowercase or whatever.

---

### Post by richbarna on 2007-04-11
**AVI-OGM-INFO** *the same as Gspot in Windows*
> *Info :* A simple GUI/console program to get usefull information from Media files. 

*Supported formats are currently :* AVI (*.avi), Ogg Video and Audio (*.ogm, *.ogg), MPEG Audio (*.mp3, *.mpa, *.mp2) and MPEG Video (*.mpg, *.mpeg)
[B]And also WinFF video converter
[/B]It's got a gtk GUI for the initial video config then runs through xterm.

[http://biggmatt.com/programs/video-converter/winff---free-video-converter.html](http://biggmatt.com/programs/video-converter/winff---free-video-converter.html)

### Post by raul_ on 2007-04-24
centericq

It's a ncurses based multi-protocol IM (like gaim). It's a valid alternative for those with low RAM pc's :) and it's very functional.

NOTE: Don't be mad if you seem to send 20 messages and your contacts don't respond...sendind is CTRL+X and not ENTER

### Post by bwhite82 on 2007-04-27
Two tools that always get installed are:

**localepurge** - It automagically gets rid of unnecessary locale files on your computer each time you install a package. The first time you use it, it will easily remove 50-60mb+.
[B]
deborphan[/B] - CLI tool that locates oprhaned (read: unnecessary) packages on your computer.

Great thread, so far I've gleaned agave and learned howto embed a terminal into my desktop.

### Post by AmyRose on 2007-05-01
Ooh, I use Qalculate a lot. :) And I could not live without Audacious Media Player (in Feisty repos, but updated packages are available from [http://morgot.free.fr](http://morgot.free.fr) ) XMMS fans might like it. It's the only player that can play MIDI without too much trouble (if you have eawpats and the appropriate timidity.cfg for it) And it also handles a bunch of emulator music formats (like SPC, NSF, VGM, GYM, etc.) out of the box.

Audacious is a fork of Beep Media Player which is a fork of XMMS.

### Post by DJiNN on 2007-05-01
> **K.Mandla said:**
> [Mirage]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/x11/mirage"), which is a very straightforward GTK image viewer. Does resizing, conversion and some other things. I use it on old machines that would suffer under the Gimp.

[ePDFView]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/text/epdfview"), which is similar in that it's a simple, lightweight PDF viewer (as you might have imagined) built on GTK. No Gnome deps.

[Leafpad]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/editors/leafpad"), GTK notepad-like editor. Does it exactly that, and not a stitch more. But that's what I like about it.

[Qingy]("http://qingy.sourceforge.net/"), a framebuffer substitute for getty (think: login manager) that is much, much lighter than KDM/GDM and looks better than XDM/WDM. 

[Kazehakase]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/web/kazehakase"), which is a Gecko-based browser that will run circles around Firefox, especially on older machines.

[lxpanel]("http://sourceforge.net/projects/lxpanel"), because Openbox users need to dump PyPanel.

[xcompmgr]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/x11/xcompmgr"), because Openbox users can do transparency too.

[Xfe]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/x11/xfe") or [PCManFM]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/utils/pcmanfm"), if you can be bothered to choose. PCManFM has more features and looks better, but Xfe is about the fastest graphical file manager I can find, and the 0.98 version actually looks good for a change.

[rxvt-unicode]("http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/x11/rxvt-unicode"), by far the best-looking terminal emulator, for my money.

+1 for Deluge, HTop, gColor2, Audacious and rtorrent. Special runner-up prize to Midnight Commander. ;)

Wow.... There's some GREAT little programs there. I especially like the browser.... not sure if it runs rings round Firefox yet, but hey, for it's size it's a fast & speedy little prog. 

I couldn't get lxpanel to download & install though.... is it in the repos? PCManFM i already use because it's just so good, and xfe is great! 

I'm going to check out the rest of the progs a little later.... just wanted to say "Thanks" for this little list, and "Thanks" to the thread started for such a great thread, especially for those of us who either run slightly older machines, or have second machines (or even third or fourth machines) that are lower spec & could do with some lightweight apps!! :)

DJiNN

### Post by SuSUntu on 2007-05-16
> **angkor said:**
> apt-file

It makes finding dependencies when compiling from source a lot easier by being able to search for specific files **within** packages.

Run 'sudo apt-file update' before use.

I agree that this is a great tool. I've used it for some time for primarily the reason stated by Angkor, i.e., finding specific files listed during compilation (the file names mentioned in compile messages are not necessarily easily associated with a specific package that contains the file).

One elaboration / clarification to Angkor's post that may not have been clear and which really sets this utility apart is that it can find files in packages that you don't have locally available. The update process Angkor mentioned actually downloads information from your sources lists about the files contained in packages and stores that information in archives within the directory,  '/var/cache/apt/apt-file'. As an example,  apt-file creates a 181 MB file compressed to 12 MB for the us.archive.ubuntu.com repository.

----

Edit:

While I'm at it, I might as well mention another "apt" related utility that doesn't get a lot of play, but that can be useful:

apt-show-versions  

Pretty much does what you would think it does. :)

---

### Post by angkor on 2007-05-16
> **SuSUntu said:**
> One elaboration / clarification to Angkor's post that may not have been clear and which really sets this utility apart is that it can find files in packages that you don't have locally available. 

That is a good clarification. It's an important aspect I forgot to mention clearly, thanks Susuntu.

### Post by tehbeermang on 2007-05-17
I didn't read the whole 28 page thread, apologies if this is a repeat:

QBrew. I read about it here, found it in synaptic.

It's a homebrewing recipe guide. Includes the Beer Judge Certification Program (BJCP) style guide so I can build my recipes to fit in the guidelines. 

Example: I want to brew an IPA. It gives me an Original Gravity (OG) and Final Gravity (FG) target, a color target, and International Bitterness Units (IBU) target. I enter ingredients, mash temps and times (if applicable) and it tells me where in the guidelines my brew fits. 

Also includes a makeshift "brewing notebook".

Since it's open source and a tool to further my enjoyment of a hobby, I feel like adding a couple of features (when I find the time: insert laugh track)

1. Calories. The calorie computation uses measurements already taken into account by the package.
2. Integrate the brewing notebook into a blog somehow. Beer should also be open source. ;)

### Post by kalbir on 2007-05-21
I'm a big fan of **Lyx**: a program which allows you to see an approximation of the graphical output of a LATEX file whilst you are editing it (great for writing a thesis say). Also has great interaction with BibTex (for your references). You can still embed Tex commands if you are fan but it is invaluable if you are writing long (i.e. 50 pages +) text documents, particuarly if they have any mathematical symbold in them!

Top thread!

### Post by dannyboy79 on 2007-05-29
screenlets are cool but I caution you that just adding repo's to your source.list everytime you like something is very danerous! They could make a package the same as a fiesty package that you should be getting from the normal repo's and it could be a trojan or anything!!!! Little apps like these you should always compile and install from source if you want to be sure. Just an FYI for ya.

### Post by reacocard on 2007-05-30
> **dannyboy79 said:**
> screenlets are cool but I caution you that just adding repo's to your source.list everytime you like something is very danerous! They could make a package the same as a fiesty package that you should be getting from the normal repo's and it could be a trojan or anything!!!! Little apps like these you should always compile and install from source if you want to be sure. Just an FYI for ya.

It's possible, I admit, however it is unlikely. It is a good idea to check the contents of the repo before you add it, however.  Some repos (like mine) make it easy to do that, by providing html pages listing the contents. Others require a little digging, but it's usually possible.

For my own repo, I try not to overwrite anything in the repos. When I do overwrite, the packages are placed in their own component so that they are not forced on anyone. Also, my repo is 100% virus/malware free. :D

### Post by dannyboy79 on 2007-05-30
> **reacocard said:**
> It's possible, I admit, however it is unlikely. It is a good idea to check the contents of the repo before you add it, however.  Some repos (like mine) make it easy to do that, by providing html pages listing the contents. Others require a little digging, but it's usually possible.

For my own repo, I try not to overwrite anything in the repos. When I do overwrite, the packages are placed in their own component so that they are not forced on anyone. Also, my repo is 100% virus/malware free. :D
Yes, I didn't mean to say that all non-trusted repo's are bad. I just want to make sure new users are aware of the possibility of what could happen. There are many people like yourself that provide great tools and or software within their repo's and it's great that you take the time to document this for people and for you to allow people to use YOUR bandwidth, this is truely the best part about open source community. 

But their are those bad apples. I feel it's better for people to know about the risk and then to make their own informed decision so we don't have new users spreading bad rumors about linux and how as soon as they added a repo to their computer and got a virus that they say linux sucks blah blah blah which just isn't true at all!!!!

Thanks for providing a repo to the community.

### Post by ukripper on 2007-06-11
Medibuntu reporsitories - [http://medibuntu.org/repository.php](http://medibuntu.org/repository.php) . after adding lets you use win32codecs,avi,wma...etc

### Post by dannyboy79 on 2007-06-12
> **ukripper said:**
> Medibuntu reporsitories - [http://medibuntu.org/repository.php](http://medibuntu.org/repository.php) . after adding lets you use win32codecs,avi,wma...etc
[http://medibuntu.org/repository.php](http://medibuntu.org/repository.php)

Then you can enable Mozilla plugins to use Mplayer by default which plays all Windows media files within firefox.
When  you tell people about adding these, it's strongly suggested that inform them that they ARE ILLEGAL in some countries. Here's what it states on a webpage which informs you about adding them to your sources.list


Note: The following archive contains software that is illegal in certain countries, including the USA. Use at your own risk. If you are in the US, please contact your Congressional Representative about getting the Boucher-Doolittle FAIR-USE Act passed this session. 


Not to mention, are these trusted by Canacoil (or however you spell it) or are they 3rd party repo's? 3rd party repo's can put whatever they want within the repo and you could end up downloading an update that's a virus or trojan or whatever just to people are aware of that. This is not saying that medibuntu is like that, I merely feel obligated to point this out about using 3rd party repos.

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2007-06-12
**COOL OPEN SOURCE GAMES**

[**Tremulous**]("http://tremulous.net") - Tremulous is a free and open source team-based first-person shooter with RTS elements that is receiving so much fuss and hype. It is believed to become a Open Source legend.  *Can be found in Feisty Fawn's Multiverse Repository.*

[**Nexuiz**]("http://alientrap.org/nexuiz/") - Nexuiz is a free software 3D first-person shooter computer distributed under the GNU General Public License.  *[I]Found in Feisty Fawn's Universe Repository.*[/I]

[**AssaultCube**]("http://assault.cubers.net/") - AssaultCube, formerly called "ActionCube", is a free first-person-shooter based on the game Cube. Set in a realistic looking environment, as far as that´s possible with this engine, while gameplay stays fast and arcade. This game is all about team oriented multiplayer fun.  You'll have to* download from *[their website]("http://assault.cubers.net/"), or get it at [URL="http://www.getdeb.net/app.php?name=AssaultCube"]GetDeb.net
[/URL]

### Post by IYY on 2007-06-19
[Liquid War]("http://www.ufoot.org/liquidwar/v5") is a fun, little and very original game. You control an "army"; a swarm of tiny coloured dots that follow your cursor. When they clash with enemy dots, they fight and destroy them. It can be played with several players in hotseat or a network, or against a rather weak AI. There are many cool maps.

I guess this isn't really little-known, but [Second Life]("http://www.secondlife.com/") is an MMORPG (although it is more flexible than usual, without any levels or quests, and the ability to create content in-game). It's free to play, except that property costs real money. Some areas are rather horrible (think a giant 3D myspace, with furries and giant orgies), but some are a pleasure to be in (for example, New Babbage and Caledon are Victorian, Steampunk cities).

[Open Arena]("http://openarena.ws/?about") is also fairly well known, but is worth mentioning. It's basically a completely Free version of Quake 3. Great if you want some quick online shooting.

---

### Post by Onyros on 2007-06-20
I had been looking for a lighter alternative to Gajim, because I don't really like the way Pidgin handles multiple accounts, because sometimes I want to offline in one and online in another, away in one, available in another and Pidgin's not flexible for that.

Gajim was great for that, but has it's written in Python instead of C or C++ it's actually a little on the heavier side. So I tried Gabber (2), but one of my Jabber contacts is a Google account and I couldn't connect to it using Gabber.

Kept on looking until I found [Gossip]("http://developer.imendio.com/projects/gossip/") IM, and even though it has a feature I dislike, as iit auto-logs every conversation BUT has no option to disable that or even to clear the history of logs, or to erase a particular log... as I can just go to Gossip's logs folder and erase it by hand, it's all good.

It's just a simple IM alternative for using several Jabber accounts, but as it's lightweight and functional, good looking AFTER I changed its icons, but I do recommend it to anyone who uses the Jabber protocol and just wants a simple, lightweight IM client that works well with no fancy features, though.

There are Feisty packages available at [GetDeb]("http://www.getdeb.net/search.php?keywords=gossip").

---

### Post by forrestcupp on 2007-06-21
[T@b Media Converter](http://www.thugsatbay.com/tab/?q=tab-video-converter-encoder) is an awesome program that will convert audio/video files to a different format.  It is a sweet front end to mencoder and sox.  You can input and output most formats.

It's not in the repos, but at their website they have Ubuntu-compiled binaries available in a tar.gz.  You just untar it to /home or wherever and run the binary file.

This was recently a life saver for me.

Edit:
If you want to try it, click on the "Linux Download Info" link rather than the straight link to the file download.  On the info page, you can download an Ubuntu specific tar.gz.

### Post by cleentrax on 2007-06-25
Scribes has already been mentioned, but it's the best editor I have found for live edits on files on a remote server. Also, great snippets/auto-completion features. Just wish it had better multi-file search/replace.

Have yet to find a decent ftp client for Linux. Yes, I've tried them all. OS X has an embarrassing number of good ones, including Transmit, Cyberduck, OneFTP, etc. Currently I use gFTP for complex transfers, and Nautilus for simple transfers and live editing. But neither is stellar.

### Post by k420 on 2007-06-27
> **tehbeermang said:**
> I didn't read the whole 28 page thread, apologies if this is a repeat:

QBrew. I read about it here, found it in synaptic.

It's a homebrewing recipe guide. Includes the Beer Judge Certification Program (BJCP) style guide so I can build my recipes to fit in the guidelines. 

Example: I want to brew an IPA. It gives me an Original Gravity (OG) and Final Gravity (FG) target, a color target, and International Bitterness Units (IBU) target. I enter ingredients, mash temps and times (if applicable) and it tells me where in the guidelines my brew fits. 

Also includes a makeshift "brewing notebook".

Since it's open source and a tool to further my enjoyment of a hobby, I feel like adding a couple of features (when I find the time: insert laugh track)

1. Calories. The calorie computation uses measurements already taken into account by the package.
2. Integrate the brewing notebook into a blog somehow. Beer should also be open source. ;)
wow being an open brewer and a ubuntu fan myself i find this a most amazing tool

---

### Post by odiseo77 on 2007-06-27
Don't know if this one has been posted, but the app I use to communicate with my friends over msn is [Mercury Messenger]("http://www.mercury.to"). I think many people might not know about it and it's very good; has webcam support, skins, etc. The only thing other people might not like is that is not open source (but it's free).

Oh, and other thing.: the packages on the official site are quite old, so, if you want to download the latest beta/RC you have to join the forum.

---

### Post by stmiller on 2007-06-27
wajig

Useful to hold a package back from Ubuntu updates. For instance, if you want to keep your present kernel and avoid kernel updates.

```

$ wajig hold <packagename>

```

---

### Post by k420 on 2007-06-27
APTONCD best one out there thankyah thankyah thankya 
if you do not know what this appZ does here is a description from there website 
APTonCD is a tool with a graphical interface which allows you to create one or more CDs or DVDs (you choose the type of media) with all of the packages you've downloaded via APT-GET or APTITUDE, creating a removable repository that you can use on other computers.
APTonCD will also allow you to automatically create media with all of your .deb packages located in one especific repository, so that you can install them into your computers without the need for an internet conection.

---

### Post by techno-mole on 2007-06-29
i dont know if its been emntioned because im too lazy to read through all 40 odd pages, but i use qjoypad, its for configuring your gamepad strangely enough, it lets you use keystrokes for actions on the gamepad.
so for example you can program it to work with beryl, and other stuff, some people have used it to turn their game pads into remote controls for watching dvds and tv on their pc,s 
i think its a good little applications if you need such a thing.
[http://qjoypad.sourceforge.net/](http://qjoypad.sourceforge.net/)

cheers.

### Post by smartboyathome on 2007-06-29
I dunno if this was said, but I use [Tilda]("http://tilda.sourceforge.net/") quite a lot. It is a a Quake-like console for Gnome, and is now easily customizable. Also, I use [Desktop Icon Preferences]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=421266") to organize my desktop.

Screenlets are definately not as popular as Superkaramba, but I find it useful because the Superkaramba in the repos is still at 3.5. Lastly, I use Opera (I know, people may know of this, but I want to mention it anyway) because it is faster than Firefox (Firefox is BLOATED) while still being really functional.

### Post by dannyboy79 on 2007-07-03
well maybe after more than 5 years but I know that I've found threads created back in 2003 within gogle, they are located within ubuntuforum archive.

Check out some awesome ubuntuforums facts!

over 14,000 new accounts each month 
average ~22,000 new threads a month 
average ~136,000 new posts each month 
average ~3.7 million visits each month 
average ~12.6 million page views per month 
~74% of visitors use Firefox 
~12% of visitors use IE 
~61% of visitors use Linux 
~35% of visitors use Windows 
~57% of traffic is recurring visitors 
~42% of traffic is new traffic visitors 
~69% of traffic comes from google 
~5% of traffic comes from *.ubuntu.com 
~3% of traffic comes from digg.com

As far as personal wikis go I like using [TiddlyWiki](http://www.tiddlywiki.com/). Not in the repositories but that's because it's only an html file. This makes it very portable, since everything is contained in one file and it can be edited by any browser. I find it useful to open it along with my homepage every time I open my browser with anything I need to be reminded of.

I also like using the Tea text editor.

### Post by DARKGuy on 2007-08-20
**Audacious** - Similar to XMMS but newer. Still the same thing with bonuses and I love it because it's WAY less bloat than Amarok or other players out there.

**Notepad++** (Emulated through WINE) - Flawless text editor which I use for programming and web development. Extendable with Plugins (which work) and I've *never* had a crash with it since Edgy :), very stable and I consider it even more powerful than gedit itself. It's also a good replacement for Kate for those who don't want to have KDE apps in their Gnome system.

**Mercury Messenger** - It's WAY better than aMSN, though it's Java-based and it might slow down your PC if you chat a lot... it's a Java drawback, but if you have a fast processor > 1Ghz by all means use it, you'll have all the features MSN has (and more!) it's skinnable as hell and the development team (Danny) is really into it, so you always get support through their forum. You won't miss winks, webcam, audio conference and custom emoticons anymore ^^.

**uTorrent** - Well maybe everyone here knows about it, but for those who don't it can be emulated through WINE and it's the best out there (anybody know a terminal-based one which can resume torrents if my PC screws up and decides to restart itself? xD).

**ies4Linux** - Internet Explorer for Linux (ie6 and 7 emulated through WINE)... it's for those websites that say you're not using Internet Explorer, you can slap them with it :P

**RapidSVN** - Lightweight basic SVN interface.

**Rainlendar2** - Skinnable, lightweight and powerful desktop calendar/ToDo/events list (compatible with Compiz Fusion!!).

**youTranslate** - Translate text from/to lots of languages without accessing a webpage to do it.

Those are all the ones I can think of right now. Oh, and btw thanks for the one who pointed out Xara Extreme, looks damn useful :D

---

### Post by FuturePilot on 2007-08-20
Nautilus image converter. I don't know if this has been mentioned already but it's a little extension for Nautilus that lets you easily resize and rotate images. Right click on an image and there are 2 options in the right click menu you can choose from. Very handy little thing.:)
```
sudo apt-get install nautilus-image-converter
```

 How to use µTorrent under Wine

wine uTorrent-1.6.1-install.exe

```

Not sure, but it worked like magic...

### Post by andrew.46 on 2007-08-22
Hi,

 I have gone through all the pages on this fascinating thread and I seem to be the first person to mention the amazing ripper / encoder / tagger program abdcde [A Better CD Encoder].

 It is in the repositories and I have published a very brief guide to using the program to produce mp3s:

[http://people.aapt.net.au/~adjlstrong/ubuntu_cli.html#mp3](http://people.aapt.net.au/~adjlstrong/ubuntu_cli.html#mp3)

 But of course you can also encode to ogg or flac. This is a CLI program that is significantly faster than the usual Ubuntu GUI ripper / Encoders.

             Andrew

### Post by finferflu on 2007-08-28
Not really an app, but really worth trying: dwm. 
It's a tiny small ultra light window manager, ultra intuitive and clever. And if you ask me it's also quite elegant, unlike other minimal ugly ones (like ion, ratpoison and the like, I'm only talking about aesthetics here).
The idea is that of a dynamic window manager, where the windows are automatically positioned by the WM, so as to improve productivity. The method which they are arranged is tiling, so you get all windows shown on the screen at the same time (you can also switch to the floating mode if you want, but there's not much point usually). You have 2 areas, a master area and a tiled area, they are divided vertically. The window in master area occupies the whole vertical space, whereas in the tiled area the rest of the windows share the vertical space in equal section. You can switch between windows to select which one occupies the master area, which is very cool.  
Another very clever feature is that of binding windows to desktops (called tags), so you can have a window turning up on desktop 1, 5, and 8. Of course you can also configure where a particular application is going to turn up when launched. I have divided my workspaces by tasks, so on 1 I have internet related stuff, on 2 terminals, 3 file browsing and so on, and if I run Firefox it turns up on desktop 1 even though I run it from another desktop. 
Well, this is not all, but they are the features that bought me, you better try this :)

[[img]http://xs118.xs.to/xs118/07353/dwm.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs118&d=07353&f=dwm.png)

---

### Post by dentaku65 on 2007-08-30
**Scite**
A little and nice text editor, in the repos

SciTE is a SCIntilla based Text Editor. Originally built to demonstrate Scintilla, it has grown to be a generally useful editor with facilities for building and running programs. It is best used for jobs with simple configurations - I use it for building test and demonstration programs as well as SciTE and Scintilla, themselves.

[http://www.scintilla.org/SciTE.html](http://www.scintilla.org/SciTE.html)

### Post by FuturePilot on 2007-09-01
Not sure if this one has been posted already, but if you use Bluetooth with your phone, gnome-vfs-obexftp will let you browse the files on your phone in Nautilus. You can also add and delete files too.
```
sudo apt-get install gnome-vfs-obexftp
```
Then just type obex:/// in the address bar.

---

### Post by Duffman2010 on 2007-09-05
yeahconsole, will make xterm or urxvt act like tilda. 

```
sudo apt-get install yeahconsole rxvt-unicode
```

Here is mi Xdefaults for yeachonsole:

```

yeahconsole*toggleKey: None+F1
yeahconsole*keyFull: Alt+f
yeahconsole*background:  rgb:00/00/00
yeahconsole*foreground: rgb:ff/ff/ff
yeahconsole*loginShell:True
yeahconsole*consoleHeight: 40
yeahconsole*aniDelay:0 
yeahconsole*stepSize:20 
yeahconsole*handleWidth:3
yeahconsole*handleColor: rgb:22/22/22
yeahconsole*term:urxvt
yeahconsole*scrollBar: false
yeahconsole*reverseVideo: false
yeahconsole*tintColor: grey40
yeahconsole*inheritPixmap: true
!yeahconsole*font: -*-fixed-*-*-*-*-*-110-*-*-*-*-iso8859-15
!yeahconsole*boldFont: -*-fixed-*-*-*-*-*-110-*-*-*-*-iso8859-15
yeahconsole*saveLines: 10000
yeahconsole*cursorBlink: false
yeahconsole*font: xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=12:antialias=true:hinting=true
yeahconsole*boldFont: xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=12:antialias=true:hinting=true
yeahconsole*italicFont: xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=12:antialias=true:italic:autohint=true:hinting=true
yeahconsole*bolditalicFont: xft:DejaVu Sans Mono:pixelsize=12:antialias=true:italic:autohint=true:hinting=true
yeahconsole*color12: DodgerBlue2
yeahconsole*fading:   50
yeahconsole*shading:   50

```

then run 

```
xrdb -merge ~/.Xdefaults
```

finally
```
yeahconsole
```

now F1 will drop a transparent terminal, and alt+f will make it fullscreen

enjoy!

---

### Post by johnraff on 2007-09-07
Quick plug for Dillo- a really fast browser. ### Post by Ingo88 on 2007-09-16
Great thread! I have now read through all the 47 pages, and it sure was worth it :D

Here are my favorites:

**Qalculate!** - A calculator with LOADS of features
**Stellarium** - Nice program for exploring the sky at night. It can even render pictures of the different constellations! On top of that, it is translated into many languages
**Secret Maryo Chronicles** - This really seems to be a nice Mario clone
**Agave** - A program that tells you what colors go together. This could be useful when you want a color scheme
**OnTV** - Shows the current program on TV channels you choose, the next program and when the next program begins. In addition to that you can easily search for programs and add reminders. The program list it downloads lasts for many days, so you don't even have to update so often

To make this post a little more useful I also want to make an addition of my own. It is my favorite Linux game so far:

**[Blob Wars: Metal Blob Solid](http://www.parallelrealities.co.uk/blobWars.php)** - A very good 2D platform/shooter from Parallel Realities. This is one I really recommend. It is in the repos (package name is *[blobwars](http://packages.ubuntu.com/feisty/games/blobwars)*). There is a sequel in the making called **[Blob Wars: Blob and Conquer](http://www.parallelrealities.co.uk/blobAndConquer.php)**, which is in 3D. That one's not in the repos, though, but you can get it from [GetDeb](http://www.getdeb.net/app.php?name=Blob+and+Conquer).

### Post by TeaSwigger on 2007-09-21
GPicView is yet another image viewer - however it is by far the fastest and lightest GUI type image viewer I've ever seen, noticeably faster even than the (superb) Mirage, and even a smidgin faster than GQView. Instant on my PIII. Great if you want a snappy GUI image viewer and heaven sent for older or slower units.

> **finferflu said:**
> I find it very annoying to load OpenOffice every time I have to read a document, so this is a very quick and elegant way to do that :D

A tip in case you don't already know; if / when you do have to open OpenOffice, it will load a whole lot faster if you uncheck the option to use javascript in preferences, and may render a tidbit faster still if you don't have it show the rulers in print mode. Those features are seldom needed and may be easily reinstated if they are needed, while disabling them cut the load time on my old PC to less than half.

Also I suggest looking into AbiWord. It's far lighter and faster and it will read and write most Word and OpenOffice docs. The ruler tip above also applies to AbiWord but it's only likely to matter on older or slower PCs. The drawbacks to AbiWord compared to OpenOffice Writer is that AbiWord lacks many features and won't handle very large (say, 5mb +) files well. Nothing wrong with having both and using them depending on requirements :)

---

### Post by malachias on 2007-09-21
I am amazed that this only got mentioned in the entire thread ONCE (well, twice, but the second time was in passing).
A definite +1 to:

mpd + mpc + conky

This is the best music solution I have ever come across. Ever. Add gmpc into the bargain and it becomes a little more user-friendly (there are other clients too), but personally I just added buttons to my panel for everything I'd want to do and wrote a shell script ask me which saved playlist I want to use.

With conky, your "player" can be right on your desktop, and your music keeps on going, even if you log out, have to restart X, whatever. If you're one of those people who hates it when your music goes down because you're upgrading your graphics drivers, or just plain trying to get compiz-fusion to work (unless you're REALLY lucky), this is definitely for you. It may seem a little complicated with the whole server/client setup, but it's really simple to use just locally as a music player.

---

### Post by Allysan on 2007-09-22
Someone may have posted it already (no way am I reading 48 pages) but for note taking in all my classes I use BasKet Note Pads.  It's designed for KDE but works in Gnome as well.  It's an excellent little application that lets you take notes and apply various different tags (such as a To-Do tag- puts a checkbox next to each note so you can check it off when you've completed the task) to your notes.  All your notes are saved automatically each time they're changed so you never have to worry about losing your work because of a power failure or any other reason.   You can also back up your notes to a tar.gz file if you're still worried.  New sections may be created with just a single click and a left hand "tree" style pane allows you to organize your notes however you like.  I highly recommend BasKet to the college student or anyone who prefers to take notes digitally.

---

### Post by finferflu on 2007-09-22

### Post by olejorgen on 2007-09-22

pdftotext <pdf file> **-** | less
```

### Post by rsambuca on 2007-09-25
> **raul_ said:**
> What about ```
./install
``` ?

No.

If you downloaded the tarball (.tgz file), then you must first unpack the tarball:```
cd /where/the/tgz/is (eg /home/yourname/Desktop)
tar -zxvf <name of tgz>
```
Then have a read through the install and readme files for a quick rundown.

Then run the following three commands:

./configure
make
sudo make install

---

tar -zxvf <name of tgz>
```
Then have a read through the install and readme files for a quick rundown.

Then run the following three commands:

sudo apt-get install build-essential
```

### Post by drfox on 2007-09-25

me@mylinux:~/Desktop/XnView-1.70-x86-unknown-linux2.x-static-fc4$ sudo sh ./install
  OS  : Linux, version 2.6.22-12-generic
This script will install nview/nconvert/xnview in the /usr/local/bin directory
cp: cannot create regular file `/usr/lib/X11/app-defaults/XnView': No such file or directory
chmod: cannot access `/usr/lib/X11/app-defaults/XnView': No such file or directory

Done!

### Post by Scruffynerf on 2007-09-26
Re: XnView

Try downloading the .rpm version.

Then ```
sudo alien - i XnView-static-fc4.i386.rpm
```

That's how I installed it on my Ubuntu.

Note: Must have 'alien' installed from the repo's. Allows package installations of .rpm files. No need to mess around with configuring and make install.

---

### Post by fuscia on 2007-09-26
> **Scruffynerf said:**
> Re: XnView

Try downloading the .rpm version.

Then ```
sudo alien - i XnView-static-fc4.i386.rpm
```

you need to lose the space between the '-' and the 'i'. then, it works.

---

### Post by Scruffynerf on 2007-09-26
> **fuscia said:**
> you need to lose the space between the '-' and the 'i'. then, it works.

cheers. Was posting from work and was working from memory.

### Post by K.Mandla on 2007-09-26

### Post by phetre on 2007-09-27
> **kadath said:**
> It's built using XUL, like Firefox, so yes, it's slow and bloated.

Miro is *much* slower than Firefox on my machine. There must be more to it than XUL.

My underappreciated faves:
[LIST]
[*][Celestia]("http://www.shatters.net/celestia/"): A 3d model of space. Yes, you can FLY THROUGH SPACE. A previous poster prefers Stellarium because "it's like looking at the sky" (see also: Google Sky), but that's exactly why I prefer Celestia. Available in standard repositories.

[*][Zotero]("http://www.zotero.org/"): A citation manager and more. I tried Bibus, EndNote (not on Linux), RefWorks, Bibtex, and the OpenOffice bibliographic tools, but none of them felt right. It was hard even to get most of them to output Chicago Style citations. Zotero is an open-source ([ECL]("http://www.opensource.org/licenses/ecl1.php")) Firefox extension that also offers plugins for MS Word and OpenOffice Writer. To me, it feels like the right tool for the job. Available from zotero.org.
[/LIST]

### Post by Paqman on 2007-09-27
> **FuturePilot said:**
> Deskbar applet. Right click on the Gnome panel>Add to Panel. Select Deskbar.
This thing is pretty cool. It does just about everything. You can launch applications from it, search for files, and even search the web.

Just discovered this little gem. Combined with a decent indexing tool like Beagle it's fantastic.

Seems to be pretty memory hungry, but if you can spare 40MB or so it's well worth it.

### Post by olejorgen on 2007-09-28
Not something you'll use everyday, but **archmage** is a great utility if you have to deal with .chm files. Usually most people will find and use gnochm, which is quite lacking imho. archmage extracts the html files and images instead, enabling a normal browser to view the files.

Theres nothing else out there like this!

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2007-09-29
**BomberClone** one of the most fun games :) As the name suggest it is a clone of the famous Bomber Man game in PlayStation, Nintendo64, Famicon, etc. Well, actually it is a clone of FamiCon (Super Nintengo in USA)  
You can find it in the respositories. 

```
sudo aptitude install bomberclone
```

### Post by julian67 on 2007-10-12
A great CD Ripper: [Asunder](http://littlesvr.ca/asunder/)

>     *  Can save audio tracks as WAV, MP3, Ogg Vorbis, and FLAC audio files
    * Uses CDDB to name and tag each track
    * Creates M3U playlists
    * *Can encode to multiple formats in one session*
    * Simultaneous rip and encode
    * Allows for each track to be by a different artist
    * Does not require a specific desktop environment



(my italics) It's great to encode to multiple formats simultaneously. The interface is much the same as Sound-Juicer but Asunder is GTK 2 and not tied to Gnome.

[Ripit](http://www.suwald.com/ripit/ripit.html) is even better though is cli not gui. It can do everything other rippers can do and more. I like it because it can encode to multiple formats simultaneously and the output can be saved in different folders in different locations, everything tagged each folder with its own playlist. Fast, simple and perfect! 

> The program will do the following without user intervention:

  # gets the Audio CD Album/Artist/Tracks information from CDDB
  # rips the Audio CD Tracks
  # encodes to flac, mp3 or ogg
  # id3 tags encoded songs
  # Creates an playlist (m3u) file
  # Can generate a toc (cue) sheet for nice DAO burning
  # Can prepare and send a CDDB submission and save it locally
  # Can extract hidden songs and split ghost songs
  # May create md5sum files for all tracks
  # Run several encoder processes at the same time and same run



[Cryptkeeper](http://www.tomatarium.pwp.blueyonder.co.uk/cryptkeeper.html)

> Cryptkeeper is a FreeDesktop.org (KDE, Gnome, XFce, etc.) system tray applet that manages EncFS encrypted folders.

Very neat and cool way to create/manage encrypted folders from a simple tray applet. 

[xpad](http://xpad.sourceforge.net/)

> Simple, attractive sticky notes
 
Xpad is a GTK+ application that emulates real-life sticky notes. If you are likely to forget something, open up an xpad and jot it down.


I prefer this to the sticky notes apps from Gnome or Xfce.

[Alltray](http://alltray.sourceforge.net/)

> With AllTray you can dock any application with no native tray icon (like Evolution, Thunderbird, Terminals) into the system tray. A high-light feature is that a click on the "close" button will minimize back to system tray.  It works well with Gnome,  KDE,  XFCE 4*, Fluxbox* and WindowMaker*

*no drag 'n drop support .

### Post by peitschie on 2007-10-12
For sync-ing up multiple computers, you can do as many as you want, in many synchronization modes including mirror, autodownload, download new etc:
Powerfolder
[http://www.powerfolder.com](http://www.powerfolder.com)

It is open source, but not quite fully free.  The free version has a limit on 3 folders & 10Gb or less of shared files.  This is ample for me to synchronize my laptop and PC however.  It can do multiway sync as well which is the coolest option.  ie., sync with more than 3 computers!  Also can swarm over the internet ;-)

---

### Post by julian67 on 2007-10-12
The free version is released under gpl v2 and source code is made available.
