```

Note that there is at least one package (possibly many) that has been mentioned but does not show up in the above list: Xara Xtreme. The reason is (can you believe it?) its package name has never been mentioned: xaralx. 

There are also some packages that won't show up in the list because they are not in the official repositories, such as wicd. I generated the list on a Gutsy machine, so my list refers to packages available on Gutsy only. If you run a different version and you don't want to miss any packages that are available for your system but not on Gutsy, you'll have to run the program below yourself.

To get more info on a package, you can use your favorite GUI, or type

```
apt-cache show <package name>
```

To generate the list, I used the [thread-listing program]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=4782850&postcount=880") and this:

```

#!/usr/bin/env python
from bz2 import BZ2File
from os import popen
import os
import re
from string import lower

pkghash={}
threadhash={}
wordboundary=re.compile(r"[^a-zA-Z0-9-]+")

cmd='apt-cache dumpavail | grep ^Package | awk \'{printf $2\"\\n"}\''
pkgfile=popen(cmd,'r')
for pkg in pkgfile:
    pkg=pkg.rstrip('\n')
    if pkg not in pkghash:
        pkghash[pkg]=1

pkgfile.close()

thread = BZ2File('thread382137.txt.bz2', 'r')

for line in thread:
    wordlist=wordboundary.split(line)
    for word in wordlist:
        lword=lower(word)
        if lword not in threadhash:
            threadhash[lword]=1
        else:
            threadhash[lword]+=1
thread.close()

mentioned={}
for pkg, value in threadhash.iteritems():    
    if pkg in pkghash:
        mentioned[pkg]=value

histogram = [ (value, pkg) for pkg, value in mentioned.iteritems() ]
histogram.sort()
histogram.reverse()
for value, pkg in histogram:
    print pkg,value
#    os.system('apt-cache show '+pkg)

```

Save it as 'parse-for-packages.py', make it executable
```

chmod 755 parse-for-packages.py
```

Then just run

```
./parse-for-packages.py
```

### Post by Mr. Picklesworth on 2008-05-22
*GASP* A thread search tells me nobody has mentioned Glom. I recently realized I could replace a pile of ugly Excel spreadsheets with a nice Glom database for some people, and have been delighted. Really easy to use, powerful and handy :)

Beats out OOo Database for me, since it has a *really* tidy interface and uses proper GTK.

Also rather interesting is X Window Information (wininfo). For some reason I had fallen into a misconception that the X window system did not follow that clever "everything - even a widget - is a window" concept. That tool knocked some sense back into me!

### Post by dizee on 2008-05-22
Almost cerainly been mentioned, but **xnest** is a program that allows you to login to another session in a window, among other things.

Simply install xnest, go to the Login Window options and uncheck the "Disable multiple logins for single user" box, and run ```
gdmflexiserver --xnest
```

Screenshot shows an Xfce session, with an Openbox session running in xnest.

---

### Post by chochem on 2008-05-23
If 'simplifying what most apps make complex' is cool, then there isn't anything cooler, than [curlftpfs]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CurlFtpFS"). It simply mounts (through ftp) my web server on a local directory and allows me to access it through whatever file manager or terminal I please. 

The connection is excellent and I've yet to see curlftpfs drop it. It evens tell me that how many terabytes free space the server holds - not that I could use without getting kicked off by the hosting provider but it's still cool... If you don't mind having your password lying unencrypted on your hard drive (you probably should), you can even have the system automount it at startup or by scripting.

---

### Post by cardinals_fan on 2008-05-25
It's not an app per se, but XKB lets you customize your keyboard layout.  Three key switches let me have some of Dvorak's efficiency with the familiarity of QWERTY.  Read this: [http://www.linux.com/articles/113715](http://www.linux.com/articles/113715)

I also can't believe that dmenu has only been mentioned once.  It's obscenely useful.  Urukrama has a good writeup at [http://urukrama.wordpress.com/2008/02/07/using-dmenu-in-pekwm-and-openbox/](http://urukrama.wordpress.com/2008/02/07/using-dmenu-in-pekwm-and-openbox/)

### Post by pastormick on 2008-05-27
I have always wanted an idiot-proof (in my case...) dvd-to-avi converter. I found just the thing to convert movies for my Nokia N800; 'Media Converter 1.43' - [http://mediaconverter.garage.maemo.org/Media%20Converter.html](http://mediaconverter.garage.maemo.org/Media%20Converter.html)
 
Last night I converted 20 hours worth of tour video into .avi's that fit on only 2 DVD's. :shock: The quality is great, the speed is incredible, and it's really hard to mess it up...

Mick

### Post by Onyros on 2008-05-28
> **pastormick said:**
> I have always wanted an idiot-proof (in my case...) dvd-to-avi converter. I found just the thing to convert movies for my Nokia N800; 'Media Converter 1.43' - [http://mediaconverter.garage.maemo.org/Media%20Converter.html](http://mediaconverter.garage.maemo.org/Media%20Converter.html)
 
Last night I converted 20 hours worth of tour video into .avi's that fit on only 2 DVD's. :shock: The quality is great, the speed is incredible, and it's really hard to mess it up...

MickI used that too, and it's pretty cool, indeed. Too bad that its Java interface doesn't work too well with Awesome.

I circumvented that by starting it with a different window manager, enabling the verbose output in the status window and then copying the mencoder options and just started the preset that fit best on my N800 on the terminal.

I'll add one that's been mentioned before but that shouldn't go forgotten, as it's priceless --> [Meld]("http://meld.sourceforge.net/")

Meld is a "diff and merge tool", meaning, I use it to compare both file contents and folder contents and then proceed with changes whenever needed by either replacing the older content or by editing the files directly in a new tab.

For example, I usually move files between computers, and the fact that one's older than the other doesn't always mean that's an older version of the file: I'll always need to compare the contents and then decide which version supersedes the other; sometimes there is valuable info in both and I'll just merge.

Meld is THE (GUI) tool for that :)

### Post by calraith on 2008-05-30
Check out [SecPanel]("http://secpanel.net/").  It's a GUI for launching ssh and scp (or rsync) sessions.  It's in the repos.  It's not all that pretty, but it's useful if you have a buttload of servers you remote into.  Unlike putty, it works with your existing public / private keys -- no need for puttygen.

### Post by Thanoulis on 2008-06-02
Here is a list of my favorite CLI utiltities:

centerim-utf8 : icq,irc,msn,yahho,etc client
hnb : outliner-notebook
links2 : web browser with X support
mutt : nice and fully customizable email client
rtorrent : fast torrent client
mpd+mpc+ncmpc : best music apps..ever :)
hexcurse : ncurses based hex editor
htop : view and manage processes
iftop : as top, but for net
unp : easy to use unarchiver frontend

As for graphical apps here we go:

agave : pick the correct color
deluge-torrent : best torrent client (for my money :P)
qalculate-gtk : best calculator (as said before)
specimen : font previewer
stardict : dictionary with endless capabilities
apwal : application laucher with lot of fun
dzen2 : make you messages. menus, everything
dmenu (in dwm-tools) : handy application launcher
feh : fast image viewer
gmrun : better than the gnome Alt+F2 run IMHO
gmount-iso : like daemon-tools but for gtk

---

Zim is a desktop wiki. I guess it's very similar to Tomboy notes which you may be familiar with, but is designed for a more general purpose. Htop is a fine alternative to top, try it out, it is in the repositories.

Are you serious?  I've never seen or used a terminal application that let you CLICK "quit" !!!!

I haven't been a linux user for more than 3 months, but that is something very new to me! Awesome!

---

### Post by FuturePilot on 2008-06-12
+1 for Htop. I use it all the time. It shows a lot of things that don't show up in gnome-system-monitor by default or even at all.


I just discovered [Kdocker]("http://kdocker.sourceforge.net/"). It's similar to Alltray but written in QT. Though I've found it to have more features than Alltray and actually run lighter on resources than Alltray. Just
```
sudo apt-get install kdocker
kdocker
```
and click on a window to put it in the notification tray. It's a good workaround, although maybe not the most optimal, for Evolution's lack of ability to minimize to the tray.

### Post by Stefanie on 2008-06-12
i just discovered a gui for pdftk (a tool for editing pdf-files): [http://www.paehl.de/pdf/gui_pdftk.html](http://www.paehl.de/pdf/gui_pdftk.html)

i tried it and it's really great! (the site is written in weird english because the developer is german, but you can trust it). you can install pdftk from the repos, but you should get the gui from the site i mentioned. 
i downloaded the binary package for linux; after extracting i got 2 files. i just copied those to /usr/bin and now i can have a simple gui by running guipdftk from the command line :-)

### Post by fifth on 2008-06-17
I use Jed for console text editing, small and light and still does syntax hilighting and provides a file browser.

```
sudo apt-get install jed
```

From Synaptic:
> editor for programmers (textmode version)
Jed is a small, fast (faster startup than bash) and powerful text editor.

Completely customizable with prepared emulation modes for Emacs, CUA
(similar to KDE/Gnome/Openoffice), Borland-IDE, Brief, and EDT. Extensible
in the S-Lang scripting language (with a syntax resembling C).

Editing functions: folding support; rectangular cut/paste; regular
expression search/replace; incremental searches; search/replace across
multiple files; multiple windows; multiple buffers; ...

Tools: directory editor (dired); info (browse GNU info files); mail;
rmail; ispell; shell mode; ...

Special modes (syntax highlight, indention, compile, ...) for
Basic, C, C++, DCL, FORTRAN, IDL, Java, NROFF, Pascal,
Perl, PHP, PostScript, Python, SH.
Modes for markup languages include HTML and (La)TeX (with AUC-TeX style
editing and BibTeX)

Additional tools and modes can be found in the jed-extra package.

 Homepage: [http://www.jedsoft.org/jed/](http://www.jedsoft.org/jed/)

### Post by raul_ on 2008-06-18
I think atool deserves another mention (only one so far).

It's a command line wrapper for the most commons compression utilities (zip,gunzip,bzip,7zip, tar, rar)

So you just type "atool -x file.rar" or "file.zip" "file.tar.gz", instead of using 3 different applications.

A must-have for CL junkies

### Post by urukrama on 2008-06-19
> **raul_ said:**
> It's a command line wrapper for the most commons compression utilities (zip,gunzip,bzip,7zip, tar, rar)

Isn't that what bash aliases are for? ;-) With the following in my .bashrc I just need to do "extract package.tar.gz/.zip/.rar" to extract an archive:

```
extract () {
     if [ -f $1 ] ; then
         case $1 in
             *.tar.bz2)   tar xjf $1        ;;
             *.tar.gz)    tar xzf $1     ;;
             *.bz2)       bunzip2 $1       ;;
             *.rar)       rar x $1     ;;
             *.gz)        gunzip $1     ;;
             *.tar)       tar xf $1        ;;
             *.tbz2)      tar xjf $1      ;;
             *.tgz)       tar xzf $1       ;;
             *.zip)       unzip $1     ;;
             *.Z)         uncompress $1  ;;
             *.7z)        7z x $1    ;;
             *)           echo "'$1' cannot be extracted via extract()" ;;
         esac
     else
         echo "'$1' is not a valid file"
     fi
}
```

---

### Post by raul_ on 2008-06-19
> **urukrama said:**
> Isn't that what bash aliases are for? ;-) With the following in my .bashrc I just need to do "extract package.tar.gz/.zip/.rar" to extract an archive:

```
extract () {
     if [ -f $1 ] ; then
         case $1 in
             *.tar.bz2)   tar xjf $1        ;;
             *.tar.gz)    tar xzf $1     ;;
             *.bz2)       bunzip2 $1       ;;
             *.rar)       rar x $1     ;;
             *.gz)        gunzip $1     ;;
             *.tar)       tar xf $1        ;;
             *.tbz2)      tar xjf $1      ;;
             *.tgz)       tar xzf $1       ;;
             *.zip)       unzip $1     ;;
             *.Z)         uncompress $1  ;;
             *.7z)        7z x $1    ;;
             *)           echo "'$1' cannot be extracted via extract()" ;;
         esac
     else
         echo "'$1' is not a valid file"
     fi
}
```

Cool, i've never thought of that

### Post by suzypeppercorn on 2008-06-19
i've spent about a week going through this thread and it is the best thread ever.

the apps that after testing i have decided to keep are:

filelight - a graphical representation of your hard drive
gnome-do - an app launcher that has many plugins that give it the edge over similar apps.

qalculate - a great calculator
stellarium - a very detailed star lab
teeworlds - a very addictive multiplayer 2-d shooter
agave - easy to use color chooser
devede - converts video files to dvd formats
miro - a great program to collect and watch video podcasts(like trs and diggnation)
fslint - finds and deletes unnecessary files and folders
htop - displays all processes and shows their cpu and memory usage it also lets you kill processes too.

xcruise - a cool app that lets you fly through space except that the whole universe is your file directory.

the next 2 i'm not for sure if they have been mentioned or not but here goes:

BOINC Manager - a distributed computing program that lets you sign up for various projects similar to Folding@home. (I'm signed up for SETI)

Cheese - a great picture or video taking application that i had no problem getting to work.

I'm pretty sure all of these apps can be found in the repos. If not please correct me.

Thanks for everyone else contributions!!

### Post by stevieP on 2008-06-21
sam2p can convert jpg, png, gif... images to pdf or eps format, with compression much better than imagemagick.  (files are much smaller).
[http://www.inf.bme.hu/~pts/sam2p/](http://www.inf.bme.hu/~pts/sam2p/)

It runs as follows:
$ sam2p  file1.jpg file2.eps 
$ sam2p  file1.jpg file2.pdf 

You need to dowload libjpeg-progs from synaptic for it to run properly. 

for example:
```
$ du -sk *
232     file.jpg 
```

```
$ convert file.jpg file.eps
$ sam2p file.jpg file2.eps
$ du -sk *
384     file2.eps
9424    file.eps
232     file.jpg 
```
Yes.. in this case the file is about 4% the size of ImageMagick's, and the quality looks about the same to me. 

-sp

### Post by asteinmetz on 2008-06-23
> **euler_fan said:**
> R--It's a statistics program that can do much much more. Best downloaded and installed separately. Also best with a CLI.

I will second the vote for 'R'.  I wish it has a longer name since it's tough to Google with any uniqueness but it's a humble nod to a commercial stats package, 'S', which it largely emulates (hubris would have meant calling it 'T').

It's a simple and powerful interpreted language for statistics and it's worth climbing the learning curve for anyone who uses spreadsheets to work with columnar data.  If you spend a lot of time building formulas and copying them in columns adjacent to your data, it's likely that 'R' is a simpler, faster and more powerful way of doing things.  Just be aware, the spreadsheet metaphor doesn't apply.

There are hundreds of add-in libraries to do just about any specialized task (sudoku generator, anyone?) , the graphics are powerful and the community support forums are active.

---

### Post by Fingers &amp; Thumbs on 2008-07-05

### Post by Brain-free on 2008-07-15
To contribute to this thread, I'd suggest gscan2pdf.

It is most helpful when handling scanned images that you want to be done quickly into a single pdf. Real life-saver if you want to put together scanned notes from a college lesson. Also very simple to handle and with a GUI.

Their site is [http://gscan2pdf.sourceforge.net/]("http://gscan2pdf.sourceforge.net/") and the latest version is now in the repos so you don't have to build it yourself.

P.S. I see that it is mentioned on page 85 but with the extent this topic has taken I believe it wouldn't hurt if I posted this once more. After all, as I said before, it is really-really useful.

P.S.2 Although it uses the SANE image scanner, it is a pretty big app by itself. I think the downloaded files are 5 MB and upon installation it expands up to 25-30 MB of space.

edit: The latest version is 0.9.24 and is in sourceforge. The version in repos is 0.9.21

### Post by imjscn on 2008-07-16
> **asteinmetz said:**
> I will second the vote for 'R'.  I wish it has a longer name since it's tough to Google with any uniqueness but it's a humble nod to a commercial stats package, 'S', which it largely emulates (hubris would have meant calling it 'T').

It's a simple and powerful interpreted language for statistics and it's worth climbing the learning curve for anyone who uses spreadsheets to work with columnar data.  If you spend a lot of time building formulas and copying them in columns adjacent to your data, it's likely that 'R' is a simpler, faster and more powerful way of doing things.  Just be aware, the spreadsheet metaphor doesn't apply.

There are hundreds of add-in libraries to do just about any specialized task (sudoku generator, anyone?) , the graphics are powerful and the community support forums are active.

R is powerful, but it takes great effort to learn the language, if need a job in the banks or institutions, learning R is a better strategy. If not,  Gretl is easier...it gets the job down without learning the language, but, if you prefer to do the odd coding job by yourself, surely you can do with gretl.

---

### Post by imjscn on 2008-07-16
> **urukrama said:**
> Isn't that what bash aliases are for? ;-) With the following in my .bashrc I just need to do "extract package.tar.gz/.zip/.rar" to extract an archive:

```
extract () {
     if [ -f $1 ] ; then
         case $1 in
             *.tar.bz2)   tar xjf $1        ;;
             *.tar.gz)    tar xzf $1     ;;
             *.bz2)       bunzip2 $1       ;;
             *.rar)       rar x $1     ;;
             *.gz)        gunzip $1     ;;
             *.tar)       tar xf $1        ;;
             *.tbz2)      tar xjf $1      ;;
             *.tgz)       tar xzf $1       ;;
             *.zip)       unzip $1     ;;
             *.Z)         uncompress $1  ;;
             *.7z)        7z x $1    ;;
             *)           echo "'$1' cannot be extracted via extract()" ;;
         esac
     else
         echo "'$1' is not a valid file"
     fi
}
```

Please explain---add this code at the end of .bashrc , or...need to edit the whole .bashrc?

---

### Post by zoe-scutterbug on 2008-07-16
> **imjscn said:**
> What's the difference between Prism's google and original google?

I use prisms set up for my gmail account and google reader, I click on my gmail prism and the prism shows my gmail account.

Its the simplest window onto the web, pointing directly to the online application you want and without any kind of tool bar, address bars, menue or any other distraction above the window.

“Prism is an application that lets users split web applications out of their browser and run them directly on their desktop,” the Mozilla Labs blog states.

"Prism is a simple XULRunner based browser that hosts web applications without the normal web browser user interface. Prism is based on a concept called Site Specific Browsers (SSB). An SSB is an application with an embedded browser designed to work exclusively with a single web application."

zoe

### Post by unutbu on 2008-07-20
> **jay019 said:**
> 
Also can anyone recommend a program that can rename photos based on the EXIF data, ie rename to the date pic was taken.

```
sudo apt-get install exif
```

Save this to a file called datestamp.py

```

#!/usr/bin/python
from os import popen,walk
from os.path import join
from shutil import move
from optparse import OptionParser

parser = OptionParser()
parser.add_option("-s", "--simulate", dest="simulate", default=False,
                  action="store_true", help="simulate the renaming")

(opt, args) = parser.parse_args()

for root, dirs, files in walk('.',False):
    for name in files:
        filename=join(root, name)
        cmd="exif --tag=DateTime %s | grep Value | awk '{print $2}' "%filename
        sock=popen(cmd,'r')
        line=sock.readline()
        sock.close()
        date=line[0:10]
        date=date.replace(':','')
        target=join(root, date+'-'+name)
        if opt.simulate:
            print "Will move %s --> %s"%(filename,target)
        else:
            move(filename,target)

```
Make it executable:

```
chmod 755 datestamp.py
```

Use it like this:

```
cd path/to/image/directory
~/datestamp.py -s            # To simulate the renaming
```

You'll see output like this:

```
Will move ./IMG_1775-0.JPG --> ./20080716-IMG_1775-0.JPG
```

If you are happy with the renaming, type
```
~/datestamp.py 
```

### Post by Rhubarb on 2008-07-20
**scanmem**
It's a really good app you can use to change values in memory.
Good for testing values in programs.
It can even let you cheat in games by finding the values used in games (like money, health, etc), then allows you to change those values to whatever value you like.

Just please don't use it to cheat when playing online games, it spoils it for everyone else.

There's a nice simple tutorial (thanks to scragar) here:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=5374557&postcount=5](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=5374557&postcount=5)

---

### Post by Mr.Crowley on 2008-07-31
I'm sure some of these have been mentioned atleast once, but I'm going to tell you about them anyway.

**rTorrent**
Lightweight, console-based bittorrent application. Extremely easy to use, you just need to set up the config file.

**Hellanzb**
Console-based nzb downloader. Downloads, par checks, unrars for you so all you have to do is call up the app in console and move the nzb file to the queue. Supports SSL out of the box. 

**Music On Console**
MOC is a console-based music player. Very lightweight with easy to use key bindings. It's a music server so you can actually close the terminal and the music will keep playing.:guitar:

**Irsii**
Console-based IRC client. Just started using this, but I like it so far.

**GNU Screen**
As you can see I'm a bit of a console junkie. It would be annoying to have all of those consoles open or tabbed all the time. That's where screen comes in. Screen allows you to close terminals but have the applications still run! You can recall all of the console apps in screen by simply typing in 'screen -r'. Of course, that's only the tip of the iceberg. This utility is very powerful and is capable of so much more. It already comes installed on most modern unix-based os's so you don't even need to download it. I just discovered this little gem a few days ago and man I love it.

---

### Post by segalion on 2008-08-01
I am really surprised that searching in this post for mldonkey.

For me the very very best P2P program for linux (and windows) because:

- Has the minimum memory and CPU requirements.
- Has all the p2p network in one program (emule-edonkey, bittorrent, etc.)
- Has the best architecture software client-server. Server is the kernel program, with a CLI and web interface. Client can be a external application to has a better grafical GUI as "Sancho". It lets you to manage it from internet or other PCs natively.

Mldonkey:
[http://mldonkey.sourceforge.net/Main_Page](http://mldonkey.sourceforge.net/Main_Page)

Sancho GUI:
[http://sancho-gui.sourceforge.net/](http://sancho-gui.sourceforge.net/)

Particulary, I only use the web interface included with MLDonkey

> For people that use mathematic and statistical programs maybe WEKA dataminig Opensourde tool 

[http://www.cs.waikato.ac.nz/ml/weka/](http://www.cs.waikato.ac.nz/ml/weka/)


I'm not sure I would compare R to Weka. Although Weka is an incredibly powerful program, it's not a drop-in replacement for people needing a basic statistical tool.

There is another generic stas program that I am watching with significant interest. When I first started getting into using stats packages I heard about the program [PSPP]("http://www.gnu.org/software/pspp/pspp.html"). At the time it appeared to be abandonware but it now looks like the project has taken off again. It is intended to (eventually) be a drop-in replacement for SPSS. SPSS is one of the most common tools in social sciences research and being able to run SPSS files would be a huge benefit to me. True, I can import the data from SPSS into R-CRAN any time I want, but then I have to develop my own analysis. Often the Feds and States (who I work for) have the analysis already developed in SPSS and it would be great to not need SPSS itself to run this syntax.

Note: The version of PSPP in Hardy is incredibly outdated. 

I hope they will eventually support the latest developments in SPSS 15, 16 which integrate SPSS' GUI with python and R. SPSS is increasingly using open-source tool to deliver the features that customers want. I hope this makes it easier for the PSPP developers to keep up with SPSS' development.

---

### Post by jjgomera on 2008-08-01
> **segalion said:**
> I am really surprised that searching in this post for mldonkey.

For me the very very best P2P program for linux (and windows) because:

- Has the minimum memory and CPU requirements.
- Has all the p2p network in one program (emule-edonkey, bittorrent, etc.)
- Has the best architecture software client-server. Server is the kernel program, with a CLI and web interface. Client can be a external application to has a better grafical GUI as "Sancho". It lets you to manage it from internet or other PCs natively.

Mldonkey:
[http://mldonkey.sourceforge.net/Main_Page](http://mldonkey.sourceforge.net/Main_Page)

Sancho GUI:
[http://sancho-gui.sourceforge.net/](http://sancho-gui.sourceforge.net/)

Particulary, I only use the web interface included with MLDonkey

too big problem for me:

-Torrent: i only use torrent for a private tracker, its banned there. rtorrent is very light too.
-ed2k: dont support upload priority :( amuled is light too


qtoctave: really the best alternative to matlab

gmrun: usuful to launch application like Alt+f2 in other wm like openbox, fluxbox
gmusicbrowser: great gtk alternative to amarok
conky: show info in screen
pyrenamer: to mass rename files

### Post by safetycopy on 2008-08-04
Don't think I saw this one mentioned so far (though there's a lot to keep track of!)...

For the compulsive list-writers out there, you should look at [hnb]("http://hnb.sourceforge.net/") [outliner]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outliner"):

> Hnb is an ncurses program to organize many kinds of data in one place, for
example addresses, todo lists, ideas, book reviews or to store snippets of
brainstorming, to make a structured packing list or just to take random notes.
It can export ascii, html and xml, supports todo checkboxes, checkbox trees
with percentages, priorities, preferences, searching and more.

For a terminal-based app, the interface is very elegant and keyboard navigation is productive and intuitive.

Also, +1 for tagtool... I tried cowbell, exfalso, easytag, etc, and tagtool beats them all!

### Post by Buntu Bunny on 2008-08-06
[ArahWeave]("http://www.arahne.si/")  

Well, it's cool if you are a fiber artist, textile designer, or handweaver.  It's a CAD/CAM system for dobby and jacquard weaving. The fully functional demo version is free and includes ArahPaint and ArahDrape, both also for textile design.  

It's written for KDE, but I've had it running with no problems on Ubuntu; first with Feisty and now with Hardy.

Oh, and it's a super easy install.

### Post by Raffles10 on 2008-08-10
[DeVeDe]("http://www.rastersoft.com/programas/devede.html")

When I first tried Linux two years ago one of the biggest problems I found, as a Windows user, was finding a GUI based DVD authoring program that was comparable to the many simple tools that are available to Windows users.

DeVeDe does the job very well, and is so simple to use. The menu's are basic but it takes the headache out of DVD authoring in Linux for those of us that are not proficient at the cli.:wink:

### Post by cardinals_fan on 2008-08-13
A couple of these have been listed, but they deserve another mention.

* [NoteCase]("http://notecase.sourceforge.net/"): an exceedingly handy and compact note-taking app.

* [Figaro's Password Manager]("http://fpm.sourceforge.net/"): a handy little password manager.

* [Wodim]("http://www.cdrkit.org/"): a convenient and compact disk recorder.

* [Parcellite]("http://parcellite.sourceforge.net/"): a nice, DE-agnostic clipboard manager.

* [Osmo]("http://clay.ll.pl/osmo/"): okay, okay.  It's been listed 7 times now.  But Osmo is a superb calendar/personal organizer.

* [Gcolor2]("http://gcolor2.sourceforge.net/"): a nice color choosing app.

* [Clex]("http://www.clex.sk/"): a neat little command line file manager.  Great for when I'm doing console work and don't want to mess around with PCManFM.

* [Sudoku Savant]("http://sourceforge.net/projects/sudoku-savant/"): a very fun little Sudoku game.

* [LostIRC]("http://lostirc.sourceforge.net/"): a nice little IRC client.

By the way, I discovered most of these apps through the tiny but awesome distro SliTaz - they're all in there, along with a bunch of other useful stuff.

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2008-08-17
Apt-ListBugs is script that warns us which (and how many) bugs are reported for a program before we want to install it. It works for Console/Terminal and Synaptic Package Manager.

With Apt-ListBugs we will save time. And the best thing of all is that it is easy to use since it is executed automatically when we want to install a program.

[[IMG]http://img205.imageshack.us/img205/2628/aptlistbuguy5.png[/IMG]](http://imageshack.us)




Apt-ListBugs is in the Debian and Ubuntu repository, you can install it by 

```
sudo apt-get install apt-listbugs
```

### Post by wd5gnr on 2008-08-19
Man it takes a long time to get to the end of this thread. Lots of cool stuff. I notice Chandler mentioned once ([www.chandlerproject.org](www.chandlerproject.org)). From looking at the screen cast it looks excellent. Sort of like outlook with super calendars, Web integration, etc. Wow.

But refuses to run on 64-bit! I am trying the source route with linux32 (will report back). But I did notice that it seems to run fine under Wine if you download the Windows version. Kind of perverse, but it does work at least well enough to hit my IMAP server in both directions.

Ok I did get a 32 bit version to run on 64-bit Hardy. No dice getting a native 64 bit version. Here's the trick.

1) Download the "source" tree and unpack it.
2) Make sure you have svn installed
3) cd chandler
4) linux32 make install
To run the program:
5) linux32 release/RunPython -O Chandler.py

Seems to work.

It's an open source media player based on Mozilla. It's still under development, but it's stable.

Personally I think Songbird is one of the most horrific projects out there on the interwebz. I try it every time a significant change is made, partly because I don't want to criticise something I don't know. But it's bloated, heavy beyond belief, wants to emulate iTunes but fails and only the latest version has a halfway decent interface.  And that's only the complaints I have about the windows version. Using it on Gnome goes against every reason why I love Gnome, sense and simplicity. 

Anyhow, sorry for the small rant, but I really felt that this application isn't really in it's place here amongst the other awesome works of love posted in this thread. 

*offers humble appologies, maybe Maupertus is getting an old Grinch*

### Post by spupy on 2008-08-30
**imagemagick**
A set of command-line utilities to modify images. The twist is: these are scriptable. For example: I have a PNG icon for the mail client. A script using imagemagick puts a little red dot on the corner of the icon, then draws a digit on the dot (number of unread emails) and adds a little drop shadow to the digit.

Some tutorials:
[http://www.imagemagick.org/Usage/](http://www.imagemagick.org/Usage/)
One of the tutorials, to see some examples:
[http://www.imagemagick.org/Usage/annotating/](http://www.imagemagick.org/Usage/annotating/)

### Post by unutbu on 2008-08-31
Hm. I wasn't able to find a libnet-freedb-perl package in the repos either.

Here are two possibilities:
[list]
[*]
```
sudo apt-get install build-essential
sudo perl -MCPAN -e shell
```
You will have to answer a bunch of questions. As far as I can recall, the default options are fine. At the cpan prompt type:
```
install Net::FreeDB
```

(See [http://www.cpan.org/misc/cpan-faq.html#How_install_Perl_modules](http://www.cpan.org/misc/cpan-faq.html#How_install_Perl_modules))

[*][http://www.getdeb.net/search.php?keywords=gcstar](http://www.getdeb.net/search.php?keywords=gcstar)
[/list]

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-08-31
Musikcube isn't a good example. As light as it may be, it's not properly maintained; buggy and has usability quirks. For similar functionality; a low system footprint and a more refined expereince, Foobar 2000 is a better example of Win media players.

The mind also boggles as to how iTunes can be, "non-intuitive", while MusikCube is used as an example of how to do it *right*, when MusikCube is another attempt to emulate iTunes' interface.

And for the record, yes; iTunes is a mess. It's a solid concept and easy enough for the average user but I swear to god, every time I have to download it for my sister, it's gotten another 10mb bigger in download size; carries more crapware and runs slower.

As for Rhythmbox, I'd be more inclined to say it lacks general UI design and hates large libraries.

### Post by phetre on 2008-09-01
Has anyone tried ThinkingRock? ([http://www.thinkingrock.com.au/](http://www.thinkingrock.com.au/)) It's a simple note-taking, task-managing application designed specifically for [GTD]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Getting_Things_Done"), and after a few days of use I'm pretty impressed.

It seems more stable than [Chandler]("http://chandlerproject.org"), although it lacks Chandler's cool e-mail and calendar integration and conceptual generality. Worth a try, at least. As they say on the website: "If you don't have time to download and use this software, then you really need it."

### Post by BionicSeahorse on 2008-09-01
Hands down, one of my favorite apps is Gizmod (aka Gizmo Daemon). It is the best input configurator out there.

I can program pretty much any input device in my computer (keyboard, logitech mouse, Powermate, etc) by editing simple python scripts. The documentation is pretty good too, and the author (Tim Burell) is a feedback junkie.

[LIST]
[*]You can install gizmod by running ```
sudo aptitude install gizmod
```
[*]The official project website is here [http://gizmod.sourceforge.net](http://gizmod.sourceforge.net)
[/LIST]

Enjoy! :guitar:

### Post by Stelaninja on 2008-09-02
Finally! After three evenings of intense reading I've come to the final post.. =) Didn't think it would take so long but since one have to stop every third or fourth post to install a new application to test something it takes some time. But it was well spent time.

I'm pretty new to Linux (besides a better period in my earlier days) and I just love the fact that all these cool apps doesn't take me more than a couple of seconds to download, install and run. Besides that they're free (most of them)!! What the f**k's on the Windozers minds? Everyone on this planet, except grandma and a couple of jerks who say "you wouldn't steal a car!" (without considering if it was possible to duplicate cars by clicking on them) "borrows" (read download/steal) software over the internet just to be up to date. Well, as I would put it with a Jack Black intonation, NOT necessary! There is an option, and it's called Linux!

Hmm.. Back to the subject.. I actually can not think of an app that's not added to the list so I'll just have to add some points (and deduct some as well).

Cheese +1 (un point) - I can use my webcam, yihaa!

Blender +2 (deux point) - Cool, 1 minute installation, lifetime to learn modeling, but cool.

Streamtuner +3 (trois point) - Well, listening to radio isn't so bad after all

Facebook plugin for Pidgin +4 (quatre point) - Smart thing

Amarok +5 (cinq point) - I haven't rediscovered my music, I've just started listening to music

UltraStar +6 (six point) - Great for parties, to bad I don't have a mic

and the twelve points goes to...

gParted +12 (douze point) - Great when you've made an 6 GB partition for Linux and has the rest for Windows (which didn't even work - now deleted for ever).

I've probably missed some great app in the djungle.. But life goes on and at this very moment I happen to know that there is a lot of hard working code soldiers out there, risking their eyes and fingers, to make new cool apps for us. So I'd like everyone to join me in a minute of silence for those who where lost out there (read booted Vista).

...

Btw the minus points goes to motion, because it didn't work(require mmap-something error) and I really wanted to try it. :( And minus as well to driftnet because it didn't work either (I actually didn't change any settings or code) :(

I'm looking forward to seeing more cool apps here and I'd really would like a business strategy game.. (Not like Monopoly)

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2008-09-17
> **L8erG8er said:**
> Gnome-Do is cool, but then I realized that Gnome comes with the good 'ole Deskbar-Applet built right in, and does exactly the same thing, plus with tracker capabilities and launch history.

I set it up to use superkey-space bar to launch, just like Gnome-Do, and it's fantastic.

Gnome Deskbar-Applet - [http://www.gnome.org/projects/deskbar-applet](http://www.gnome.org/projects/deskbar-applet)
Actually GNOME Do is more than just a replacement for Deskbar-Applet. Take a gander at all the [plugins]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/GnomeDo/Plugins") that are available (that list may not be up to date). I haven't gotten the AptUrl plugin to work yet, but I love the Locate applet. I use Google Desktop search rather than Tracker, and the combination of that and the Locate plugin is a fantastic 1-2 punch for finding apps. Plus I got Do to let me launch my Wine programs without having to reach for my rodent to launch apps. Not having to reach for my rodent just to launch an app is a WIN in my book anytime. (See my blog, in my sig, to see how I got the WINE launchers added to Do.) I won't give up my Do for anything, although my buddies are welcome to any Dew that gets my name on it. ;)

> **raul_ said:**
> But the looks man....
/me lvuz dat eye candy. Even with the default theme, it fits in beautifully with Mac4Lin.

> **Whiffle said:**
> I'm going to throw gmusicbrowser out there.  I just found out about it today and I like it very much.  Its very fb2kish.
I checked out gmusicbrowser and I'm not thrilled with the steps I had to take to actually queue up a specific group of songs. I may have to play with layouts some more, but Sonata and Amorak serve my needs better.

### Post by BionicSeahorse on 2008-09-20
shell-fm is a great last.fm streamer... Entirely console-based, and can even be controlled remotely (via socket). Consumes minimal resources, and easy to extend.

The author can be reached at IRC channel [#shell-fm]("irc://irc.freenode.org"), and is very knowledgeable.
Highly recommended!

More info here: [http://nex.scrapping.cc/code/shell-fm/](http://nex.scrapping.cc/code/shell-fm/)

### Post by grappler on 2008-09-28
I've been, quickly through all 125 pages. I've seen several applications I know and love - eg: basket notepads, htop, tilda, etherape

Incidentally I've set up basket notepads to be a kind of project management tool. I make notes on all projects there and links to directories associated with those projects. 

I've learned about some new applications here that I really like - thanks everyone!  

But there are some I haven't seen in the thread - maybe I read too quickly.

Most obvious is

wcd - a smart "change directory"  that saves lots of typing of full paths - use it all the time

Then there are 

kleansweep for removing duplicates, orphans etc

powertop  for laptops - minimizing battery use

dolphin - now the default file manager in kde4 but I run it under gnome. I'd like to find better ways of integrating it with gnome. I find it far preferable to nautilus. 

Lastly, everyone knows about emacs, but if you want to type latex files use it with auctex and reftex. I keep looking at texmaker and kile but always come back to this combination for efficiency.

### Post by KageKeeper on 2008-09-28
I do not think this one is mentioned yet,at least not that I have seen.

I have been using **fish** (*friendly interactive shell*) and I must say I really like it. The subcommand tab completion is very cool. 

You can type sudo apt-get install and then the very first couple of letters of the package and hit tab and fish will show you all possible packages that match so far. 

The syntax highlighting is great too. If you are typing a command and perhaps you misspell an argument, fish will highlight it in red to alert you. When it is spelled correctly, it will be green. 

There are some fundamental differences between fish and bash, however. Namely in the scripting syntax.

You can read all about fish here: [http://www.fishshell.org/]("http://www.fishshell.org/") 

fish is also in the repos.

Check it out.

---

### Post by urukrama on 2008-10-01
For all you mpd + ncmpc enthusiasts: check out [ncmpc++ (ncmpcpp)]("http://unkart.ovh.org/ncmpcpp/"). It is a clone of ncmpc, with some added features (some neat, some unnecessary for my tastes).

From the website:

> Ncmpcpp is almost exact clone of ncmpc but it contains some new features ncmpc doesn't have. It's been also rewritten from scratch in C++. Lack of some function (eg. tag editor, no possibility of going to chosen position in playing song without fastforwarding/rewinding) eventually pushed me to rewrite it as ncmpcpp and include these functions in it.

**New features:**
[LIST]
[*]tag editor
[*]playlists editor
[*]easy to use search screen
[*]media library screen
[*]lyrics screen
[*]possibility of going to any position in currently playing track without rewinding/fastforwarding
[*]multi colored main window (if you want)
[*]songs can be added to playlist more than once
[*]a lot of minor useful functions
[/LIST]

### Post by urukrama on 2008-10-16
If you are looking for a good rss feed reader, have a look at [canto]("http://codezen.org/canto/"). I've been looking for a good command-line newsreader with a simple, clean interface, with customizable keybindings, that shows full posts rather than the first few sentences of new posts. Canto has all of these, and is a lot lighter than something like raggle. The documentation is also excellent.

If you install it on Ubuntu, you may want to install [Debian's pythan-feedparser]("http://packages.debian.org/sid/python-feedparser") package, as the Ubuntu version still has a bug that doesn't go well with Wordpress feeds (instead of the post titles, you'll see the author's name).

---

### Post by JT673 on 2008-10-25
[SIZE="7"][COLOR="Red"][OpenDialect]("http://dialect.openmodeling.net/wiki/OpenDialect")[/COLOR][/SIZE] FOR THE WIN

This unassuming little app is basically a freaking Adobe AIR/Flash app creator rolled into one.  While it's still prone to crashes and has only rudimentary art tools (only rectangles and beizers at most) and some basica application forms (tables, lists), if you want basic Flash/AIR apps like a Jeopardy clone or a web-based presentation, this is your app.

For an example of a product: [http://www.t21northamerica.com/PolicyResistance.html](http://www.t21northamerica.com/PolicyResistance.html)

### Post by crazyfuturamanoob on 2008-10-26
[SIZE="4"]***_[COLOR="Red"]G[/COLOR][COLOR="Lime"]c[/COLOR][COLOR="Cyan"]o[/COLOR][COLOR="DarkOrange"]l[/COLOR][COLOR="Purple"]o[/COLOR][COLOR="Sienna"]r[/COLOR][COLOR="SeaGreen"]2[/COLOR]_***[/SIZE]

That is a color chooser. Only thing it does is to let user pick up a color, then it says what is that color in html, rgb, or some other numbers.
**Very** useful when making a website with html, and setting text colors or something else. Or just programming an application or game which needs some colors in weird formats.

### Post by brunovecchi on 2008-10-26
**txt2tags**

I just discovered this application, it's fantastic. It's for writing your documents and then converting them to any format you want: LaTeX, html, xhtml (with css), Docbook, wikipedia, google code, text only, MagicPoint presentation, etc. It's not an editor, just a script that converts a specially marked-up document to many other document types.

I has a nice and simple sintax, and many tools like sintax highlighting files and plugins for most popular editors (vim, emacs, gedit, kate, etc.).

The philosophy is simple, you write your document (blog, web page, paper, resume, etc.) once and then you use the program to convert it to any format you want, so you keep a centralized master document, and you don't have to worry about learning or recalling more than one markup language.

**_[Web page]("http://txt2tags.sourceforge.net/")_**

I suggest you try it, it's fantastic!

---

### Post by Idefix82 on 2008-10-27
> **IYY said:**
> 
**Beneath a Steel Sky**

This is an old cyberpunk point-and-click adventure game that has been ported (with ScummVM) to Linux. It's completely free, can be downloaded from the repositories, and even comes with speech (that is, every line of dialog in the game is spoken). The graphics are a bit dated, but the storyline is excellent. If you enjoyed games like Monkey Island, King Quest and Quest for Glory, you will love this one.


Just to second that Beneath a Steel Sky is one of the best adventures I have ever played. Most of the modern adventures with fancy graphics are not nearly as good. The riddles are clever and not far fetched at all, the humour is very nice and the voices are brilliant!
As the original poster wrote, this is right up there with Monkey Island I and Day of the Tentacle.

---

### Post by alwayshere on 2008-11-02
sceenlets is handy heres how 

Open your sources.list file to add the repository:
sudo gedit /etc/apt/sources.list


Add this line to the end of the file
Now 
deb [http://ppa.launchpad.net/gilir/ubuntu](http://ppa.launchpad.net/gilir/ubuntu) hardy main universe
-----------------------------------------------------------------

Save and close the text editor
Now
sudo apt-get update
-----------------------------------------------------------------

Install the Screenlets 
Now
sudo apt-get install screenlets
-----------------------------------------------------------------

Now
sudo apt-get install python-feedparser
-----------------------------------------------------------------

Gtkmozembed needs to be installed
Now
sudo apt-get install python-gnome2-extras
-----------------------------------------------------------------

Now 
sudo apt-get update
------------------------------------------------------------------

Rightoo ya sorted now find screenlets icon under applications
to pick a screenlet double click it and if you want it to start on start up 
tick the Auto start on logon. 

I chosse the trash can ,main menu and sysmonitor

go to this address to find more custom screenlets [http://www.gnome-look.org/index.php?xcontentmode=6700](http://www.gnome-look.org/index.php?xcontentmode=6700)

---

### Post by brunovecchi on 2008-11-13
**ImageMagick** - GREAT command line tool for image processing. It can do an unimaginable amount things. And because it's CLI, you can batch process many files with a single command!. Really handy when you just want to resize, rotate, convert between formats, change color or create a layout of images.

### Post by SanskritFritz on 2008-11-13
> **KageKeeper said:**
> I do not think this one is mentioned yet,at least not that I have seen.

I have been using **fish** (*friendly interactive shell*) and I must say I really like it. The subcommand tab completion is very cool. 

You can type sudo apt-get install and then the very first couple of letters of the package and hit tab and fish will show you all possible packages that match so far. 

The syntax highlighting is great too. If you are typing a command and perhaps you misspell an argument, fish will highlight it in red to alert you. When it is spelled correctly, it will be green. 

There are some fundamental differences between fish and bash, however. Namely in the scripting syntax.

You can read all about fish here: [http://www.fishshell.org/](http://www.fishshell.org/) 

fish is also in the repos.

Check it out.I second that, really worth mentioning! I was about to recommend fish, but searched the thread first, and presto :)

---

### Post by andrei_m on 2008-12-08
_wmjump_

[http://sourceforge.net/projects/wmjump/](http://sourceforge.net/projects/wmjump/)

Keyboard navigation of the desktop. Use the keyboard to switch between windows and workspaces. "Mouseless navigation". Shows a menu with the colored list of windows, marked by letters a-z. Pressing the key a-z "teleports" to that window.

[IMG]http://sourceforge.net/dbimage.php?id=195485[/IMG]

### Post by feisty john on 2008-12-08
Easy Editor (ee).

I'm not sure if it's been mentioned in this thread because I didn't read all 130 pages, but I hope someone sees this post and tries it. It is a command-line text editor like Vi or Emacs, but I think it's better. At least, for doing basic stuff, just editing a file that requires root access, like fstab or the GRUB menu file or Apache configuration file. I don't know why it's NEVER mentioned in Linux tutorials for noobs along with Vi, Emacs, joe, et al.

sudo aptitude install ee

To use it, just sudo ee /directory/filename

### Post by unutbu on 2008-12-16
There is also the showfsck package.

```
Description: show the number of reboots before next forced fsck
 This package displays during startup and halt the number of mounts for each
 ext2/3 partition before an fsck will be forced, so that the user will not be
 suprised.
 .
 Very useful for people that often reboot (laptop users for example)

```

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-12-20
> Me either, although the default theme for Firefox 3/Linux has been changed to use native (GTK) widgets.  FF3 on linux *emulates* gtk+ widgets but it's always done that. The only difference between FF2 and FF3 is 3 does a slightly less horrible job or emulating GTK+. 3 also picks up all of about 5 icons from the freedesktop spec and defaults all others to a static archive of fixed-size tango icons.

> Personally I think they should have left Firefox looking like Firefox and left the "native look" theming to the theme developers, but it's no big secret that I am definitely not in love with Firefox 3 and would have preferred being able to run Firefox 2.5 rather than Firefox 3.My only real disappointment with 3 was the promised performance benefits from moving to an SQLite backend for history/bookmarks/etc provided no real performance benefit. Everytime I open my history, 3 goes completely unresponsive for about 10-20 seconds and chews up memory.

If I had a wishlist for FF4, it would simply be for real native widgets; a speedier history storage system and an awesomebar which doesn't seem completely random in it's suggestions.

> [Glipper]("http://glipper.sourceforge.net/") - a great clipboard manager, it's on the repos.

[GCStar]("http://www.gcstar.org/") - want to make a database of all your dvds, books...? This is the right app to do it with.

The terminal is what you get when you press <ctrl><alt><F1>, <ctrl><alt><F2>, etc... A terminal emulator gives you the ability to run commands from inside a GUI.

### Post by TheMyself on 2008-12-25
It took me some time to read all the 135 pages and now I'm not the same person!! Many thanks to the contributers. I have a few apps to mention:

Xfig : A stark  vector graphics editor. Suitable for old machines (as well as new ones).

Kile : A powerful and highly costomizable LaTeX editor. I find Emacs very stark. I you install Kile, install kdvi as well.

Texmacs : An innovative, very useful and very smart WYSIWYG LaTeX-like editor. Something like LyX but much smarter. It even allows you to do computer algebra! It can export documents you make into LateX, pdf and HTML. It's a pity that it is not well-known.


some useful firefox add-ons:

 Adblocker Plus: It blocks the annoying ads on webpages you visit. You can use it to block any annoying website (say, google-analytics).
[https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/1865](https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/1865)


Download Helper: It allows you to download streaming video. Similar to youtube-dl but it works "on the spot".
[https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/3006](https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/3006)

Batch image download: When you visit a webpage with thumbnails of images, it enables you to download the whole gallery automatically and it is smart enough not to download small images. Doesn't work on all websites though (e.g. Flickr).
[https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/3104](https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/3104)

Bugmenot: Allows you to log in instantly  to many websites that require (free) registration. It uses an online database.
[https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/6349](https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/6349)

---

### Post by wootah on 2008-12-27
Second time in this thread :)

**Giver** - Local network sharing for Linux (mostly Ubuntu/GNOME based). Uses auto discovery by use of Avahi network services and has a big promotion on complete auto configuration. Other users of Giver see each other on the local network and it displays their name and picture (System -> Preferences -> About Me). You can drag and drop files and folders for quick transfer across the LAN.

Hey, nifty! A guide -> [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=494198](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=494198) but it is available in the repos. however, it depends on Mono :/

PS: Not a promotion, I just thought it was a cool program :)

### Post by flyguy97 on 2009-01-08
I developed a front-end for the SopCast video streaming service. For those that may not know what SopCast, it is a commercial program that allows people to stream video over the internet. It utilizes peer-to-peer streaming which means the more that use the service, the better the service is for everyone. The typical use for SopCast is streaming footy games, TV shows and the like.

The project home page is:
[http://code.google.com/p/sopcast-player]("http://code.google.com/p/sopcast-player")

Be sure to follow the installation instructions, due to licensing I am unable to provide the streaming client with the player. Installation instructions can be found at the following:
[http://code.google.com/p/sopcast-player/wiki/Installation]("http://code.google.com/p/sopcast-player/wiki/Installation").

Have fun with it, and let me know what needs to be improved. Please use [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1032901]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1032901") to post any questions or comments.

Happy computing,
Jason

### Post by unutbu on 2009-01-14
lftp comes by default on Intrepid. It is also in the official repos. It is like wget, but has some nifty features, including the ability to set a maximum transfer rate:
Type 
```

lftp
lftp :~> set net:limit-total-rate 5120
lftp :~> get URL

```
The second command ("set net...") throttles the max transfer rate to 5120 bytes/second. The third command downloads the url.
There is a way to set the limit-total-rate ~/.lftprc. See the man page.

Sometimes lftp can also download large files quicker than wget by using several connections. For example:
```

time lftp -e 'pget -n 7 -c http://kernel.org/pub/linux/kernel/v2.6/linux-2.6.17.11.tar.bz2'
```
uses 7 connections. 

However, the man page comes with this warning:```

This can speed up transfer, but loads the net and server heavily 
impacting other users. Use only if you really  have  to
transfer the file ASAP.
```

### Post by bgs100 on 2009-02-09
> **RiceMonster said:**
> This is true

Tiny, crappy GUI I made for umplayer. Uses mplayer's controls.
```
#!/bin/bash
zenity --info --title="uMplayer - Controls" --text="Controls:\np and SPACE Keys: Pause and Play\nLeft and Right Keys: Go backward/forward 10 seconds\nDown and Up Keys: Go backward/forward 1 minute\nPgdown and Pgup Keys: Go Back/Forward 10 minutes\n[ and ] Keys: Increase/decrease playback speed by 10%\n{ and } Keys: Halve/double playback speed\no Key: Scroll Through Views: none / seekbar / seekbar + timer\nf Key: Toggle fullscreen\n* and / Keys: Increase and Decrease Volume\n q and ESC Keys: Quit" &
a=$(zenity --file-selection --title="uMplayer - Pick File")  &&
b=$(gnomevfs-info -s "$a" | awk '{FS=":"} /MIME type/ {gsub(/^[ \t]+|[ \t]+$/, "",$2); print $2}')
if [[ $b == video* ]]
then
mplayer "$a"
fi
if [[ $b == audio* ]]
then
gnome-terminal --window-with-profile-internal-id=Default --title=uMplayer --hide-menubar -x mplayer "$a"
fi
if [[ $b != audio* && $b != video* && $b != ""]]
then
zenity --error --title="uMplayer - Error" --text="The selected file is not an audio or video file!  Oops"
fi


```
BTW, pretty thing with awk wasn't mine.

### Post by xX-Felipao-Xx on 2009-02-09
Finally I'll keep with anoter one, much prettier. 
**Yakuake**. Its nice !

_Enable Transparency_
* Your Window Manager (kwin/compiz) must support your hardware and have Desktop Effects enabled. *
For Yakuake skin:
Open Yakuake configuration window and go to Appearance tab.
Enable "Use translucent background if possible" and apply.
For main window (actual console) background:
Right click on console and select "Edit Current Profile...", and go to Appearance tab.
Click on "Edit" button and use the "Background Transparency" slider.

(stolen from a kde-look post ^^)

There you have my screenshot!

palette=#22cc22dd22ee:#aaee44774477:#77ee99ff66dd:#cc77cc9933dd:#66ff9999bb44:#aaaa88ccbbff:#6688bb44bb11:#770077667788:#aa33aa55aa66:#eeee66336633:#9900aa5577dd:#dd00cc5544dd:#77cc9966bb00:#88ff44cc7700:#22dd88228855:#ee22ee22ee22

allow_bold=false

### Post by martynp on 2009-02-11
xX-Felipao-Xx

1. Set your terminator config (/home/yourhome/.config/terminator/config) with the following:

use_theme_colors = False
font = mono 10
scrollback_lines = 750
scrollbar_position = disabled
titlebars = false
borderless = true

background_type = transparent
enable_real_transparency = true
background_darkness = 0.0
background_color = black
foreground_color = grey

copy_on_selection = true

[keybindings]
split_horiz = <Ctrl><Shift>H
split_vert = <Ctrl><Shift>V

2. In Compiz Config Manager go to Window Rules and set the following:

Skip Taskbar, Skip Pager, Below, Non-Resizable, Non-Minimizable, Non-Maximizable and Non-Closable with:

name=terminator

Finally go into Window Rules > Size Rules and set 'name=terminator' to your chosen size and then go to Place Windows > Fixed Window Placement and set 'name=terminator' to your chosen position.

Hope this helps as I am not the best at writing howtos!

Regards

---

### Post by sarang on 2009-02-20
[FONT="Courier New"]wmname[/FONT], a part of the [FONT="Courier New"]dwm-tools[/FONT] package.

Changes the window manager name as seen by programs. Very useful for getting rid of 'gray rectangle' windows created by Java


Edit: Quick tip - running the command [FONT="Courier New"]wmname LG3D[/FONT] solves the Java problem. Also make sure that [FONT="Courier New"]AWT_TOOLKIT=MToolkit[/FONT] is not set.

### Post by sarang on 2009-02-21
> **terdon said:**
> Hey all, anyone know of an app that will let me assign priorities to different programs accessing the internet?

The thing is that when using azureus to download torrents, all other internet access slows to a standstill and sometimes i can hardly browse. I would like to set say firefox's access to the internet to have priority over azureus. I am guessing that playing with nice values will have no effect.

Any ideas?

While there exist torrenting programs that can do this, you can also do this at the kernel level using rules and it can be done for all programs - even those that do not have built-in support for this. A way of doing it at the kernel level is using the powerful utility called [FONT="Courier New"]tc[/FONT] (traffic control) that is a part of the [FONT="Courier New"]iproute[/FONT] package. It has many uses - from prioritizing packets and grouping them by priority to simulating network delay etc, but also a terrible syntax in my opinion and it takes a while to be able to use it to its fullest extent. Read the howtos at [http://tldp.org/HOWTO/Adv-Routing-HOWTO/](http://tldp.org/HOWTO/Adv-Routing-HOWTO/) and [http://devresources.linux-foundation.org/shemminger/netem/example.html](http://devresources.linux-foundation.org/shemminger/netem/example.html) and [http://pupa.da.ru/tc/](http://pupa.da.ru/tc/) for more details.

---

### Post by Deathserver on 2009-02-21
Haven't read the entire thread but plan to. 
here is my contribution to the thread assuming it hasn't been posted yet, i do highly recommend this app i found it using a live cd systemrescue to save my system...long story short Partimage is a program that comes on the live cd and will allow you to backup a partition. So when ever you have a system crash and cant fix you can format using your backed up OS  image i had to do it last night and the image i used to reinstall was almost a year old so i would back up often if you make major system changes or install apps often and thanks to this thread i am.
understand this is only useful with the live cd or usb version but i recommend the live cd  [http://www.sysresccd.org/Main_Page](http://www.sysresccd.org/Main_Page) and information on how to back up to external HDD or usb stick i use a 8gb usb stick  [http://www.psychocats.net/ubuntu/partimage](http://www.psychocats.net/ubuntu/partimage) 
Hope it helps someone let me know what you think, i hope this hasn't been posted:p

im editing: i want to thank BLutack for the Autofsck he mentioned on page 68 post#671 TYTYTYTY!!!

### Post by michaelzap on 2009-02-21
> **terdon said:**
> Hey all, anyone know of an app that will let me assign priorities to different programs accessing the internet?


I do this on my router so that every computer that's connected has to play by the same rules. You just need firmware with QoS (Quality of Service) rules and a router that can run it. I use Tomato on a Linksys WRT54GL (that last L is important; it stands for Linux!), but you can also use OpenWRT on a lot of other router models.

### Post by bob-linux-user on 2009-02-22
This is not really a Ubuntu program as it runs in Wine (and Windows of course) As far as I know the only other programs that do this look a lot prettier but cost large amounts of money.

The program is called "cut+fill" and is on 

[http://sites.google.com/site/cutandfillsite/](http://sites.google.com/site/cutandfillsite/)

The PC computer program Cut+Fill.exe is designed to help surveyors to easily,quickly and objectively carry "Cut and Fill" exercises to at least the same degree of accuracy as would be achieved by other methods, and display the results in a logical manner.
The program will work either for the excavation and fill over an individual building or across a whole site; the principles involved are exactly the same.
The known existing level points are plotted to scale on the screen. The new levels, as provided by the architect or layout designer, are treated in the same way. This enables the computer to ascertain the location of any intermediate points required for the depth and volume calculations.
The "cut” and/or "fill" quantities are then calculated as a series of volumes. For more details of the principle see the instructions included in the zip file on the website.

---

### Post by r m h on 2009-02-22
Tasque - a ToDo list application.  AVailable via Synapric Package Manager.  When set up using a Remember the Milk (RTM) account, you can have one set of ToDo lists accessible from all of your machines.  Additionally, RTM integrates with iGoogle (via a google gadget) and iPhones (app is $25/yr available on AppleStore).  RTM includes private, public and shared lists, and Tasque is a clean local app to manage tasks on those lists.

### Post by HuaiDan on 2009-02-26
Don't know if anyone's mentioned it but Tuxguitar is an excellent musical notation/tab editor/sequencer, taking place of GuitarPro in windows. It reads musical scores which are saved as gp3/4/5 files, and can play them back as MIDI, with multiple tracks. Great for learning and playing along.

### Post by FakeOutdoorsman on 2009-02-27
**txt2regex**: command-line regular expression wizard that outputs to several formats (*grep, procmail, php, sed, etc).

**pngcrush, optipng, advancecomp**: png optimization tools.  optipng works well by itself and pngcrush fixes the dreaded IE png color issues, but I've noticed that pngcrush and advpng (from advancecomp package) may make subtle color changes from the original image.
```
#!/bin/sh
# ./pngoptimze.sh input.png output.png

# Remove color profiles for Innanet Explowuh so it renders correctly.
pngcrush -rem gAMA -rem cHRM -rem iCCP -rem sRGB $1 $2

# Reduce the size of the PNG IDAT data stream.
optipng -o7 $2

# Remove ancillary chunks, concatenate all individual IDAT chunks, then re-encode the combined PNG image file using the 7-Zip deflate method. May not always optimize further than pngcrush and optipng.
advpng -z -4 $2

exit
```

**ffmpeg** (recent svn): a versatile and necessary tool for video nuts.  Convert, encode, decode, transcode.  Even better with the new x264 presets to make high quality H.264 encoding much easier than before.  I dumped all of my old encoding scripts for the new presets.  More info (own horn tootage): [HOWTO: Install and use the latest FFmpeg and x264](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=786095)

**sshfs**: I use this to mount remote directories to my local machine.  Good for using local programs on remote files.

**vless**: an alias to mimic a colored "less" command using vim
```
alias vless='vim -u /usr/share/vim/vim71/macros/less.vim'
```

**medit**: simple, yet effective text editor.  Previously mentioned, but a good one.

---

### Post by Firestem4 on 2009-02-27
Filelight is a program I found in the repositories early on when i started using linux (ie: about 2 months ago lol). However I've fallen in love with it for a number of reasons

[http://www.methylblue.com/filelight/](http://www.methylblue.com/filelight/)

It organizes your hard drive into a pie-chart showing you Root, folders, subfolders, files etc. As a beginner to linux, I find it is a great way to learn how the Linux file-tree structure is organized. 

Also it helped me recover 1.5gigs from a botched .cedega removal DOH!. (EVE Online client)

### Post by martynp on 2009-03-02
> **monkeyKata said:**
> Hello.  I'm also trying to check out flux.  Why shouldn't you add only the xflux command?  Are the default settings unnoticeable/too much, or will it not work correctly? This is how I start f.lux from a script at system startup:

exec /home/martyn/.xflux/./xflux -l 58.2

58.2 is my longitude and I am happy with the default colour setting of 3400

I also have this as a bash alias (flux) and a killall bash alias (deflux) so I can easily manage it from the command line.

Hope this helps as it seems many of you are checking it out after my initial post.

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2009-03-02
> **binbash said:**
> Add it to your startup : 

System > Preferences > Sessions

But dont add ONLY the xflux command . Sample : 

xflux -l **33.55, 44.55**


> **monkeyKata said:**
> Hello.  I'm also trying to check out flux.  Why shouldn't you add only the xflux command?  Are the default settings unnoticeable/too much, or will it not work correctly?  

xflux needs to know where you are since it changes the what they call ["color temperature"]("http://stereopsis.com/flux/faq.html") depending on your location/time zone, and geographic location. 
For that you have to tell the program the latitude and longitude (coordinates).

_If you live in the US, you can **just input your zipcode**_ and it will be automated. 

To do that use the command:

```
xflux -z nnnnn
```

**n** represents your zip code.


**If you don't live in USA**, [check out this website]("http://stereopsis.com/flux/map.html") and type the city and country where you live. It will tell you the exact longitude and altitude,

[http://stereopsis.com/flux/map.html](http://stereopsis.com/flux/map.html)

Once you know your longitude and altitude, use the following command:
```

xflux -l **L, L**
``` 
Replace **L, L** with [your Longitude and latitude]("http://stereopsis.com/flux/map.html").

---

### Post by ricky22 on 2009-03-14
EBView - enables you to use any dictionary in the EPWING format, i.e. most commercial Japanese dictionaries like Kenkyusha, Kojien etc. It's in the repositories.

[http://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/EPWING](http://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/EPWING)

___

Kydpdic - Linux interface for the PWN-Oxford English-Polish Polish-English dictionary. You will need the files angpol.win and polang.win from the Windows installation of the dictionary.

[http://members.elysium.pl/ytm/html/kydpdict.html#english](http://members.elysium.pl/ytm/html/kydpdict.html#english) 

Only .rpm available, but it can be converted to .deb using alien.

___

qgo and Quarry - GUI for GNU Go, for KDE and GNOME respectively. IMHO much nicer than cgoban or Jago.

Patrick

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2009-04-07
I just found a cool application called "[BlueProximity]("http://blueproximity.sourceforge.net/")" by accidentally stumbling to [this thread ]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=70237").

Quote from BlueProximity's Homepage:

"This software helps you add a little more security to your desktop. It does so by detecting one of your bluetooth devices, most likely your mobile phone, and keeping track of its distance. If you move away from your computer and the distance is above a certain level for a given time, it automatically locks your desktop (or starts any other shell command you want)."

***

If you are a KDE user, you might want to try [K-Blueproximity]("http://www.kde-apps.org/content/show.php/K-Blueproximity?content=66969").
I haven't tried it since I don't use KDE.

### Post by alphacrucis2 on 2009-04-26
> **darksideforge said:**
> I love Kompozer's ui, but every time I attempt to use it, it crashes when I try to import a file for a background. I'll try it with beta and see if it's any different than any of the 9.04 alphas.

I looked for Gtkdebconf and didn't see it in the repos...any idea why?

The issue is that Kompozer 0.71 is not compatible with the version of GTK in Intrepid or Jaunty. An updated version is being worked on. Alpha2 version of kompozer 0.8 which corrects this issue is available here (remember it's still a test version:

[http://sourceforge.net/projects/kompozer/]("http://sourceforge.net/projects/kompozer/")

More info here:

[http://www.geckozone.org/forum/viewtopic.php?t=74242&postdays=0&postorder=asc&start=30&sid=4e680ca815b394dbc28480094055c8ac]("http://www.geckozone.org/forum/viewtopic.php?t=74242&postdays=0&postorder=asc&start=30&sid=4e680ca815b394dbc28480094055c8ac")

If you don't speak French then google translate does enough to get an idea of the progress.

### Post by dazzlindonna on 2009-04-30
**[SIZE="4"]My latest fave: geany[/SIZE]**

> Geany is a small and lightweight Integrated Development Environment. It was developed to provide a small and fast IDE, which has only a few dependencies from other packages. Another goal was to be as independent as possible from a special Desktop Environment like KDE or GNOME - Geany only requires the GTK2 runtime libraries.

Some basic features of Geany:

    * Syntax highlighting
    * Code folding
    * Symbol name auto-completion
    * Construct completion/snippets
    * Auto-closing of XML and HTML tags
    * Call tips
    * Many supported filetypes including C, Java, PHP, HTML, Python, Perl, Pascal (full list)
    * Symbol lists
    * Code navigation
    * Build system to compile and execute your code
    * Simple project management
    * Plugin interface (see Plugins) 

Geany is known to run under Linux, FreeBSD, NetBSD, OpenBSD, MacOS X, AIX v5.3, Solaris Express and Windows. More generally, it should run on every platform, which is supported by the GTK libraries. Only the Windows port of Geany is missing some features.

The reason I went in search of a text editor / IDE to replace gedit was because I needed a way to easily save files using the old Windows DOS file format with CR/LF line endings.  While there were other ways to handle it, they were all extra steps, clunky, etc.  

Geany gives me the option to set the line endings in Windows, Unix or Mac format, so it won my heart.  I love everything else about it too, btw, so it was an easy decision for me to stick with it.

---

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-05-03
Geany rocks! :guitar: I don't recall where I found Geany but it was a perfect tool to take over for Notepad+ that I used to use when I was a Windows user. Now Geany is one of the first things I re-install when I do a fresh Ubuntu install. All I really need to recall each time is which PPA I get it from, but it turns out the [Geany devs]("https://launchpad.net/%7Egeany-dev/+archive/ppa") have their own PPA.

### Post by darkzeus85 on 2009-05-25
I use roadnav for real time driving directions just like dashboard gps devices. It dose require a gps antenna to be attached in order to receive position data but it seems to work well if you have a small computer or tablet pc and some kind of mount to use while driving or if you have a co pilot.

### Post by doorknob60 on 2009-05-26
WinFF: [http://winff.org/html/](http://winff.org/html/) or [http://code.google.com/p/winff/](http://code.google.com/p/winff/)

Open soure simple GUI to convert media files using ffmpeg. Has loads of presets to convert the video/song to the right format for things like iPods, Rockboxed MP3 players, PSPs, and just generic formats like WMV or MP3. I use it to convert videos to play on my Sansa e260 with Rockbox, and it works great :)

### Post by The Real Dave on 2009-06-05
Not an app, but a Firefox add-on, but still worth a mention I reckon :D

DownThem All, a great download manger, accelerator, and mass downloader that runs from within Firefox. Get it through tools>add-ons>get add-ons and then just search. Its lightweight, and it unlike many other download "accelerators" it actually works. Eg, ATM I'm downloading an Ophcrack ISO. Through the Firefox downloader, I was getting around 20Kb/s, with DownThem all, average of 80Kb/s, at times going up to around 400-500Kb/s. Other people have reported even better increases. 

[www.downthemall.net](www.downthemall.net) 

Give it a try :D

---

### Post by papangul on 2009-06-05
Webmin - a web-based interface for system administration:
[http://www.webmin.com/index.html](http://www.webmin.com/index.html)

One can also use it like a "Learn linux system administration in a day" guide book(remember the good old "Learn DOS in a day"?). Since it offers a bird's eye view of the system, the options that are associated with a command or configuration file are apparent with a glimpse, you don't have to go through lengthy manuals to know that they exist.

### Post by Xylar Wasterend on 2009-06-08
Mozilla SeaMonkey's Nightlies. Not the official releases such as 1.1.15 no-bin, which I found to be horrible, actually, but rather the whole suite, found at: [http://ftp.mozilla.org/pub/mozilla.org/seamonkey/nightly/latest-trunk/](http://ftp.mozilla.org/pub/mozilla.org/seamonkey/nightly/latest-trunk/) . Been using Mozilla Suite nightlies since 2004, and continued even after the brand name change to SeaMonkey. The .tar.bz2 file as well as the extra archive within are simply extracted to a folder and run straight from it (seamonkey, not seamonkey-bin), no official installation needed. :)

---

### Post by kimberlite on 2009-06-11
> **papangul said:**
> Webmin - a web-based interface for system administration:
[http://www.webmin.com/index.html](http://www.webmin.com/index.html)

One can also use it like a "Learn linux system administration in a day" guide book(remember the good old "Learn DOS in a day"?). Since it offers a bird's eye view of the system, the options that are associated with a command or configuration file are apparent with a glimpse, you don't have to go through lengthy manuals to know that they exist.

Yes, it is really cool. Thanks.

### Post by ukripper on 2009-06-19
Not sure if mentioned earlier:

FREENX - Secure and easy to setup and run over SSH. It allows you to access your desktop from another machine over the Internet or LAN. NX client available for Linux, Windows and Mac as well which is quiet useful just like VNC but lot easier to setup than VNC. [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FreeNX](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/FreeNX)

DROPBOX - [http://www.getdropbox.com/](http://www.getdropbox.com/) gives 2GB free space for Linux,Mac and Windows.

Unetbootin - Easy way to create bootable USB drives on both Windows and Linux [http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net/](http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net/)

Grsync - Graphical user interface for rsync to sync/backup files locally or remotely through SSH. It is in ubuntu repos.

---

### Post by rkirk on 2009-06-20
I'm almost certain someone's mentioned this earlier in the thread, but it's the only app I use that's not already popular: [rTorrent](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RTorrent) is a BitTorrent client that runs from the command line. It might be psychological, but I also swear it's faster than KTorrent or Transmission.
