### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-07-20
> **cb951303 said:**
> nice little dvd ripper: [http://thoggen.net/](http://thoggen.net/)
> **binbash said:**
> Can this one extract subtitles?
I think VLC can rip with subtitles (aka Closed Captions, or as I call them, caps) but I'm not 100% sure. One app I've found that can use caps is the app I use to convert videos for my [iriver E100]("http://www.iriverinc.com/e100/prod/e100common.aspx"): [iriviter]("http://iriverter.thestaticvoid.com/"). It supports not only the iriver players, but also Creative's Zen and several models from iAUDIO. It may not look all that great full screen (vids I rip for the E100 have a resolution of 320x240 for my 2.4" screen, but other players may use larger screen sizes), but I was able to enjoy the pilot for Aaron Sorkin's *[Studio 60 on the Sunset Strip]("http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0485842/")* over the weekend, complete with closed captions.

One issue with their website: They don't have a site that gracefully sits in a windowed (non full screen) browser. I tend to have my browser window measuring about 817x667 (according to an old screenshot I have on my drive) and part of the text on the left hand side is cut off, with the horizontal scroll bar all the way to the left.

> **Ian dewhurst said:**

Integration with last.fm and if you miss the fact you can view the lyrics of songs just add the lyricmaster addon

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-07-26
While this is just my own experience, I actually find all of the Firefox addons useless since I decided that I would use another browser due to Firefox 3 getting bloated enough to make a WinXP user see how slow it's getting, plus my own seeing how many addons are being added to the core app that now devs have to write removeons to get back behaviors that have been in Firefox since 1.5. I realize Fx3's the default browser in Ubuntu because so many people love it, but that love is far from universal. I do keep the Fox around, but only when I need to download vids (The Epiphany Vid Downloader addon doesn't work as wll as the Fox's) or to download multiple files (such as wallpapers) from a single page. Byond that I've actually had to learn how to do without such great addons as Copy Link Name and Gmail Notifier since there aren't tools for Epiphany that do the job, as well if not all.

As for a torrent app, I loved using Azureus when I was able to do more torrent stuff. I've used a few others (can't recall which ones they were) but Azureus was always my go-to torrent client.

### Post by DJ_Peng on 2009-07-26
I know what you mean. I looked at Opera and it's simply a 3rd or 4th tier browser for me. I've got Chromium installed, and I'll use it when I need to either check one of my other Gmail accounts (but not both) or I want to look at a site that doesn't require Flash, etc., that seems to be misbehaving in Epiphany. Although I made both a launcher and an Alias for GNOME Do for Firefox 2 for some of my Fx work just so I could do it without firing up Fx3. Yes, it's slower and some of my old addons aren't compatible anymore, but it doens't require Remove-ons.

I hate to see what I've been missing since I stopped following the addon forums over at mozillaZine when I made the switchover to Epiphany for a good 90% of my web browsing. I stopped reading the threads because they were too aggrevating/derpressing seieng what hoops addon devs were being forced to jump through in the spirit of resolving the "many requests" they got from what must be noobs to Firefox. the Foz was great because it used to be sleek and fast and if you wanted another feature you just had to find an addon, but as of Firefox 3 it looks like the devs were throwing away history in favor of getting Firefox to look and behave like IE, Safari and (maybe) Opera. When FIrefox 2 reached it's end of life date it was like an very good old friend died.

### Post by saintthomas on 2009-07-29

### Post by saintthomas on 2009-08-03
**recordmydesktop**
Really great tool to capture your desktop activitiy. :D It will capute any movements you do in your desktop and will give a .ogv video file output. :P Really great eh...? Just watch a recordmydesktop output in youtube: [http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zQ5iEmGNAlo](http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zQ5iEmGNAlo)

### Post by saintthomas on 2009-08-03
> **Mateo said:**
> good thread, i'm definitely giving some of these applications a shot.

There are two scripts in my signature that I know no one uses but me.  Included in these scripts is:

**theyoke**: a very simple CLI rss aggregator.  it's good to use in conjunction with wget or some other application for grabbing files or posts.

**youtube-dl**: command line program for downloading youtube videos.

----------------

some others I use that aren't super popular:

**Stellarium**:  In my mind, the best astronomy program. I like it much better than celestia because it's like looking at the night's sky from your house.

**hellanzb**: I don't know why it's not more popular.  I guess because torrents are more popular than usenet.  but for grabbing binary files, it's definitely the best program that exists.

**gcolor2**: a very nice program for web development. it will tell you the color of anything on your computer.
clive also is very easy-to-use CLI programme to download youtube videos.

### Post by fcuk112 on 2009-08-03
to prep a new machine at the moment, i first do "sudo tasksel" and install LAMP and SAMBA.

then i run
```

sudo apt-get install ubuntu-restricted-extras irssi build-essential checkgmail guake gnome-do compizconfig-settings-manager fusion-icon vlc lm-sensors sensors-applet avant-window-navigator virtualbox-ose vim-full texlive-latex-base k3b agave miro gisomount glabels nautilus-open-terminal geany monodevelop ruby rubygems ruby1.8-dev libsqlite3-dev gedit-plugins git-core rails

```

most of these have already been mentioned, but to summarize:
ubuntu-restricted-extras - codecs, fonts, etc.
irssi - irc client
build-essential - for compiling stuff
checkgmail - gmail tray notifier
guake - terminal dropdown (i map it to F9)
gnome-do - application launcher
compizconfig-settings-manager - for compiz
fusion-icon - tray icon for compiz
vlc - media player
lm-sensors - to detect CPU/GPU/mobo temps
sensors-applet - display said temps in panel
avant-window-navigator - dock
virtualbox-ose - VM
vim-full - full version of vim
texlive-latex-base - latex
k3b - cd/dvd burner
agave - color management
miro - media rss player
gisomount - to mount iso files
glabels - to print labels
nautilus-open-terminal - open a terminal within nautilus
geany - development
monodevelop - C# / GTK development
ruby 
rubygems 
ruby1.8-dev 
libsqlite3-dev 
gedit-plugins 
git-core 
rails - for ruby/rails development

i also install skype and dropbox from their respective sites (use the link in my signature for dropbox!).

and finally these FF addons rock:
adblock plus - block adverts
delicious - bookmarks management in the cloud
yoono - social network management
fast dial - thumbnails of frequently accessed websites
downloadthemall! - download manager

---

### Post by jis on 2009-08-04
> **matthew.ball said:**
> So is:



Sorry, I had to...

Using that makes your computer faster as videos can be played without Adobe Flash plugin ;)

Perhaps more convenient way to do it is to use YouTube Perfect:
[http://userscripts.org/scripts/show/38074](http://userscripts.org/scripts/show/38074)
Still all video sites should provide alternative to using Flash plugin by default without additional custom scripts.

### Post by miegiel on 2009-08-05
```
sudo apt-get install vnstat
```

CLI network trafic stats, today, yesterday, weekly and monthly up and download totals and estimates.

```
user@laptop:~$ vnstat 

                     rx      /     tx      /    total    /  estimated
 eth0:
     yesterday    857.49 MB  /  100.28 MB  /  957.76 MB
         today    753.54 MB  /   83.24 MB  /  836.78 MB  /    1.33 GB

 wlan0: Not enough data available yet.
```

### Post by stinkeye on 2009-08-06
hot-babe
Just stumbled on this in medibuntu repo.
Description:
Hot-babe is a small graphical utility which display the system activity
in a very special way. When the CPU is idle, it displays a dressed girl,
and when the activity goes up, as the temperature increases, the girl
begins to undress, to finish totally naked when the system activity
reaches 100%. Of course, if you can be shocked by nudity, don't use it!

I'm not saying its useful or cool but I had to have a look.

### Post by slakkie on 2009-08-12
alpine - cli mail client
guessnet/ifplugd/wpa_supplicant - beats any network manager, configure your networks and go.
abcde - CD ripper (cli)
dict - dictionary (see dict.org) cli
fortune - need to say more, it pretty common, gnome had it as wanda the fish which spits out fortune messages cli
crystal-fvwm - a nice WM, never tried it long enough, but it look really cool out of the box
screen/irssi - think new users don't know these two cli
zsh - most people use bash, but zsh is just as nice cli
antiword/xlhtml/a2ps - combine these and you can print Office docs from the cli

Most apps for me are cli orientated, since I do a lot of stuff (almost everything) from a terminal. Konsole (but xterm when using windowmaker).

### Post by battleTop on 2009-08-21
I use various apps with Ubuntu to get what I need done, and some things I enjoy doing. 
Ardour: a great music recorder/editor. I use it with LADSPA plugins which are fairly common.
Screem: A great html editor
Elinks: sometimes I just want to read the text of a page, and not waste time looking at the flashy stuff. Many sites still support a non-graphical browsers. Also, for simplicity's sake, my server has no GUI environment so when checking 127.0.0.1 (loopback interface Elinks it is.
Lighttpd: Its actually a little less of a drain on the system than Apache I think.

The point is with Ubuntu being Debian based, there are so many possibilities.

### Post by Jim_in_Omaha on 2009-08-26
> **jis said:**
> The deb files are available at
[http://kornelix.squarespace.com/packages/](http://kornelix.squarespace.com/packages/)
Additionally you may have to install libfreeimage3,  ufraw and libimage-exiftool-perl (the answer to my own question).

Yes it shows it on the .deb's for the 32 and 64.
I found it here:
[http://www.getdeb.net/]("http://www.getdeb.net/")

-------------------------------------------------
fotoxx-8.2.2-32.deb
fotoxx-8.2.2-64.deb
The following programs are not needed to install fotoxx,
but are used by fotoxx at run time: ufraw, exiftool
-------------------------------------------------

The most amazing thing I'm finding with this is the panorama function. I have been digging through ton's of pics over the years where I took series of images of a wide area. I did not have the software then to make the panorama's out of them and kind of forgot about it. Fotoxx  is doing an amazing job of stitching them together and automatically adjusting brightness and contrast of each image. You can also correct for bowing of the image where straight lines curve in your picture. The Red eye was right on fixing my granddaughters blue eyes that go red all the time.

Yet another great piece of software.

### Post by KIAaze on 2009-09-21
Dependencies: python, python-gtk2, python-pypdf (>= 1.10), python-poppler
So this should do:
```
sudo apt-get install python python-gtk2 python-pypdf python-poppler
```

"python-poppler" is only available since Ubuntu v9.04 jaunty.
So if you have an older version, that might explain why the package failed to install.
cf: [http://packages.ubuntu.com/search?keywords=python-poppler&searchon=names&suite=all&section=all](http://packages.ubuntu.com/search?keywords=python-poppler&searchon=names&suite=all&section=all)

edit:
PDF shuffler is really excellent by the way. Thanks! :)

Two more: Apps to download comics so you can read them offline:
[https://launchpad.net/comicget](https://launchpad.net/comicget) (under development, but already usable for most webcomics)
[http://wnd.katei.fi/comic-get/](http://wnd.katei.fi/comic-get/)

### Post by KIAaze on 2009-09-21
Just download the latest .tar.gz, i.e. python-poppler_0.8.1.orig.tar.gz :)
Just for your information:
> orig.tar.gz is the original (upstream) package. (i.e. the source package. What you need.)
diff.gz is ubuntu specific patches. (might be necessary eventually, but in most cases not)
.dsc is (d)ebian (s)ource (c)ontrol file (contains info like maintainer, version, dependencies ...)


Actually, you might even try downloading the .deb for python-poppler and see if it installs. This could be a lot easier.

Here are some instructions for compiling from source:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/CompilingEasyHowTo](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/CompilingEasyHowTo)

The short version is:
```
tar -xzvf PACKAGE.tar,gz
cd PACKAGE
./configure
make
sudo checkinstall

```

edit:
Forcing myself to find some cool application:
For KDE4 users: [http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/I+HATE+the+Cashew?content=91009](http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/I+HATE+the+Cashew?content=91009)
But I don't hate the cashew. :)

### Post by VCoolio on 2009-09-21
- [kupfer]("http://kaizer.se/wiki/kupfer/") is a light python-based gnome-do like app-launcher. Easy to make your own plugins.
- xcompmgr in the [crunchbangers repo]("https://launchpad.net/~crunchbangers/+archive/ppa") is called xcompmgr-dana and has a -m option to get transparent menus
- in the same crunchbangers repo there is oblogout, which darkens and / or blurs the screen like gksudo and presents options to exit / logout etc. You may need to change the commands if you don't use openbox.

---

### Post by KIAaze on 2009-09-21
> **Robbyx said:**
> I was able to install the following version of python-poppler into Intrepid with no problems:

[https://launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/python-poppler/0.8.1-1/+build/770676/+files/python-poppler_0.8.1-1_i386.deb](https://launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/python-poppler/0.8.1-1/+build/770676/+files/python-poppler_0.8.1-1_i386.deb)

I have just run:

sudo apt-get install python python-gtk2 python-pypdf
(without the poppler in the earlier post, as I had installed direct)

It seemed to install with no problem but I wonder where the startup command is hiding. I can not see it in Applications.

python-poppler is just a library (more precisely "python bindings" for a library), so it probably doesn't have a startup command as it's not something you can start up.
> Poppler Python bindings

This package includes Python bindings for LibPoppler. It is needed to run programs written in Python and using Poppler set. LibPoppler is a PDF rendering library based on xpdf PDF viewer, and used by kpdf and evince PDF viewers. 


It's just a dependency of PDF shuffler. So now go on and install PDF shuffler. :)

---

### Post by fluxbuntu on 2009-09-21
I'll add 2 apps. 

wbar- lightweight stand alone launcher for those of us who use window managers instead of desktops.
osmo- lightweight stand alone PIM includes a calendar, contacts, tasks and notes.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-10-01
[B]Wanted:
[/B]
Tool that allows me to set windows to predefined sizes via keyboard shortcuts.

Idea being that I can make the active window, "compact", "medium", or, "large-ish", instead of just, "maximised", and, "normal".

Anything like this exist (possibly as a compiz plugin) or am I simply engaging in wishful thinking?

Cheers in advance.

---

### Post by unutbu on 2009-10-01
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> [B]Wanted:
[/B]
Tool that allows me to set windows to predefined sizes via keyboard shortcuts.


If you use fvwm, you can add lines like this to your ~/.fvwm2rc file 
```

Key v		A	CM	Maximize 50 100
Key h		A	CM	Maximize 100 50
Key q		A	CM	Maximize 50 50
```

Then, pressing Ctrl-Alt-v will resize the window to occupy 1/2 of your screen (vertically).
Pressing Ctrl-Alt-h will resize the window to occupy 1/2 of your screen (horizontally).
Pressing Ctrl-Alt-q makes it a quarter the size of your screen.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-10-01
Just found an awesome tool to do exactly what I was asking for: wmctrl. It's in the repos.

I just created two shell scripts, with the following:
```
wmctrl -r :ACTIVE: -e 0,-1,-1,476,300
```
```
wmctrl -r :ACTIVE: -e 0,-1,-1,716,458
```

I then used compiz's Commands plugin, to bind these two scripts to Super+1 and Super+2 on the keyboard.

### Post by jdunn on 2009-10-10
Here is an app that has been mentioned only once on this huge thread and I feel it deserves more recognition:  If you have a Texas Instruments graphing calculator, I highly recommend TiLP.  TiLP is software that connects your linux PC to said calculators, allowing you to transfer programs, delete programs, sync your calc clock to your PC, make screendumps of your calc, backup, restore and more.  It is the linux equivalent (but better) of TI-Connect (for MS Windows).

Since TI-Connect will not work on Vista 64, TiLP is the ONLY option for me.  BTW, there are also Windows binaries available but, I never got those to work on Vista because the drivers are unsigned.

The version in the Ubuntu repositories is old.  To get the latest version along with the tilibs, go to [http://www.ticalc.org/]("http://www.ticalc.org/").  Sadly, there may be no more updates of this software after this year.

### Post by winh8r on 2009-10-17
I found that [COLOR="Red"]krename[/COLOR] is a really simple and useful tool for batch renaming files.
Very good for .jpg files as you can rename and edit loads of files in seconds. Well worth a look.

Another really handy application is [COLOR="Red"]ConvertAll[/COLOR] which is great for quickly converting all types of measurement units, like square feet into square metres.

[COLOR="Red"]PasswordGenerator[/COLOR] is good for exactly what it's name says, generating passwords of up to 256 characters using a variety of formats.I have done some testing of it and it does seem to generate truly random passwords with little chance of repetition. good security tool for anyone requiring advanced level passwords (virtually uncrackable unless you have 234,000 years and a 50000ghz processor!!!!!!)

### Post by Yeti can't ski on 2009-11-16
> **Stelaninja said:**
> 
If you don't want to pay, there's always FlightGear. It's actually really good and it's in the repos. If only I could get it to work with PulseAudio :cry:

Try blocking the "autospawn" of Pulseaudio and then make a script for FlightGear with "killall pulseaudio" + "/.<your executable file> + "pulseaudio -D". 

For details: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1306356]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1306356")

---

### Post by KIAaze on 2009-11-16
This might work too and is easier:
```
padsp GAMECOMMAND
```
From the man page:
```
NAME
       padsp - PulseAudio OSS Wrapper

SYNOPSIS
       padsp [options] PROGRAM [ARGUMENTS ...]

       padsp -h

DESCRIPTION
       padsp starts the specified program and redirects its access to OSS compatible audio devices (/dev/dsp and auxiliary devices) to a PulseAudio sound server.

       padsp uses the $LD_PRELOAD environment variable that is interpreted by ld.so(8) and thus does not work for SUID binaries and statically built executables.

       Equivalent to using padsp is starting an application with $LD_PRELOAD set to libpulsedsp.so

```

---

### Post by coldReactive on 2009-11-16

padsp GAMECOMMAND
```
From the man page:
```
NAME
       padsp - PulseAudio OSS Wrapper

SYNOPSIS
       padsp [options] PROGRAM [ARGUMENTS ...]

       padsp -h

DESCRIPTION
       padsp starts the specified program and redirects its access to OSS compatible audio devices (/dev/dsp and auxiliary devices) to a PulseAudio sound server.

       padsp uses the $LD_PRELOAD environment variable that is interpreted by ld.so(8) and thus does not work for SUID binaries and statically built executables.

       Equivalent to using padsp is starting an application with $LD_PRELOAD set to libpulsedsp.so

```

And if OSS doesn't start or gives an error saying there are no devices or you haven't configured OSS because you don't know how?

### Post by spupy on 2009-12-21
The **lndir** command, part of the imake package (at least on ArchLinux).

Give it a folder and it will create a copy of the directory structure, while the files in the copy are links to the originals.

I use it to create a "shadow" of my external disk, so I always know what's on it, even when I don't have it by my laptop.

---

### Post by thetankgirl on 2009-12-23
> **IYY said:**
> Here are the rules:

[LIST=1]
[*]No commonly used applications: This means, no Firefox, Gimp, Inkscape, Open Office, Beryl etc.
[*]Application must be in the repositories (Kubuntu, Xubuntu, Feisty repos are all fine).
[*]Application must be fairly easy to use, so that its usefulness can be quickly apparent.
[/LIST]

Ok, so here are a couple of applications I've recently discovered that are truly amazing:

**Qalculate!**

This is without doubt the most powerful calculator I've ever used. And not only is it powerful, but it's also incredibly easy to use. It can not only be used for simple calculations, but also to factor, simplify, integrate, differentiate, sum, take means, calculate areas, do unit conversions, matrix multiplication... anything you can think of in the realm of math, science, engineering or finance. It even has a periodic table built in!

One thing I can tell you for certain: if I had this nifty little tool during my highschool education, I would not have learned anything, because it can do everything for me!

Even for simple calculations this tool is better than a regular calculator due to its intuitive interface that helps eliminate errors. For example, suppose I type in a slightly ambiguous expression like

12+5^2

as I type, text will appear underneath the input box telling me that the calculator understands the expression as 
 
12+(5^2)

Makes you far more confident, and less error prone.

The program is available in both QT and GTK.

**Agave**

A far less ambitious program than Qalculate, but useful nonetheless. Agave is a colour scheme designer. You can pick a colour, and the program will show you its complement, split complement (a 3 colour scheme), triads, tetrads, an analogous scheme, or a monochromatic scheme. 

So, if you are designing a webpage or a pamphlet, or even doing some digital painting, this program will tell you which colours go well together. 

A tip: some people don't know that in GTK, you can drag and drop almost anything. So, you can grab a colour from The Gimp, drag it into Agave, and then drag and drop the complement of that colour back into The Gimp. Very useful.

**Hydrogen**

I am an amateur musician, but when it comes to electronic music I am twice as uneducated. Anyway, Hydrogen still managed to impress me. This application can be used to create drum and other percussion patterns. It's very easy to use (I figured it out instantly, with 0 experience in the field), and can be fun for those who have never played an instrument or done any work with sound. 

It's a QT app, but looks equally good in both Gnome and KDE since it has its own theme anyway.

**Zim**

Zim is a desktop wiki. I guess it's very similar to Tomboy notes which you may be familiar with, but is designed for a more general purpose. You can create your own wikis (like Wikipedia) on your own computer, without using a browser, and with a very simple WYSIWYG interface. Can be handy to stay organized.

A GTK app.

**Beneath a Steel Sky**

This is an old cyberpunk point-and-click adventure game that has been ported (with ScummVM) to Linux. It's completely free, can be downloaded from the repositories, and even comes with speech (that is, every line of dialog in the game is spoken). The graphics are a bit dated, but the storyline is excellent. If you enjoyed games like Monkey Island, King Quest and Quest for Glory, you will love this one.

Ok... I'm done. Your turn!

Oh Wow, agave looks great, THANKS!:KS:KS

---

### Post by philipg on 2009-12-25
whew! what a list.
 **TopShelf** - quick panel applet to quickly launch favorite files
**pyNeighborhood** - similar to winbloze network neighbourhood
**assoGiate** - An editor of the file types database for GNOME
**ntfs-config** - allow you to easily configure all of your NTFS devices
to allow write support via a friendly gui
**zsync** - a file transfer program to download files from
remote web servers. If a previous version of a file is available
locally, zsync will only download changed parts and hereby
minimise the download volume.
**winetricks** - script to help install MS dependancies in wine

[**UnRaid**]("http://www.lime-technology.com/joomla/") - not really an app. This is a parity protected media server based on cut-down slack distro. Next version is rumoured to support PAR as well giving you multiple simultaneous HD failure recovery :)

BTW **gMusicBrowser** is great for really large collections although it takes a bit of poking around in the prefs to get the look/operation to your taste.

---

### Post by DaveHi on 2009-12-31
Hi

If there is one computing subject that really confuses me it's networking! So, when I recommend an easy remote desktop assistant, you can be sure it really is easy to use;

[COLOR="Blue"]Remote Help Assistant[/COLOR] - Does what it says on the can! A lot of thought has been put into making this program easy, but secure, for the less technical who are likely to be using, at least, one end of it. Suffers from a little lag and there may be a Java bug, leading to high CPU use after closing, but it works!

Launchpad page is: [https://launchpad.net/remote-help-assistant](https://launchpad.net/remote-help-assistant)

But for downloads I have found this mirror better (thanks to Andrew Sayers): 
[http://pileofstuff.org/remote-help-assistant/](http://pileofstuff.org/remote-help-assistant/)

If there's a better solution would be interested to hear of it.

### Post by stevebond001 on 2010-01-14
Hi
Not sure if anyone's mentioned this before but aTunes ([www.atunes.org](www.atunes.org)) is a really good media player.  Info from the website as follows:

[B][I]aTunes is a full-featured audio player and manager, developed in Java programming language, so it can be executed on different platforms: Windows, Linux and Unix-like systems, ...

Currently plays mp3, ogg, wma, wav, flac, mp4 and radio streaming, allowing users to easily edit tags, organize music and rip Audio CDs.[/I][/B]

It also links into last.fm to download lyrics for your songs and (if you have a last.fm account) even lets you set your music as "favourites" so you can listen to your songs online.

Hope others find this useful.

---

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2010-01-14
Most of them that I could think of are all terminal centric apps. I will mention one here. It's called supercat.

This one is an enhanced version of cat. I know it wouldn't mean a lot for most, but if there are people like me who program a lot and use cat to quickly view some source code, this app would come in handy. Wouldn't it be great to have the syntax highlighting maintained upon concatenating? This is where supercat comes in handy.

Here is an example.

Simple concatenation and printing of a C file.

[[img]http://omploader.org/vMzk1bg[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMzk1bg)

Now, the same with supercat (spc)

[[img]http://omploader.org/vMzk1bw[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMzk1bw)

The best part, you can write your own config files for a variety of source files, and spc would do the rest. Pretty handy.

---

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2010-01-15
> **Hells_Dark said:**
> Cool :] Thanks

alias cat="spc" :]

No problems. But remember spc needs config files for different source files. A C file has a specific spc config, and so on. so if you try to issue spc on a txt file you will get an error message.


But as i mentioned, writing a config file is very very easy.

### Post by VCoolio on 2010-01-17
I didn't know about supercat, so I tried and it worked on for example python, but bash was all cyan. But I was pointed to highlight, which is also cool and even has themes (highlight -w for a list). It's actually some sort of converter, so use highlight -W for bash terminal output, -n for line numbering. 

While I'm posting let me also mention uzbl, a keyboard-centred browser; it is in development and was thrown back because of a security issue, but it's very promising.

Also there is [redshift](https://launchpad.net/redshift/+download), a better and more customizable alternative for xflux; from version 1.1 onwards a tray icon is included to disable / toggle.

For cli people: have a look at dpkg and dpkg-query options; eg.:
dpkg-query -S <file>			find what package <file> belongs to
dpkg-query -S <folder>		find what package installed something in <folder>
dpkg-query -L <package>		find what files <package> owns / installed

### Post by ETbluez on 2010-01-27
Gnome Control Center
The control center is already installed by default. You just need to make its shortcut "appear" in the menu. Go to:
System &#8594; Preferences &#8594; Main Menu
  And check:
System &#8594; Control Center
  You can also uncheck "Preferences" and "Administration", as all the items displayed under "Preferences" and "Administration" will be accessible through the control center:
[Screenshot.jpg]("http://ubuntuforums.org/attachment.php?attachmentid=145150&stc=1&d=1264626975")

### Post by markp1989 on 2010-02-11
> **spupy said:**
> The **lndir** command, part of the imake package (at least on ArchLinux).

Give it a folder and it will create a copy of the directory structure, while the files in the copy are links to the originals.

I use it to create a "shadow" of my external disk, so I always know what's on it, even when I don't have it by my laptop.

Thanks for this, gona come in handy when organizing my media files :)

edit: i have 2 drives, 1s full, 1 is going to be eventualy, i used this tool to create a shadow of the full drive in the empty drive, so it looks like my tv series are in the same folder when there in different drives ... :) 

only problem im having is nfs  clients not being able to follow the links (samba is fine with it), but i will probably sort that out in a bit :)

### Post by rimshot4 on 2010-02-11
CMAP and Freemind.

Freemind is a hierarchal mind map writing program. CMAP requires you to connect concepts with verbs and is generally more flexible. A little bit of a learning curve, but both are excellent study tools. I use them all the time.

### Post by lvleph on 2010-04-07
QuickSynergy/ Synergy: Allows you to control the mouse and keyboard of another computer. It even allows for copying and pasting text from one computer to another. This is really nice when I am at home and I want to do various things on my Media-PC while using my laptop to do other things. Much more convenient than picking up the mouse and keyboard. Also, not everything can be done with a remote control.

### Post by KIAaze on 2010-04-23
Not really an app, but a great place to find alternatives:
[http://alternativeto.net/](http://alternativeto.net/)

Password manager: [http://www.keepassx.org/](http://www.keepassx.org/)
```
sudo apt-get install keepassx
```
(There are a lot of others, but this one is cross-platform, generates random passwords, allows custom save location and has a nice GUI. Only drawback: not integrated like kwallet or gnome keyring.)

secure password and data storage manager: [http://gringotts.berlios.de/](http://gringotts.berlios.de/)
```
sudo apt-get install gringotts
```

Digital diary: [http://lifeograph.wikidot.com/](http://lifeograph.wikidot.com/)
```
sudo apt-get install lifeograph
```

P.S.: When posting apps, please post links to their sites or package names from the repos. I hate having to google everytime. :/

### Post by segalion on 2010-04-26
Like tucan (download manager) you have [pyload]("http://pyload.org/").
Seems more stable, and has webserver gui, and cli.

$ wget [http://get.pyload.org/get/](http://get.pyload.org/get/)
unzip pyLoad.zip to a directory of your choice
$ sudo apt-get python-crypto python-pycurl tesseract python-django

and 
$ python module/web/manage.py syncdb
to create initial user for gui interface.

### Post by stevebond001 on 2010-04-27
I have found an app which (IMHO) is better than Tucan Manager (used for downloading Rapidshare, etc files).

Overall, a great piece of software

### Post by BoneKracker on 2010-05-17
urxvt (configured as urxvtd/urxvtc)

Terminal emulators have become major resource hogs.  Most of the new new terminal emulators are major pigs, sucking up megabytes of RAM for each terminal window opened (Gnome's included, as well as most of the popular alternatives).  This sucks if you're like me and often have six or eight terminal windows open, or if you have a lightweight machine.

Urxvt (unicode rxvt) is great because you can run one instance as a daemon (by starting it as 'urxvtd') and then connect to that by opening all future instances as 'urxvtc' (i.e., client).

So you can have numerous terminal windows open but only be using as much about as much memory as a single instance.

I just start up urxvtd automatically (I do it in my ~/.xsession, like so, but you do it however you want):```
# start X terminal emulation daemon
/usr/bin/urxvtd -q -o -f
```

Works great.  By default it's horrifyingly ugly, but don't let that scare you off -- with the right settings in ~/.Xresources, it looks as nice as any terminal emulator I've tried:```
! URxvt settings (class="URxvt"; instance="urxvt")

URxvt*font: xft:DejaVuSansMono:pixelsize=13
URxvt*scrollstyle: plain
URxvt*scrollBar: true
URxvt*scrollBar_right: true
URxvt*iconFile: /usr/share/pixmaps/gnome-color-xterm.png
URxvt*background: #000010
URxvt*foreground: #ffffff
URxvt*cursorColor: magenta
URxvt*color0: #000000
URxvt*color1: #9e1828
URxvt*color2: #aece92
URxvt*color3: #968a38
URxvt*color4: #414171
URxvt*color5: #963c59
URxvt*color6: #418179
URxvt*color7: #bebebe
URxvt*color8: #666666
URxvt*color9: #cf6171
URxvt*color10: #c5f779
URxvt*color11: #fff796
URxvt*color12: #4186be
URxvt*color13: #cf9ebe
URxvt*color14: #71bebe
URxvt*color15: #ffffff
```

### Post by TironN on 2010-05-17
> **unutbu said:**
> I know what you're thinking -- linux has every cool app I will ever need... except, wait a minute... How do I download this 'cool apps' thread as a text file so I can search and/or print it? 

```
#!/usr/bin/perl
# Usage:
snip
}

$cmd="bzip2 thread${thread_num}.txt";
system($cmd);
```Save it to a file called 'dl-ubuntuforum-thread.pl'.
Make it executable:
```

chmod 755 dl-ubuntuforum-thread.pl
```and run it like this:

```
dl-ubuntuforum-thread.pl http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=382137
```Requires perl, wget, lynx, bzip2. Outputs a file called 
'thread382137.txt.bz2'.

Edit: the script can now download any ubuntuforum thread. Just go to the first page of the thread and copy/paste the url into the command above.


Thought I'd make a python version for the hell of it :) I learn't some new things too:

```
import urllib2
import sys
import os
import re

site = sys.argv[1]
page = 1
max_page = 25
site_num = re.findall('(?<=\?t\=)[\d]+', site)[0]
onerun = 0

print "Thread number = %s" % site_num
while page <= max_page:
    
    cmd = 'wget -O thread-%s-%s.html \'http://ubuntuforums.org/printthread.php?t=%s&pp=75&page=%s\'' % (site_num, page, site_num, page)
        
    print "\nNow running: " + cmd
    os.system(cmd)
        
    if onerun == 0:
        file = open('thread-%s-%s.html' % (site_num, page))
        found = re.search('Page\ (\d+)\ of\ (\d+)', file.read())
        page = int(found.group(1))
        max_page = int(found.group(2))
        print max_page
        print page
        onerun = 1
    
        file.close()
    
    cmd = 'lynx -dump thread-%s-%s.html > thread-%s-%s.txt' % (site_num, page, site_num, page)
    print "\nNow running: " + cmd
    os.system(cmd)
        
    page += 1



file_list = []
for i in range(1, (max_page + 1)):
    
    file_list.append('thread-%s-%s.txt ' % (site_num, i))
    
    print file_list

    cmd = 'cat '
for i in file_list:
    cmd = cmd + i + " "

cmd = cmd + '> thread-%s.txt' % site_num

print "Now running: " + cmd
os.system(cmd)

ext = ['html', 'txt']

for p in range(1, (max_page + 1)):
    for e in ext:
        file = 'thread-%s-%d.%s' % (site_num, p, e)
        print file
        os.remove(file)
        
cmd = 'bzip2 thread-%s.txt' % site_num
os.system(cmd)


```

### Post by empty_spaces on 2010-06-01
> **BoneKracker said:**
> Using synergy is a major security hole, unless you use an ssh tunnel.

Can you please elaborate? I'm using it over a WPA2 encrypted network with just my 2 computers, so I'd like to know.

---

### Post by BoneKracker on 2010-06-01
> **empty_spaces said:**
> Can you please elaborate? I'm using it over a WPA2 encrypted network with just my 2 computers, so I'd like to know.

It depends on how risk-averse you are and how well-controlled access to your network is.

Basically, unless the synergy communication itself is encrypted, anyone who has gained access to your network can take over.  They can monitor your keystrokes.  They can assume control of your keyboard and mouse.

Assuming you choose to operate synergy "in the clear" (or "free-balling it", depending on your preferred vernacular):

[LIST]
[*]If you have a wired network that over which you have bullet-proof physical access control, and your network is not connected to the Internet, then you're fine.

[*]If your wired network is connected to the Internet, but you offer no (or few) services, and you are confident in your firewall, then you are accepting some risk (you never know when a machine on your network will be compromised by a rootkit or something and someone could gain access to the network from outside).

[*]If you use a wireless network and you use a good WPA2 setup, then you are accepting some increased risk.  WPA2 is considered secure, when properly configured.  However, WEP and WPA were also considered secure not too long ago (just consider the hubris in that name: "Wired-Equivalent Privacy").  The problem is that using any wireless significantly expands your attack surface by making it possible for anyone (not just people physically connected to your subnet) to sniff your traffic.  Encrypted or not, this is an increased vulnerability.  And as I have said, wireless protocols have a history of vulnerabilities.  I have WPA2(CCMP), but I run it as a discrete subnet that is firewalled from my wired subnet with controlled and monitored communication between the two, because I treat it as being inherently less secure.

[*]Naturally, the risks go up as you start doing certain other things, such as using zeroconf networking (e.g. Avahi), providing externally-facing services (opening ports), participating in P2P file-sharing, using UPnP, having Windows machines on your subnet, mis-configuring your firewall, having guests that use your network, etc.
[/LIST]

So, depending on your level of risk-aversion, and depending on your situation in terms such as those outlined above, you may want to consider encrypting your synergy traffic, even though it's only going over your own LAN.

---

No.

gimpshop's over-window can also close without closing GIMP, which is a no-no.

### Post by Redsandro on 2010-07-31
Mentioned before but underrated:

[SIZE="3"][Geany]("http://www.geany.org/")[/SIZE]

A sweet text-editor with IDE-features using GTK2. It was developed to provide a small and fast IDE, which has only a few dependencies from other packages. It supports many filetypes and has some nice features.

It's my Linux companion as [Notepad++]("http://notepad-plus-plus.org/") is to Windows. Notepad++ has more awesome editing tricks but Geany has an instant symbol browser, just by opening a file. No need to 'start a project' or something annoying as with most IDE's.

I wish wish wish Notepad++ [SIZE="1"](Win32)[/SIZE] and Geany [SIZE="1"](Linux)[/SIZE] would merge somehow.

### Post by juancarlospaco on 2010-08-21
[http://www.web2py.com/](http://www.web2py.com/)

Is an...

[SIZE="1"] a SSL-enabled and streaming-capable web server, a relational database, a web-based integrated development environment and web-based management interface, a Database Abstraction Layer that writes SQL for you in real time, internationalization support, multiple authentication methods, role based access control, an error logging and ticketing system, multiple caching methods for scalability, the jQuery library for AJAX and effects.
Runs on Windows, Mac, Unix/Linux, Google App Engine, Amazon EC2, and almost any web hosting via Python 2.4/2.5/2.6, or Java with Jython.
Runs with Apache, Lighttpd, Cherokee and almost any other web server via CGI, FastCGI, WSGI, mod_proxy, and/or mod_python. It can embed third party WSGI apps and middleware.
Talks to SQLite, PostgreSQL, MySQL, MSSQL, FireBird, Oracle, IBM DB2, Informix, Ingres, and Google App Engine.
Secure It prevents the most common types of vulnerabilities including Cross Site Scripting, Injection Flaws, and Malicious File Execution.
Enforces good Software Engineering practices (Model-View-Controller design, Server-side form validation, postbacks) that make the code more readable, scalable, and maintainable.
Speaks multiple protocols HTML/XML, ATOM, RSS, RTF, JSON, AJAX, XML-RPC, CSV, REST, WIKI, Flash/AMF, and Linked Data (RDF).
Available under the GPL2[/SIZE]

In short, a Web Framework to make Web applications on 9 lines of Python :)
*Even if you dont know how to code, my cat start their own e-Bussiness with this.*

### Post by bunburya on 2010-08-21
After almost 200 pages of posts there is undoubtedly nothing I can say that hasn't been said already. But still, here are a few programs I use that you may/not have heard of...

**Guake**, a drop-down terminal (I saw Yakuake and Tilda mentioned earlier, but not Guake)

**FreeMind**, an application for creating mind maps. I find it's often best to draw these out by hand, but if it gets complicated and you haven't much page space or something, FreeMind is good for keeping track.

**Akregator** and **Liferea**, RSS feed readers. Akregator is a KDE app and probably the best RSS feed I've used. Liferea is DE-independent but integrates well with Gnome.

**Simon Tatham's Portable Puzzle Collection**, a collection of small, simple logic-based games. Good for when you're bored; I particularly like Bridges.

**Fortune**, very useful, I use it for guidance every day :D

**Dosbox**, an MS-DOS emulator.

**Atari800**, an Atari emulator (I downloaded this to play M.U.L.E., fantastic game).

### Post by sarang on 2010-08-25
Tucan Manager - [http://www.tucaneando.com/](http://www.tucaneando.com/)
Downloader for rapidshare, megaupload, depositfiles and many such file sharing sites.

You can queue downloads and the program will download them after waiting for some time between the downloads, as is required by the download site. It uses the Tesseract OCR engine in combination with the Python Imaging Library to solve any captchas whitout user action.

### Post by GrouchyGaijin on 2010-10-17
AutoKey

[http://code.google.com/p/autokey/](http://code.google.com/p/autokey/)

AutoKey is a desktop automation utility for Linux and X11. It allows you to manage collection of scripts, and assign abbreviations and hotkeys to these scripts allowing you to execute them on demand in whatever program you are using.

The core part of AutoKey is sending and receiving keyboard events via the X server. It supports multiple X interfaces and should therefore be compatible with virtually any version of Linux running an X server. Full unicode support is provided and it should in theory work with any keyboard layout.

---

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2010-10-17
[PyRoom]("http://pyroom.org/") is a distraction free **text editor**. Very handy for those who want to concentrate on their writing. Distributed under GNU General Public Licence v3.

It can be found in Ubuntu 10.10's reporitory.

[http://pyroom.org/index.html](http://pyroom.org/index.html)

For KDE users, [FocusWriter]("http://gottcode.org/focuswriter/") is also a distraction-free word processor designed to immerse you as much as possible in your work. The program autosaves your progress, and reloads the last files you had open to make it easy to jump back in during your next writing session, and has many other features that make it such that only one thing matters: your writing.

FocusWriter is not in (K)Ubuntu 10.10 reporitory, but the author provides a link to a PPA.

[http://gottcode.org/focuswriter/](http://gottcode.org/focuswriter/)

### Post by madmax75 on 2010-11-11
**cpulimit** - a CLI application for limiting resource-hogging programs from taking over the whole CPU. A GREAT app for a laptop, I've been able to run some graphically intensive programs with this one without heating the processors too much

Usage example (Terminal):

First find the PID number of the offending process (I use **top** for this). Let's say the PID is 1234 in this case. 

Then exit **top **with Ctrl+C and enter this:

```
sudo cpulimit --pid 1234 --limit 60
```

The *--limit* part tells the offending process what percentage of the processor resources it can take. I usually allow processes to take no more than 60-70 percent.

You can also use the name of the process:

```
sudo cpulimit --exe process-name --limit 40
```

But I've found that using the PID seems to catch the process somewhat better.

---

### Post by ubudog on 2010-11-11
Yeah, cpulimit is a great tool to have.  It works great on old "Windows-only" laptops on which Linux can't control the CPU.

---

### Post by Habitual on 2010-11-15
Yes, I read the WHOLE THREAD in 2 days.

Keeping in line with the "never heard of" theme here. Here are some that haven't been mentioned... 

**TaskCoach** (by far, the best Time/Project Management app EVER)
Description: Your friendly task manager.
 Task Coach is a simple open source todo manager to manage personal tasks
 and todo lists. It grew out of a frustration that well-known task managers,
 such as those provided with Outlook or Lotus Notes, do not provide
 facilities for composite tasks. Often, tasks and other things todo consist
 of several activities. Task Coach is designed to deal with composite tasks.

**hotssh**
Description: graphical interface to secure shell
 HotSSH is an interface to Secure Shell, for GNOME and OpenSSH.
 It intends to be a better experience than simply invoking "ssh"
 from an existing terminal window.

**gnome-shell**
Description: graphical shell for the GNOME desktop
 The GNOME Shell redefines user interactions with the GNOME desktop.
 In particular, it offers new paradigms for launching applications,
 accessing documents, and organizing open windows in GNOME. Later, it
 will introduce a new applets eco-system and offer new solutions for
 other desktop features, such as notifications and contacts
 management. The GNOME Shell is intended to replace functions handled
 by the GNOME Panel and by the window manager in previous versions of
 GNOME. The GNOME Shell has rich visual effects enabled by new
 graphical technologies.

**ccze**
Description: A robust, modular log coloriser
 CCZE is a robust and modular log coloriser, with plugins for apm,
 exim, fetchmail, httpd, postfix, procmail, squid, syslog, ulogd,
 vsftpd, xferlog and more.


and 2 non-apps (Firefox plugins)
**LastPass** ([https://lastpass.com](https://lastpass.com)) 
Description: LastPass is a password manager that makes web browsing easier and more secure
and 
**reminderfox** ([http://reminderfox.org](http://reminderfox.org))
Description:
   1. Display and manage lists of reminders and to-dos.
   2. Make sure you remember all of your important dates via easy-to-use lists, alerts, and alarms.
   3. Be reminded right in your browser without the need for a separate calendar application.

### Post by thinkinhurtz on 2010-12-09
WinFF, I know how it sounds but this is a Linux application now in the Ubuntu repositories. This is a lightweight GUI that quickly converts video files from one format to another. Winff also works specifically well with .flv files downloaded from YouTube and other sites allowing you to convert them to .avi files or whatever format you choose.

### Post by ubudog on 2010-12-09

Winff also works specifically well with .flv files downloaded from YouTube and other sites allowing you to convert them to .avi files or whatever format you choose.

Yeah, but it produces terrible quality videos when being used with gtk-recordmydesktop.

---

### Post by Lucradia on 2010-12-09
> **ubudog said:**
> Yeah, but it produces terrible quality videos when being used with gtk-recordmydesktop.

That's why there's the command line:

**For Audio:**
```
recordmydesktop --full-shots --fps=60.0 --channels=2 --freq=44100 --s_quality=10 --no-wm-check --no-frame --overwrite
```

and to transcode for youtube:
```
ffmpeg -i out.ogv -r 60 -vcodec msmpeg4 -ar 44100 -qscale 5.5 out.avi
```

**No Audio:**
```
recordmydesktop --no-sound --no-frame --overwrite --fps=60 --no-wm-check
```

transcode for youtube:
```
ffmpeg -i out.ogv -r 60 -vcodec mpeg4 -qscale 5.5 out.m4v 
```

You'll see what happens when you try to mpeg4 audio, hence why I chose msmpeg instead.

---

### Post by Mark76 on 2010-12-15
Plan.

Let Synaptic tell you all about it

> [B]X/Motif day planner (dynamically compiled with LessTif2)
[/B]
Plan is a schedule planner based on X/Motif. It displays a month calendar
similar to xcal, but every day box is large enough to show appointments in
small print. By pressing on a day box, the appointments for that day can be
listed and edited. Appointments are entered with the following information
(everything except the time is optional):


And a screenshot

[img]http://farm6.static.flickr.com/5244/5265028574_4a42aef9ca.jpg[/img]

### Post by Sean Moran on 2010-12-16
I hope nobody has mentioned this one before, particularly my forgetful self.  I checked back to September, but not keen to go through 200 pages.  

It's nothing fancy, but great when I'm working on a whole lot of files, particularly things like photos.  I took over 10,000 photos in the past year, and it gets to be a lot of work to edit them all down and save the results as meaningful filenames, and usually any particular series will end up with names like:
 restaurant001.jpg, restaurant002.jpg, ... restaurant789.jpg.

GPRename is a nice little GUI utility for renaming a batch of files.  It can do the numbering, insert, delete, replace and remove characters, as well as change cases.  

Not very exciting, but it comes in handy every now and then, and it's not massive.

---

### Post by Drenriza on 2010-12-16
> **suziequzie said:**

(My boyfriend, when I tried to explain the program to him, said "That means nothing to me you know..." I told him if there's any videos he likes, I can use this to save them for him. He won't remember how).

-------------------
For anyone with an iRiver H10 series MP3 player, I'd have to say **easyh10**.  
This perfectly sets the database for my player so I can navigate using the native firmware, as opposed to using rockbox (which eats battery power big time).

Also **streamtuner** is good. I love listening to streaming comedy stations, and I've got it set with **streamripper** to download the stream to my harddrive to later place on my mp3 player.

An easy way to download youtube videoes, is to just watch the video to the end. and do
```
mv /tmp/Fl* /home/user/Desktop
```
And voila, you have the youtube video you just watched on your desktop.

### Post by kimberlite on 2010-12-21
> **Drenriza said:**
> An easy way to download youtube videoes, is to just watch the video to the end. and do
```
mv /tmp/Fl* /home/user/Desktop
```
And voila, you have the youtube video you just watched on your desktop.

Also you can convert /tmp/Flash* to mp3 to whatever you would like to name your file with ffmpeg.
```
$ffmpeg -i /tmp/Flash... /home/YOURLOGINNAME/_what_ever_you_would_like...mp3

```
Than you can start to normalize volume your mp3 files with mp3gain program.

### Post by MaxIBoy on 2011-02-22
I just discovered rlwrap, which is in the repositories. It provides a command-line editing and history interface similar to that of Bash, and acts as a wrapper around any program that uses stdin and stdout. If you use a program that takes input at the command line but does not provide a command history, use rlwrap to add one yourself. If you are writing a program and don't feel like using the GNU Readline library, you can just recommend that your users use rlwrap. Usage:
```
rlwrap command arguments
```I personally use it for dedicated game servers. 

NOTE: In order to add tab-completion and history saving, you will have to edit your Readline configs.

It can be found in Ubuntu 10.10's reporitory.

[http://pyroom.org/index.html](http://pyroom.org/index.html)

For KDE users, [FocusWriter]("http://gottcode.org/focuswriter/") is also a distraction-free word processor designed to immerse you as much as possible in your work. The program autosaves your progress, and reloads the last files you had open to make it easy to jump back in during your next writing session, and has many other features that make it such that only one thing matters: your writing.

FocusWriter is not in (K)Ubuntu 10.10 reporitory, but the author provides a link to a PPA.

[http://gottcode.org/focuswriter/](http://gottcode.org/focuswriter/)

### Post by Eddison on 2011-03-13
CRYPTKEEPER !!!

Bulletproof program. It creates hidden folder, and you can put anything in there, like a list of passwords, or business files- in fact anything. You make up a password for the folder, and the new folder will not even show up. 
Cryptkeeper will be displayed on the panel bar at the top of the screen. If you want to access a folder, just tick next to the name, then put in password, and the folder is displayed. you can have dozens of hidden folders, and I created a hidden folder on a USB drive, and backed up some personal stuff there.
Another feature is the program will dismount the folder (or virtual drive) in the time you specify. So unless you are using the folder, it will simply disappear in 3 minutes if you have it set to that time.

This program is really simple, and thats what I like most about it- no mess, no fuss, and flexible too.

Its in the repositories



eddison

### Post by ngubk on 2011-04-04
Hi! Everyone. This is the first time i join this forum. Though i've been using ubuntu for 2 years as my main OS. Here's some very nice apps that're very important to me:
1/ Bleachbit(as root): clean up your computer( really great one)
2/ Parcellite or Glipper: clipboard manager (if you copy and paste a lot, then it's a must have)
3/ Crypt keeper: keep (porn :-> ) folders safe with password protection.
4/ Mount manager: edit /etc/fstab using GUI. Perfect tool to automount other partitions at start up.
5/ Sopcast player: watch online football over internet.
6/ World of Goo: great game.Just try it and you'll know
7/ Narcissu: a visual novel game that make me cry every time i play.
8/ Some other useful apps that you may already know: ubuntu tweak, gnome do, getting things gnome, stardict, boot manager, virtualbox( i highly recommend this one), docky, emerald...

### Post by knattlhuber on 2011-04-06
> **Ranko Kohime said:**
> Does anyone know of a simple file search program that picks up hidden files?  I'm trying to clean out my drives and folders of .DS_Store files leftover from using a Mac, but Nautilus' built-in search doesn't return any results.

To clean out these annoying DS_Store files, you could use the command line:

```
find /path/to/music/folder -name ".DS_Store" -exec rm {} \;
```

### Post by Popcynical on 2011-04-18
Just got through the whole thread, whew.  Sorry if you guys didn't want this bumped, but:

**Guayadeque** is a music management program designed for all music enthusiasts. It is Full Featured Linux media player that can easily manage large collections and uses the Gstreamer media framework.

I'm new to Linux and had trouble finding a media player that could handle my large library.  Amarok, Banshee, Rhythmbox, Clementine, they all failed me...  lagged and crashed constantly.  Not Guayadeque!  It's amazing.  Try it.

### Post by debd on 2011-04-19
MULTISYSTEM USB BOOT
'''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''''
A great tool for making a Multiboot USB drive of linux OS s. 
Download the .sh file, make executable & run; this will download and install the app. The UI is pretty intuitive.
[http://liveusb.info/multisystem/install-depot-multisystem.sh.tar.bz2](http://liveusb.info/multisystem/install-depot-multisystem.sh.tar.bz2)

MOC
''''''''''''
I've been recently using MOC (Music On Console) a terminal based music player, a lot. It supports OGG, wave and MP3 formats. Good for machines with low resources.

SNOWNEWS
'''''''''''''''''''''''''''
A simple command-line RSS aggregator.

### Post by Eddison on 2011-05-11
Terminal server client used for accessing a remote server desktop is good, but a bit limited. For instance the size of the screen is too big or too small.
  A much better program is Gnome-RDP. You can set the size of the screen to what you want, and it nests at the top of the screen for easy connecting without going to applications all the time.

It will save passwords but first you have to go to >system>preferences>passwords and encryption keys then right click on passwords:login, and set to 'default'

Now all you do it right click the icon at the top of the screen, and select which desktop you want to remote into. Also has SSH and VNC, but most important for me is RDP too.

An excellent remote desktop client.

### Post by ubuntu27 on 2011-05-27
**[Reverse Package Dependency Look-up]("http://manpages.ubuntu.com/manpages/lucid/man8/apt-rdepends.8.html")**

apt-rdepends allows you to list forward and reverse package dependencies. It can also print a image showing the relationship between dependencies.

Very clever tool.

More info here: 

[http://blog.hartwork.org/?p=108](http://blog.hartwork.org/?p=108) 

[https://chrisjrob.wordpress.com/2011/03/17/listing-a-packages-dependencies-with-apt-rdepends/](https://chrisjrob.wordpress.com/2011/03/17/listing-a-packages-dependencies-with-apt-rdepends/)

### Post by ninjaaron on 2011-09-02
I like a lot of CLI utilities that über useful and probably less known to many Ubuntu users, though they are kinda Linux staples.

Lately, I've been using **curl** a lot, which is similar to wget, but it has different strengths.  By default, it writes the page to the standard output, rather than a file, which can be much more useful for scripting.  I like to use the two in combination of scripting mass-downloads.

One I just discovered today is called **pdfgrep** which allows you to search PDF's just like you would plain text with grep (and grep is one of my all-time favorite programs).  This is extremely useful for me, as I use a couple of dictionaries in PDF format in conjunction with other software, and this will allow me to script lookups instead of searching for them manually every time.  This may sound trivial, but as someone who works with linguistics on a daily basis, it makes a huge difference for me.

I like **cmus** a lot for an ultra-light music player.

I've sorta been getting excited about less and man lately.  I know this is super weird, but when I first started Linux, man pages were like pure gibberish for me.  Now I know how to search them, and I almost always understand what they say.  Man pages are so cool!

---

### Post by ilovelinux33467 on 2011-09-02
I spend quite a bit of time in the command line and for the past 6 or so months I have been using **zsh** as my default shell (The Z Shell). It has some nice features like a built in ftp client, menu completion,  a right prompt (RPROMPT), which I use to display my laptop's current battery status, and spelling correction (for example if I accidently type for example 'vmi' and press enter it will ask "zsh: correct 'vmi' to 'vim' [nyae]?"). I have also added syntax highlighting as well by using [https://github.com/zsh-users/zsh-syntax-highlighting]("https://github.com/zsh-users/zsh-syntax-highlighting"). I have also set it so when I type 'ssh user@' and I press <TAB> <TAB> it will get a list of hosts from ~/.ssh/known_hosts (hosts that I have ssh'd into in the past) and show them up in a menu which I can tab through and pick the one I want to connect to. Zsh can also emulate sh, ksh and csh. Zsh is always one of the first things I install on a clean install.

---

### Post by debd on 2011-09-02
two command line programs I use for manipulations with image and pdf files..

**sam2p**  to convert almost any image file to pdf, postscript, eps, and some other formats. has great compression ability and also canb used to compress images to reduce size.

another one is **pdftk**

as the man page describes:
> If PDF is electronic paper, then pdftk is an electronic staple-remover,
       hole-punch, binder, secret-decoder-ring, and X-Ray-glasses.  Pdftk is a
       simple tool for doing everyday things with PDF documents.  Use it to:

       * Merge PDF Documents
       * Split PDF Pages into a New Document
       * Rotate PDF Documents or Pages
       * Decrypt Input as Necessary (Password Required)
       * Encrypt Output as Desired
       * Fill PDF Forms with X/FDF Data and/or Flatten Forms
       * Generate FDF Data Stencil from PDF Forms
       * Apply a Background Watermark or a Foreground Stamp
       * Report PDF Metrics such as Metadata and Bookmarks
       * Update PDF Metadata
       * Attach Files to PDF Pages or the PDF Document
       * Unpack PDF Attachments
       * Burst a PDF Document into Single Pages
       * Uncompress and Re-Compress Page Streams
       * Repair Corrupted PDF (Where Possible)


just an awesome tool to do stuffs with pdf files. :)

read the man pages.

### Post by Aquix on 2011-09-03
Mkvmerge - also have a gui and is a program to easily merge videos of many formats into a mkv. Very useful formp4 files from youtube where mencoder and ffmeg doesn't always work

cvlc - we all know and love vlc but cvlc is the dummy of vlc and that means that you can use cvlc to play sounds and songs in the terminal:  cvlc ~/folder/somesong.mp3  and anything in the terminal is usefull, especially for cronjobs

kazam - simple simple desktop recorder, screencast recorder, for those that will learn ffmpeg someday they have time.

### Post by ilovelinux33467 on 2011-09-03
Here are some more:
KGet - Great download manager that I use all of the time

### Post by WasMeHere on 2011-09-14
Thank you so much, everybody,
for a thread with so many valuable tips about existing software. Some I already use, some I have been looking for, some I did not think were possible...

I [[COLOR="Red"]_searched this thread_[/COLOR]]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=11250351&nojs=1#goto_threadsearch") but did not find **OpenShot**. Its man page tells you > OpenShot Video Editor is a program designed to create videos on Linux. It can easily combine multiple video clips,  audio  clips,  and  images into a single project, and then export the video into many common video formats.

OpenShot is a non-linear video editor, which means any frame  of video can  be  accessed at any time, and thus the video clips can be layered, mixed, and arranged in very creative ways.  All video clip edits (trimming,  cutting,  etc...) are non-destructive, meaning that the original video clips are never modified.

You can use OpenShot to create photo slide  shows,  edit  home  videos, create  television  commercials and on-line films, or anything else you can dream up.

***I find it powerful yet easy to use*** in order to transform my video clips into a movies other people can enjoy. It can also be used to convert between different video formats (resolutions as well as encodings and containers). For example, I can transform from my camera's highest HD,*1920x1080p 50Hz*, to *1280x720p 30Hz* or lower, that can be played back without a powerful computer.

It's in the repositories, so install it with
```
sudo apt-get install openshot
```

By the way, **VLC 1.1** with GPU enabled and some other tweaks can play HD video quite well with an old computer. I have nvidia video which can be used for decoding.

Have fun

---

### Post by WasMeHere on 2011-09-14
@Oxwivi: Use ```
crontab -e
``` to edit the jobs you want **cron** to perform! Read 'man cron' and 'man crontab' or search for better explanations on the internet!

The following table is listed using
```
crontab -l
```
```
# Minute   Hour   Day of Month       Month          Day of Week        Command    
# (0-59)  (0-23)     (1-31)    (1-12 or Jan-Dec)  (0-6 or Sun-Sat)
    0       *          *               *                 *             date '+Klockan är \%-H'|espeak -v sv -p 65 -s 120 -k10 -a 150 >/dev/null 2>/dev/null
    30      *          *               *                 *             date '+Klockan är \%-H och \%M'|espeak -v sv -p 65 -s 120 -k10 -a 150 >/dev/null 2>/dev/null
    59     18          *               *                 *             espeak -v sv -p 65 -s 120 -k10 -a 150 >/dev/null 2>/dev/null 'nu är det dags för Kvällsfiika'
    45      6          *               *                 *             espeak -v sv -p 65 -s 120 -k10 -a 150 >/dev/null 2>/dev/null 'Väckningsdags'
```
and it uses **date** and **espeak** to tell the time in Swedish every half-hour as well as remind when the children should wake up and start to prepare for bed. In English you may prefer **saydate**, but of course you can make a much nicer and funnier clock with your own real recorded sound and play it with **VLC**.

---

### Post by aaaantoine on 2011-09-14
This thread is massive.  There are bound to be duplicates.

That said, I use Unison to sync files between computers.  As a bonus, it's cross-platform.

Why Unison and not rsync?  Unison lets me cherry-pick files for syncing after they've been compared.  Unison also allows me to see what files are different and say, "I'd prefer to keep *that* version, thanks."  Rsync could probably do this with some helper tools... But Unison was easier for me to set up.

---

### Post by halon78 on 2011-10-10
At first I was leery of purchasing music for my Ubuntu laptop, since I was so deeply entrenched in the iTunes method of buying on my old Windows systems - so I decided to run with the devil on Amazon, but quickly ran into a mess of proprietary software that wasn't going to work (especially when downloaded straight from Amazon's website - they have a version of their downloader client for Ubuntu 9.04, but it doesn't seem to work with Natty).  

I found clamz.  First mentioned two years ago by doorknob60, it's a nifty little command line function ($ clamz Amazonwhateverwhatever.amz) and it just works.  It ain't pretty, it ain't fast, but it makes life a lot simpler than having to deal with all of the nonsense.  It's got a whole lot of tweakability based on the man page, but I'm happy as a clam (har har) to use it as is.

---

### Post by ergo-proxy on 2011-10-10

unoconv -f odt *.rtf 
```magic :)

### Post by lazylew on 2012-05-14
> **go_beep_yourself said:**
> JSpeak, I created it because I was sick of rebooting to Windows to use 2nd Speech Center and ReadAloud. It turned out very nice. There's a youtube video demonstrating it on my blog. Check it out =)

[http://linuxinnovations.blogspot.com/2012/05/jspeak-ultimate-in-linux-text-to-speach.html](http://linuxinnovations.blogspot.com/2012/05/jspeak-ultimate-in-linux-text-to-speach.html)I tried this "Obtaining and running the app"```
$ wget https://github.com/downloads/BullShark/JSpeak/JSpeak.tbz
$ tar -xf JSpeak.jar
$ cd JSpeak
$ java -jar JSpeak.jar
```but it didn't work. Instead did this
```
$ tar -xf JSpeak.tbz
$ cd JSpeak
$ java -jar JSpeak.jar
```and now it works. So your info there has a mistake (.tar instead of .tbz) I think?

### Post by GrouchyGaijin on 2013-05-04
I've started using a couple of command line apps for Google services.

1.gcalcli - the Git Hub version see my signature for a link.  It supports oath so there is no need for your password in a gcalclirc file anymore

2. Tasky - also a script from Git Hub (see my signature for a link) that lets you add, view and edit Google Tasks.
[COLOR=#ff0000]NOTE: [/COLOR][COLOR=#000000]This script requires you to register "your" application at [/COLOR][[COLOR=#000000]https://code.google.com/apis/console/[/COLOR]]("https://code.google.com/apis/console/")[COLOR=#000000]
[/COLOR]
3.YouTube Uploader for the command line - [https://code.google.com/p/youtube-upload/](https://code.google.com/p/youtube-upload/)
[COLOR=#ff0000]NOTE:  [/COLOR][COLOR=#000000]There is a bug in the current version that causes the uploader to crash unless you use a Gmail address, even if the non-Gmail address is a Google ID[/COLOR][COLOR=#ff0000][/COLOR]

### Post by a-you on 2014-07-08
GNOME Wave Cleaner, aka gwc, for de-noising an audio file. It has various spectral subtraction algorithms, rather nicely implemented. Unfortunately not altogether documented but ain't that so common ;-). But it's a REAL NICE app.

oh and fsarchiver for backing up your / partition
